Ijarah — Hire and Lease
intermediate
8 min
Leasing an Undivided Share: Abu Hanifa vs. the Sahibayn
Dispute on permissibility of leasing an undivided share

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on leasing an undivided share and explain the proofs and rebuttals between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
The Hanafi school permits leasing an undivided share despite Abu Hanifa's objection, because benefit exists and delivery can be arranged.

This lesson explores a key intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the lease of jointly owned property. While Imam Abu Hanifa held that an undivided share cannot be leased to a non-partner, his two main disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, disagreed. Their reasoning, along with Abu Hanifa's detailed rebuttals, forms the core of this passage from al-Hidayah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed issue and positions
Determine what exactly is being contested – leasing an undivided share to a non-partner. Note the two views: Abu Hanifa prohibits it; the Sahibayn permit it.
The dispute is about the validity of the contract, not its formation.
2
Examine the Sahibayn's proof
The Sahibayn argue that benefit exists in a musha' share, delivery is possible via takhliyah (vacating) or tahayyu' (mutual division), and they analogize to leasing to a partner or two persons, and to sale.
Their evidence is based on qiyas (reasoning by analogy).
3
Analyze Abu Hanifa's counter-arguments
Abu Hanifa refutes each point: takhliyah does not give control over an indefinite share; tahayyu' is a post-contractual ruling, not a precondition; leasing to a partner eliminates commonness; sale aims at ownership transfer, not benefit.
His main concern is the impossibility of delivery (taslim).
4
Understand the practical consequence
The thamarah al-khilaf: if a person leases his undivided share to a stranger, the contract is void according to Abu Hanifa (no rent due) but valid according to the Sahibayn (rent is due).
This directly affects everyday transactions.
5
Determine the mufta bihi position
The relied-upon position in the Hanafi school is that of the Sahibayn, as endorsed by al-Marghinani in al-Hidayah.
This is the operative ruling for fatwa today.

کوئی یہ کہے کہ اگر اس صورت سے شیوع نہیں ہے تو شریک کی طرف سے ہبہ اور رہن جائز ہونا چاہئے ۔ حالانکہ جائز نہیں ہے۔ جواب یہ ہے کہ عدم شیوع سے مراد یہ ہے کہ ایسا شیوع نہیں ہے جو مانع تسلیم ہو۔ اور یہ بات جائز ہے کہ شیوع ایک اعتبار سے مانع
He said: It is not permissible to lease an undivided share (musha') according to Abu Hanifa except from a partner, and the two said: leasing an undivided share is permissible. Its form is that he leases a portion of his house or his share from a shared house from other than the partner. For them: that the undivided share has benefit, therefore an equivalent rent becomes obligatory, and delivery is possible by vacating (takhliyah) or by mutual division (tahayyu'), so it is as if he leased from his partner or from two men, and it becomes like sale. And for Abu Hanifa: that he leased something he cannot deliver, so it is not permissible. This is because delivery of the undivided share alone is not conceivable, and vacating is considered delivery because it occurs as enabling, which is the action by which capability is attained, and there is no capability in the undivided share, unlike sale because capability is attained therein. As for mutual division, it becomes a right of the contract by means of ownership, and the ruling of the contract follows it, and ability to deliver is a condition of the contract, and a condition of a thing precedes it, and what is delayed is not considered prior. And if he leases from his partner, then everything occurs on his ownership, so there is no commonness, and difference in proportion does not harm him, except that it is not valid in the narration of Hasan from him. And unlike subsequent commonness, because ability to deliver is not a condition for continuation. And unlike when he leases from two men, because delivery occurs wholly then commonness arises from division of ownership between them subsequently. [URDU: Translation and it is not permissible to lease an undivided share according to Imam Abu Hanifa except from a partner, and the two companions said that leasing an undivided share is permissible. And its form is that he gives a portion of his house on lease or gives his share of a shared house to other than the partner on lease. Their proof is that in an undivided share there is benefit, therefore an equivalent rent becomes obligatory, and delivery is possible by vacating or by dividing turns, so it becomes like when he leases to his partner or to two persons, then it becomes like sale. Imam Abu Hanifa's proof is that he gave on lease something he cannot deliver, therefore it will not be permissible. And this is because delivery of an undivided share separately is not conceivable, and vacating is considered delivery because it gives control, and it is the action by which control is obtained. However, in an undivided share there is no control, unlike sale because control is obtained. As for fixing turns, it is a right of the contract by means of ownership, and the ruling of the contract comes after it, while ability to deliver is a condition for the contract, and a condition always precedes the conditioned, and what is delayed cannot be considered prior. As for leasing to his partner, then everything occurs on his ownership, so there is no commonness, and difference in proportion does not harm. Besides, according to Hasan's narration, this is also not valid. And unlike subsequent commonness, because ability to deliver is not a condition for continuation of the lease. And unlike leasing to two persons, because delivery occurs at once, then commonness arises from division of ownership between them subsequently. Commentary on his statement: Leasing an undivided share... etc. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, Imam Zufar, Imam Ahmad, leasing an undivided share, i.e., a shared undivided thing, is not permissible, whether it is divisible like land and goods etc., or indivisible like a slave etc. According to the Sahibayn, Imam Malik, and Imam Shafi'i, leasing an undivided share is absolutely permissible. His statement: And its form... etc. The form of an ijarah contract for an undivided share is that he gives a portion of a house on lease, which is not intended. As for giving his share of a shared house to someone other than the partner on lease, because leasing to a partner is unanimously permissible, and leasing to someone other than the partner is permissible according to the Sahibayn and others. And similarly if he leases half a slave or half an animal to other than the partner. His statement: For them that the undivided share... etc. The Sahibayn's proof is that ijarah is based on benefit, and an undivided share has benefit. This is why if the lessee resides therein, according to Imam Abu Hanifa, an equivalent rent is obligatory. If an undivided share had no benefit, the ijarah would not be valid, like land for a specific crop (ard sanjah) is not valid. Then delivery of the undivided share is also possible by vacating or dividing turns. So it is like when he leases to his partner or to two persons, the ruling of vacating is like its ruling in sale, that vacating is considered delivery. His statement: And for Abu Hanifa... etc. Imam Abu Hanifa's proof is that the purpose of ijarah is to obtain benefit from the substance of the thing, and this is not conceivable in an undivided share because delivery is not possible. This is because delivery is complete with possession, and possession is a sensory matter that only occurs on a specific thing, whereas an undivided share is unspecified. So delivering an undivided share separately is not conceivable. His statement: And vacating is considered... etc. The response to the Sahibayn's statement that delivery is possible by vacating is that vacating is considered delivery not by itself but because it gives control to act and benefit in the substance of the thing. And in an undivided share, vacating and removing obstacles do not give control of benefit, unlike sale because control is obtained there, because the purpose of sale is not benefit but transfer of ownership of the substance. For this reason, the sale of a young donkey is permissible. His statement: And as for mutual division... etc. The response to the Sahibayn's statement about mutual division is that mutual division (fixing turns) is among the rulings of the contract by means of ownership, so the contract is what establishes ownership, and mutual division comes after it. That is, when the contract is concluded, then its ruling is established. Because the ruling of a thing is the effect established after it. The ruling of the contract occurs after the validity of the contract, and for the validity of the contract, possession of ability to deliver is a condition, and a condition always precedes the conditioned. So dividing turns will not benefit because it is delayed due to being a ruling of the contract, and something that occurs later cannot be considered prior. His statement: And if he leases... etc. The response to the Sahibayn's analogy is that the permissibility of leasing to one's partner is because all benefit occurs on his ownership (i.e., some benefit by virtue of ownership and some by virtue of lease). So there is no commonness here. It is possible that someone might say that if there is no commonness in this case, then gift (hiba) and pledge (rahn) from the partner should be permissible, but they are not. The answer is that by absence of commonness we mean that there is no commonness that prevents delivery, and it is possible that commonness is a preventer from one aspect.
Source pages p. 64

Commentary
This passage addresses the permissibility of leasing an undivided share (ijarah al-musha'). It is a classic dispute within the Hanafi school and with other madhhabs. The text presents the matn from al-Hidayah stating the disagreement: Abu Hanifa prohibits leasing an undivided share to a non-partner, while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) permit it. The Sahibayn argue that benefit exists in a musha' share, and delivery can be achieved through takhliyah (vacating) or tahayyu' (mutual division). They analogize it to leasing to a partner or to two persons, and to sale. Abu Hanifa responds that delivery of a musha' share alone is impossible; takhliyah gives control only if the thing is definite, but musha' is indefinite. Tahayyu' is a ruling that follows the contract, so it cannot serve as a pre-condition. Leasing to a partner is distinguished because the entire benefit occurs on his ownership, eliminating commonness. The commentary then clarifies that if the partner himself is the lessee, there is no commonness, so it is permissible. The passage also notes a narration from Hasan ibn Ziyad that even leasing to a partner is not permissible. The discussion concludes by distinguishing subsequent commonness (which does not invalidate) and the case of leasing to two men (where delivery occurs wholly and then commonness follows). The authority weight: this is from Zahir al-Riwayah as presented in al-Hidayah, with the mufta bihi position being that of the Sahibayn (permissibility). The commentary provides a thorough usuli analysis of conditions for contract validity, particularly the condition of ability to deliver (qudrah 'ala al-taslim).

Key Terms
إجارة المشاع (ijārat al-mushāʿ): The lease of an undivided share of a jointly owned property (e.g., a share in a house) to someone other than the co-owner.
تخليہ (takhliyah): The act of vacating or removing obstacles to enable the lessee to take possession and use the property.
تہایؤ (tahayyuʾ): A mutual division or arrangement between co-owners to use the property in turns (e.g., each uses it on alternate days).
شیوع (shuyūʿ): The state of being common or undivided (commonness) between co-owners.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position (mufta bihi), is leasing an undivided share (e.g., half a house) to a non-partner valid?
A) No, because delivery is impossible.
B) Yes, because the undivided share has benefit and delivery can be achieved through vacating or dividing turns.
C) Only if the share is specifically designated.
D) Only if the partner agrees.

Key Takeaway
The mufta bihi Hanafi position permits leasing an undivided share because benefit exists and delivery can be arranged, overcoming Abu Hanifa's objection on impossibility of delivery.

Ijarah — Hire and Lease
advanced
10 min
Leasing an Undivided Share to a Non-Partner: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on validity of leasing musha' to non-partner

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on leasing musha' to a non-partner and state the proofs of Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
Leasing an undivided share to a stranger: invalid for Abu Hanifa, valid for Sahibayn — over whether delivery of benefit is possible.

This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute on the validity of leasing an undivided share (musha') to someone other than the co-owner. Imam Abu Hanifa holds it invalid because delivery (taslim) of an undivided thing is impossible. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold it valid because benefit exists and delivery can be achieved through takhliyah (vacating) or tahliah (time-sharing). The passage details their proofs, rebuttals, and related analogies.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling being debated
Recognize that the core issue is the validity of ijarah on musha' property to a non-partner. State the two positions: Abu Hanifa says invalid, Sahibayn say valid.
The consensus position for leasing to a partner is valid, contrasting with the dispute for non-partners.
2
State the Sahibayn's proof and Abu Hanifa's response
Sahibayn argue that manfa'ah exists in musha', and delivery is possible via takhliyah (analogous to sale) or tahliah. Abu Hanifa responds that takhliyah in sale transfers ownership, not use; tahliah is an effect, not a precondition.
The response centers on the nature of qabd (possession) requiring specificity.
3
Analyze the rebuttal regarding takhliyah and tahliah
Understand why takhliyah does not give control over benefit in musha' (unlike sale), and why tahliah cannot retroactively satisfy the condition of deliverability.
Takhliyah works in sale because purpose is ownership transfer; in ijarah, purpose is use, requiring exclusive control.
4
Evaluate the analogy to leasing to a partner
Leasing to a partner is valid because all benefit accrues to his composite ownership, removing true shuyu'. This is a special case and does not extend to non-partners.
Abu Hanifa distinguishes based on the absence of shuyu' as a hindrance to delivery, not on general permissibility.
5
Understand the concept of subsequent shuyu'
Subsequent shuyu' (e.g., after leasing to two persons and one dies) is valid by consensus because ability to deliver is a condition for inception, not continuation. This distinguishes it from initial shuyu'.
This rebuts an objection that musha' ijarah could remain after death.

قـولـه و بخلاف ما اذا أجر .... الخ - فصار كما اذا اجر من رجلين " کا جواب ہے کہ اگر ایک شخص نے دو شخصوں کو ایک مکان کرایہ پر دیا تو یہ اس لئے جائز ہے کہ تسلیم و سپردگی یکبارگی مجموعہ واقع ہوئی یعنی شیوع نہیں ہے۔ پھر ان دونوں میں ملک اجارہ حاصل ہونے کے شیوع آئندہ طاری ہوا ہے پس یہ شیوع طاری ہوا۔ نہ کہ ابتدائی اور شیوع طاری بالا تفاق جائز ہے۔ تاج الشریعہ کہتے ہیں کہ اگر کوئی یہ اراض کرے کہ شیوع کا طاری ہونا تسلیم نہیں بلکہ یہ شیوع مقارن ہے۔ کیونکہ عقد اجارہ ساعت بساعت منعقد ہوتا ہے فکان الطاری کا لمقارن
جواب یہ ہے کہ جو عقد غیر لازم ہو ۔ اس کی بقاء کے لئے من کل الوجوہ ابتداء کا حکم ہوتا ہے اور جو عقد لازم ہو اس کی بقاء کے لئے من ابتداء ہوتا ہے اور من وجہ نہیں ہوتا اور اجارہ عقد لازم ہے تو اس کی بقاء کے لئے من وجہ ابتداء کا حکم نہ ہوگا۔ پس اس وجہ کے لحاظ سے
Book of Ijarah. Page 64. Ashraf al-Hidayah Urdu commentary of Hidayah Volume 12. One gives his share in a jointly-owned house on ijarah to someone other than the partner, because giving it on ijarah to the partner is permissible by consensus, and giving it to someone other than the partner is permissible according to Sahibayn and others. Similarly if one leases half a slave or half an animal to a non-partner. His saying: 'For them two, [the argument] is that musha' has manfa'ah...' etc. - The proof of Sahibayn is that the basis of ijarah is manfa'ah, and manfa'ah exists in a thing that is musha' (undivided). That is why if the lessee resides in it, then according to Imam Abu Hanifa a fair rent (ujr al-mithl) becomes obligatory. If there were no manfa'ah in a musha' thing, the ijarah would not be valid, just as it is not valid for 'ard sinjah' (barren land). Then it is also possible to deliver the undivided thing by making it available (takhliyah) or by dividing the time (tahliah). So it is like when one leases to one's partner or to two persons. In that case, takhliyah is considered delivery, just as it is considered delivery in sale. His saying: 'And for Abu Hanifa...' etc. - Imam Abu Hanifa's proof is that the purpose of ijarah is to derive benefit from the specific thing (ayn), and this is inconceivable in a musha' thing, because delivery (taslim) is not possible. Complete delivery is by possession (qabd), and qabd is a sensory matter that can only occur on a specific thing, whereas a musha' thing is not specific. Therefore, delivering an undivided thing separately is inconceivable. His saying: 'And takhliyah is considered...' etc. - This is a response to Sahibayn's saying that delivery is possible by takhliyah. The response is that takhliyah is counted as delivery not in itself, but because it enables control over the thing and its use. But in a musha' thing, takhliyah and removal of obstacles do not give control over the benefit, unlike in sale where control is achieved because the purpose of sale is not use but transfer of ownership (tamlik al-raqabah). For this reason, sale of a young donkey is valid. His saying: 'And as for the tahliah...' etc. - A response to Sahibayn's saying about tahliah. Tahliah, i.e., designating turns, is among the effects of the contract that is a cause of ownership, so tahliah comes after the contract. The effect of a contract is only after its validity. For validity, the ability to deliver is a condition, and a condition always precedes the conditional. So tahliah does not help because it is subsequent as an effect. His saying: 'And as for when he leases...' etc. - A response to Sahibayn's analogy. The permissibility of leasing to one's partner is because all benefit accrues to his ownership (some as owner, some as lessee), so here shuyu' (commonness) is not realized. It might be objected: if there is no shuyu' in this case, then hibah and rahn to the partner should be permissible, but they are not. The answer is that the absence of shuyu' means here it is not the kind that prevents delivery. It is possible that shuyu' is a hindrance from one aspect and not from another. Thus shuyu' prevents hibah due to qabd not being complete in a musha' thing, and prevents rahn because the subject matter (manfa'ah) which is the object of rahn is non-existent. Unlike our case where the subject matter is not non-existent, only delivery is difficult. And that is not found in the case of the partner. His saying: 'And the difference in the basis [of enjoyment]...' etc. - Answer to a question. The question: It is conceded that leasing to the partner results in all benefit accruing to his ownership, but he benefits from his share as owner and from his partner's share as lessee. So due to the difference in the basis, shuyu' still exists. The answer: Difference in the basis does not matter, because after the unification of the subject matter, difference in causes is not considered. His saying: 'Rather it is not valid...' etc. - That is, the above answer is according to one narration that leasing a musha' thing to the partner is permissible. But from Imam Abu Hanifa there is a narration by Hasan that this too is not valid. Indeed, Imam al-Quduri mentioned in al-Taqrib that from Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Zufar, there is a narration by Hasan that the ijarah of musha' is invalid whether with the partner or with a non-partner. Thus it is like rahn according to this narration. His saying: 'And as opposed to subsequent shuyu' (al-shuyu' al-tari)...' etc. - This is a response to an objection to the proof mentioned on behalf of Abu Hanifa. Objection: It is well-known that subsequent shuyu' by consensus does not nullify ijarah. For example, if someone leases a house to two persons, then one of the lessees dies, by consensus the ijarah of the living person remains musha'. This is the apparent narration. Yet here too there is no power to deliver. Answer: For the continuation of the ijarah contract, ability to deliver is not a condition, just as takbir al-iftitah is a condition for the beginning but not for the continuation of prayer. His saying: 'And as opposed to when he leases to two men...' etc. - Response to 'it becomes like when he leases to two men.' If a person leases a house to two men, it is valid because delivery was made to both collectively at once, so there is no shuyu'. Then after each acquires the ijarah ownership, shuyu' arises subsequently. So this is subsequent shuyu', and subsequent shuyu' by consensus is permissible. Taj al-Shari'ah says that if someone argues that the arising of shuyu' is not subsequent but simultaneous (muqarin) because the ijarah contract is concluded hour by hour, so the subsequent is like simultaneous. The answer is that for a non-binding (ghayr lazim) contract, its continuation has the ruling of the beginning in every respect. For a binding (lazim) contract, its continuation has the ruling of the beginning in some respects but not in all. Ijarah is a binding contract, so its continuation does not have the ruling of the beginning in every respect. Therefore, from this aspect, it is as mentioned.
Source pages p. 65

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute on the validity of leasing an undivided share (musha') of property to someone other than the co-owner. The issue is whether one can lease his portion of a jointly-owned house or animal to a third party. The passage begins by stating the known position: leasing to the partner is permissible by consensus, but to a non-partner, the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) and others hold it permissible. Imam Abu Hanifa disagrees. The passage then details their proofs and rebuttals.

The Sahibayn argue that ijarah is based on benefit (manfa'ah), and manfa'ah exists in musha' property. They cite that if the lessee resides there, Abu Hanifa himself would require a fair rent, proving manfa'ah exists. Delivery is possible by takhliyah (vacating) or tahliah (time-sharing). Abu Hanifa responds that ijarah aims to derive benefit from the specific thing, but musha' is not specific; complete delivery requires possession (qabd), which can only occur on a specific thing. Takhliyah is considered delivery in sale, but sale's purpose is ownership transfer, not use. Regarding tahliah, it is a subsequent effect of the contract, but ability to deliver is a condition before the contract, so tahliah cannot retroactively satisfy that condition.

The passage also addresses the analogy with leasing to a partner. Leasing to a partner is permissible because all benefit accrues to his composite ownership (part as owner, part as lessee), removing true shuyu' as a hindrance to delivery. This does not extend to hibah or rahn because those have different requirements (complete qabd for hibah; existence of subject matter for rahn). The text then notes a different narration from Abu Hanifa (via Hasan) that even leasing to a partner is invalid, equating it to the ruling of rahn.

Finally, the text discusses the concept of subsequent shuyu' (al-shuyu' al-tari). An objection arises: if someone leases a house to two people, then one dies, the remaining lessee's ijarah becomes musha' by consensus, yet it remains valid despite inability to deliver individually. The response is that ability to deliver is a condition for the inception of the contract but not for its continuation, analogous to takbir al-iftitah in prayer. The text further distinguishes between initial shuyu' (invalid) and subsequent shuyu' (valid) and addresses a subtle argument about simultaneity versus subsequence, concluding that for a binding contract, the ruling of inception does not fully apply to continuation.

Key Terms
مشاع (mushā'): Undivided share in a property; common ownership without physical division.
تخلیہ (takhliyah): Vacating or making a property available without physical handover, considered delivery (taslim) in certain contracts.
تہائی (tahlī'ah): Designating turns or time-sharing for use of an undivided property.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, why is leasing an undivided share (musha') to a non-partner invalid?
A) Because the lessee cannot pay the rent in advance.
B) Because the benefit (manfa'ah) does not exist in musha' property.
C) Because delivery (taslim) requires possession (qabd) which is only possible on a specific thing, not on an undivided share.
D) Because the partner's consent is required by consensus.

Key Takeaway
The validity of leasing an undivided share to a non-partner depends on whether delivery of benefit (taslim) is considered possible; Abu Hanifa says no, Sahibayn say yes.

Ijarah — Hire and Lease
advanced
12 min
The Hanafi Dispute on Ijarah al-Musha'
Intra-Hanafi dispute with proof and counter-proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on ijarah al-musha' and explain the reasoning behind each position using the distinction between existence of the subject matter and delivery.

Core Idea
Leasing an undivided share is valid per Sahibayn because shuyu' does not negate the subject matter, unlike in hibah or rahn.

This lesson examines the internal Hanafi dispute on leasing an undivided share (ijarah al-musha'). The difference between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two disciples (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) rests on whether shuyu' is an obstacle to delivery or to the very existence of the subject matter. Understanding this distinction is crucial for applying the correct ruling in contemporary property leases.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal issue
What exactly is being disputed? The validity of leasing an undivided share (musha') to a partner or to a non-partner.
The passage focuses on leasing to a partner first, then extends the dispute.
2
State the Sahibayn's position and proof
Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that ijarah al-musha' is valid. Their evidence: shuyu' does not make the subject matter (benefit) non-existent; only delivery is hindered, and delivery is not a condition for the contract's continuation.
They distinguish from hibah (where complete possession is impossible) and rahn (where benefit is non-existent).
3
State Abu Hanifa's position and proof
According to a narration from Hasan from Abu Hanifa, and also Imam Zufar, ijarah al-musha' is invalid in all cases. They analogize to rahn: shuyu' prevents valid delivery, and delivery is essential for the contract's validity.
This position is from the nawadir (rare transmissions), not the zahir al-riwayah.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response to objections
The commentator rebuts Abu Hanifa's analogy: in rahn, the benefit is non-existent; in ijarah, it exists. Delivery is a condition for inception, not continuation. Therefore, even if initial delivery is difficult, the contract can be valid.
The response uses the example of emergent shuyu' (shuyu' tari) to show that delivery is not needed for continuation.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
If a person leases half of an undivided house to someone, the lease is invalid (fasid) according to Abu Hanifa but valid (sahih) according to the Sahibayn. This affects whether rent must be paid from the start.
The lesson does not give a definitive tarjih; later fatwa positions vary.

فصار كما اذا اجر من رجلين “ کا جواب ہے کہ اگر ایک شخص نے دو شخصوں کو ایک مکان کرایہ پر دیا تو یہ اس لئے جائز ہے کہ تسلیم و سپردگی یکبارگی مجموعہ واقع ہوئی یعنی شیوع نہیں ہے۔ پھر ان دونوں میں ملک اجارہ حاصل ہونے کے شیوع آئندہ طاری ہوا ہے پس یہ شیوع طاری ہوا۔ نہ کہ ابتدائی اور شیوع طاری بالا تفاق جائز ہے۔ تاج الشریعہ کہتے ہیں کہ اگر کوئی یہ اراض کرے کہ شیوع کا طاری ہونا تسلیم نہیں بلکہ یہ شیوع مقارن ہے۔ کیونکہ عقد اجارہ ساعت بساعت منعقد ہوتا ہے فكان الطاری کا لمقارن جواب یہ ہے کہ جو عقد غیر لازم ہو ۔ اس کی بقاء کے لئے من کل الوجوہ ابتداء کا حکم ہوتا ہے اور جو عقد لازم ہو اس کی بقاء کے لئے من ابتداء ہوتا ہے اور من وجہ نہیں ہوتا اور اجارہ عقد لازم ہے تو اس کی بقاء کے لئے من وجہ ابتداء کا حکم نہ ہوگا۔ پس اس وجہ کے لحاظ سے شیوع مقارن عقد نہ ہوا۔ فلم يكن الطاری كالمقارن فائدہ اولی مسئلہ کا خلاصہ یہ ہوا کہ اگر کسی نے اپنا کل مکان دوسرے شخص کو اجارہ پر دیا تو یہ بالاتفاق جائز ہے۔ نیز اگر یہی مکان دو شخصوں کو یکبارگی اجارہ پر دیا تب بھی جائز ہے اور اگر ایک شخص کو نصف مکان غیر مقسوم اجارہ پر دیا یا دو شخصوں میں سے ایک کو نصف مکان اجارہ پر دیا اس کے بعد نصف مکان دوسرے کو اجارہ پر دیا تو غیر مقسوم ہونے کی وجہ سے جائز نہ ہوگا بر خلاف قول صاحبین کے۔ اور اگر ایک شخص کو کل مکان یا دو شخصوں کو یکبارگی اجارہ پر دیا۔ پھر نصف مکان کا اجارہ فتح کر لیا۔ یا ان دو میں سے کوئی ایک مر گیا تو نصف کا اجارہ باقی رہے گا۔
The passage discusses the ruling on leasing an undivided share (ijarah al-musha'). It states that shuyu' (undividedness) prevents validity in gift (hibah) due to lack of complete possession, and in pledge (rahn) because the subject matter (benefit) is non-existent. In ijarah, shuyu' does not make the subject matter non-existent, only delivery is difficult. Then it addresses leasing to a partner: the partner benefits from his share by ownership and from the other's share by ijarah, but difference in cause does not matter after the contract. However, according to a narration from Hasan from Abu Hanifa, it is not valid even to a partner; Zufar also holds it invalid. Then it discusses emergent shuyu' (shuyu' tari): if two persons hire a house and one dies, the living person's lease remains partially valid by consensus, because delivery is not a condition for continuation of a contract, analogous to takbir not being a condition for continuation of prayer. Then it addresses the objection that when a person leases to two persons, the shuyu' is simultaneous (muqarin), not emergent. Taj al-Shari'ah argues it is emergent because the contract is non-binding? Actually the text says ijarah is binding, so its continuation does not require the same conditions as inception. The first benefit summarizes: leasing whole house to one person is valid by consensus; leasing whole house to two at once is valid; leasing half of an undivided house to one is invalid according to Abu Hanifa, contrary to Sahibayn; if the lease is terminated for half or one lessee dies, the other half remains valid.
Source pages p. 66

Commentary
This passage is an expansion on the Hidayah's text regarding ijarah al-musha' (leasing an undivided share). The author first clarifies why shuyu' is an obstacle in some contracts but not others: in hibah it prevents complete possession; in rahn the benefit is non-existent; in ijarah the benefit exists but delivery is hindered. The key dispute is between Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), who permit leasing an undivided share to a partner, and Abu Hanifa (in Hasan's narration) who prohibits it in all cases, analogizing to rahn. The author presents objections regarding emergent shuyu' (e.g., when two lessees and one dies) and responds that delivery is not a condition for the contract's continuation, using the analogy of takbir in prayer. The first benefit summarizes the ruling: leasing whole property is valid by consensus; leasing half of an undivided property to one person is invalid per Abu Hanifa but valid per Sahibayn; if the property becomes shared later (e.g., one lessee dies), the remaining half lease continues. This passage is from a later commentary, not the original matn, and provides detailed reasoning for the Hanafi position.

Key Terms
شیوع (shuyū‘): Undividedness or common ownership; the state of a property being owned in shares without physical partition.
مشاع (mushā‘): An undivided share in a jointly owned property.
اجارہ مشاع (ijārah al-mushā‘): Leasing an undivided share of a property.
معقود علیہ (ma‘qūd ‘alayh): The subject matter of the contract; in ijarah, it is the benefit (manfa'ah).
قبضہ تامہ (qabḍah tāmmah): Complete possession; taking full control of the subject matter.
تسلیم (taslīm): Delivery of the subject matter to the lessee.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the position of Sahibayn regarding leasing an undivided share to a partner?
A) It is invalid (fasid).
B) It is valid (sahih).
C) It is valid only if the wage is payable in advance.
D) It is invalid only if the lessor owns less than half.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school has a well-known internal dispute on ijarah al-musha', with Sahibayn permitting it and Abu Hanifa (in one narration) prohibiting it, based on whether delivery is a condition for validity or only for inception.

Ijarah — Hire and Lease
intermediate
10 min
Emergent Shuyu' and the Continuation of Ijarah
Clarifying emergent shuyu' with analogy to salah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define emergent shuyu' (shuyu' tari) and explain why it does not invalidate an ijarah contract, using the analogy of takbir in salah.

Core Idea
Emergent shuyu' does not break an ijarah contract because delivery is required only at the start, not for the contract's continuation.

This lesson addresses a specific question: what happens if a lease becomes undivided after the contract is made? For example, two persons hire a house, and then one dies. The passage explains that such emergent shuyu' is harmless, drawing an analogy to the takbirat al-ihram in prayer—required at the beginning but not for the prayer's continuation. This principle clarifies the scope of delivery as a contractual condition.

Guided Path
1
Define emergent shuyu' (shuyu' tari)
Emergent shuyu' occurs when a valid contract, initially free of shuyu', later becomes affected by undividedness due to an external event (e.g., death of one of two joint lessees).
This is contrasted with initial shuyu' (shuyu' ibtida'i) that exists at the time of the contract.
2
State the consensus on emergent shuyu'
By consensus (bil-ittifaq), emergent shuyu' does not invalidate the ijarah. The remaining contract for the surviving lessee continues to be valid despite the undivided share.
The passage emphasizes 'بالاجماع' (by consensus).
3
Understand the objection and response
An objection is raised: when two persons hire a property, the lease is initially valid (no shuyu'), but the shuyu' is simultaneous (muqarin), not emergent. Taj al-Shari'ah argues it is emergent because the contract is binding (lazim); for non-binding contracts, continuation is treated like inception. For binding contracts, different rules apply.
The passage clarifies that ijarah is a binding contract (عقد لازم).
4
Apply the analogy to prayer
The takbirat al-ihram is a condition for starting prayer but not for its continuation. Similarly, delivery is a condition for starting ijarah, not for its ongoing validity. Therefore, after the lease is validly formed, a subsequent delivery failure (like shuyu') does not break it.
This is a key usul principle: conditions for inception vs. continuation.
5
Summarize the first benefit (fa'idah ula)
The passage concludes with a summary: leasing the whole property to one person is valid by consensus; leasing to two persons at once is valid; leasing half of an undivided property to one person is invalid per Abu Hanifa but valid per Sahibayn; if half becomes undivided later (e.g., one lessee dies), the remaining lease continues.
This summary helps differentiate the various scenarios.

The author presents objections regarding emergent shuyu' (e.g., when two lessees and one dies) and responds that delivery is not a condition for the contract's continuation, using the analogy of takbir in prayer. This passage is from a later commentary, not the original matn, and provides detailed reasoning for the Hanafi position.

Key Terms
شیوع طاری (shuyū‘ ṭāri’): Undividedness that arises after the contract is made, e.g., when one of two joint lessees dies.
تسلیم (taslīm): Delivery of the subject matter to the lessee.
قبضہ تامہ (qabḍah tāmmah): Complete possession; taking full control of the subject matter.
عقد لازم (‘aqd lāzim): A binding contract that cannot be unilaterally rescinded.
شیوع مقارن (shuyū‘ muqārin): Undividedness that is simultaneous with the contract, i.e., present at the time of formation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because the contract is non-binding and flexible.
B) Because delivery is a condition for validity only at the inception, not for continuation.
C) Because the lessee can always deliver the property later.
D) Because shuyu' does not affect the subject matter directly.

Key Takeaway
Emergent shuyu' does not invalidate an ijarah contract because delivery is a condition for inception, not continuation, analogous to takbir in salah.

Fatwa Hierarchy for Ijarah al-Musha': Abu Hanifa vs. Sahibayn
Clarifying conflicting fatwa positions on ijarah al-musha'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the mufta bihi (operative fatwa) position on ijarah al-musha' from the zahir al-riwayah position, and explain the role of balwa 'amm in shifting the fatwa within the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
For ijarah al-musha', later Hanafi fatwa follows Abu Hanifa, not Sahibayn, due to widespread need.

In this lesson, you'll encounter a critical refinement in Hanafi fatwa practice: although the transmitted (riwayah) position on ijarah al-musha' is that of the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani), later authorities shifted the operative fatwa to Imam Abu Hanifa's view. This shift was driven by the principle of balwa 'amm (widespread need) and reflects the dynamism of the Hanafi fatwa tradition—where practical necessity can override the default narrational hierarchy.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Core Issue
The issue is ijarah al-musha': leasing an undivided share of co-owned property. The Hanafi school has a known difference between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on its validity. Determine which ruling is in the zahir al-riwayah (the standard transmitted corpus).
Zahir al-riwayah: the six core works of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani.
2
Compare the Two Fatwa Transmissions
The passage presents two transmissions: one from Mani (in Tabyin) stating the fatwa is on the Sahibayn; another from Fatawa Sughra distinguishing between contracts. Identify what each transmission says about ijarah al-musha'.
Mani is a source, possibly a scholar or text.
3
Understand the Principle of Balwa 'Amm
Balwa 'amm (general need) is a recognized factor in later Hanafi fatwa that allows adopting a weaker or minority opinion when the stronger opinion would cause hardship. Note how Fatawa Sughra applies it to muzara'ah, mu'amalah, and waqf, but not to ijarah al-musha'.
The passage shows balwa 'amm supporting Sahibayn in some contracts but not in ijarah al-musha'.
4
Identify the Authorities Supporting Abu Hanifa
The Haqa'iq cites Shaykh Nasafi, Burhan al-A'immah Mahbub, and Sadr al-Shari'ah as relying on Abu Hanifa's view. Recognize their authority in the later Hanafi school.
These are major later Hanafi figures (fatawa mutakhkhirin).
5
Determine the Mufta Bihi
Weigh the conflicting transmissions. The passage does not explicitly resolve, but the weight of authorities quoted (Fatawa Sughra, Haqa'iq, and the named scholars) suggests the mufta bihi for ijarah al-musha' is Abu Hanifa's position.
The mufta bihi is the operative ruling for fatwa, not necessarily the zahir al-riwayah.

Source Text

Hiring a Wet Nurse for a Known Wage
Establishing permissibility and legal nature of hiring a wet nurse

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on hiring a wet nurse, identify the two opinions on the subject matter of the contract, and apply the condition that the wage must be known.

Core Idea
Hiring a wet nurse is a valid ijarah on her service; the milk is only a subordinate benefit.

This passage from the Hidayah establishes the permissibility of hiring a wet nurse (istijar al-dha'ir) for a known wage. It cites the Quranic command to pay wet nurses their wages and the continuous practice of the early Muslim community. The key legal discussion centers on whether the contract is for the service of nursing (benefit) or for the milk itself, with the Hanafi school preferring the former. This distinction is crucial because ijarah is fundamentally a contract on benefits, not on the consumption of physical objects.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage rules on hiring a wet nurse (istijar al-dha'ir). The hukm is ja'iz (permissible) provided the wage is known.
The ruling is based on the Quran and established practice.
2
Locate the dalil
The primary evidence is Quran 65:6: 'If they suckle your children, then give them their wages.' This is a general command to pay wages for nursing.
The imperative indicates obligation, but the permissibility of the contract is derived from the implied approval.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The phrase 'fatuhunna ajoorahunna' is an imperative, and in Hanafi usul, al-amr yufidu al-wujub. However, the context here establishes the legitimacy of paying wages for nursing, which implies the permissibility of making a contract for it.
The text also cites the ongoing practice during the Prophet's time and his confirmation.
4
Analyze the two opinions on the subject matter
Two opinions are presented: (1) the contract is on the benefit (the wet nurse's service), with milk as subordinate; (2) the contract is on the milk, with service as subordinate. The text prefers the first because ijarah is not meant for the destruction of physical objects ('ayan).
The analogy: hiring a cow to drink its milk is invalid because it involves consuming the 'ayn. Similarly, if the contract were for milk itself, it would be an invalid ijarah.
5
Determine the condition for validity
The wage must be known (ajrah ma'lumah). This is a general condition for ijarah contracts, analogous to hiring for service.
If the wage is unknown, the contract is fasid (voidable) according to Hanafi fiqh.

And it is said that the contract is on the milk and the service is subordinate; that is why if she feeds with goat's milk, she does not deserve the wage. The first opinion is closer to fiqh because a contract of ijarah is not concluded primarily for the destruction of physical objects ('ayan), as if one hires a cow to drink its milk. And we will explain the excuse for suckling with goat's milk, God willing. And when what we mentioned is established, it is valid if the wage is known, by analogy to hiring for service. Explanation: He said 'and it is permissible to hire a wet nurse...' i.e., hiring a nursing woman with a known wage is permissible.
Source pages p. 67

Commentary
This passage presents the ruling on hiring a wet nurse (istijar al-dha'ir) for a known wage. It is a ruling with proof from the Quran: 'If they suckle your children, then give them their wages' (Surah al-Talaq, 65:6) and from the established practice of the Prophet ﷺ. The key legal discussion is the nature of the contract: two opinions are given. The first opinion holds that the contract is on the benefit (the wet nurse's service of nursing and caring for the child), and the milk is merely a subordinate consequence, like dye on cloth. The second opinion holds that the contract is on the milk itself, and the service is subordinate. The text prefers the first opinion as more consistent with the principles of fiqh, because an ijarah contract is not primarily intended for the destruction of physical objects (like consuming milk directly); analogous to hiring a cow to drink its milk, which is invalid. If the contract were on the milk, then feeding the child with goat's milk (which is not the wet nurse's own milk) would still entitle her to wages, but the law says she does not. This supports the first opinion. The passage concludes that the contract is valid if the wage is known, by analogy to hiring for service. This is a classic Hanafi analysis distinguishing between the benefit (manfa'ah) and the substance ('ayn), with the benefit being the proper subject of ijarah.

Key Terms
ظئر (dha'ir): A wet nurse; a woman hired to breastfeed a child.
اجرت معلومہ (ajrah ma'lumah): A wage that is known and specified in the contract, a condition for validity of ijarah.
منافع (manafi'): Benefits or services that are the subject matter of ijarah.
تبع (taba'): Subordinate; something that follows the primary subject of the contract.
اتلاف اعیان (itlaf a'yan): Consumption/destruction of physical objects; ijarah is not valid for this purpose.

The Subject Matter of Ijarah for a Wet Nurse: Service or Milk?
Analyzes two views on the object of ijarah for a wet nurse.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the two Hanafi views on the ma'qud 'alayh of a wet nurse's ijarah and state the preferred position with its proof.

Core Idea
Ijarah is on usufruct, not on 'ayn; the contract of a wet nurse is on service, milk subsidiary.

This passage examines a nuanced dispute among later Hanafi scholars: when you hire a wet nurse, is the contract actually on her milk or on her service of nursing? The answer carries practical consequences for the validity of the contract and entitlement to wages. We will walk through both views, the reasoning behind each, and the preferred Hanafi position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two views
First, clearly state the two opinions: View 1 says the subject matter (ma'qud 'alayh) is the wet nurse's service (khidmah), and the milk is subsidiary. View 2 says the subject matter is the milk itself, and the service is subsidiary.
Note that both views accept the contract is valid; the disagreement is about the exact object.
2
Understand the evidence for View 1
The author of al-Hidayah and others argue that ijarah is fundamentally on usufruct (manafi'), not on a physical entity ('ayn) that is consumed. Milk is an 'ayn that is destroyed by consumption, so it cannot be the direct subject. They analogize to renting a cow for its milk, which is invalid.
The analogy (qiyas) is central: if ijarah on milk were allowed, it would be like renting a cow just to drink its milk.
3
Understand the evidence for View 2
Al-Sarakhsi and others point to the case where the wet nurse feeds the child goat's milk instead of her own: she is not entitled to the wage. They argue this shows the contract is on her specific milk, not on general service.
The text notes that the reason for that ruling will be explained later as 'she did not perform the required work', which actually supports View 1.
4
Apply the principle of ijarah
Recall the Hanafi rule: ijarah is a contract on manafi' (usufructs), not on 'ayn. Therefore, the subject matter must be a service or benefit, not a physical substance like milk that gets consumed.
This principle is from Zahir al-Riwayah and is well-established.
5
Determine the preferred view
The author of al-Hidayah declares View 1 as 'aqrab bi usul al-fiqh' (closer to legal principles). This is the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position. The second view is weaker because it contradicts the nature of ijarah.
The tarjih is based on the strength of the qiyas argument and the foundational principle.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله ثم قيل ... الخ - اتا کے اجارہ میں معقود علیہ اس کا لین یعنی اس کا دودھ ہوتا ہے یا اس کے منافع ؟ اس کی بابت مشائخ کا اختلاف ہے۔ بعض نے کہا ہے کہ معقود علیہ اس کے منافع ہوتے ہیں یعنی بچہ کی خدمت کرنا اس کے امور کی دیکھ بھال کرنا وغیرہ، رہا دودھ سو وہ تابع ہو کر مستحق ہوتا ہے جیسے کپڑے میں رنگ ہوتا ہے۔ صاحب ایضاح، صاحب ذخیرہ ، امام احمد و امام شافعی کے بعض اصحاب صاحب ہدایہ اور حافظ الدین صاحب کافی نے اس قول کو اختیار کیا ہے اور بعض نے کہا ہے کہ عقد اجارہ در حقیقت دودھ پر واقع ہوتا ہے۔ رہا بچہ کی خدمت کرنا سو وہ اس کے تابع ہے۔ یہی وجہ ہے کہ اگر انا بچہ کو بکری کا دودھ پلائے تو وہ اجرت کی مستحق نہیں ہوتی محقق شمس الائمہ سرخسی نے اس کو اختیار کیا ہے اور صاحب نہا یہ وعلامہ عینی نے اسی کو میچ ٹھہرایا ہے۔
قوله والا ول اقرب ..... الخ - صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ اقرب باصول فقہ پہلا قول ہے کہ اجارہ در اصل خدمت پر واقع ہوتا ہے اور دودھ تابع ہے۔ اس لئے کہ عقد اجارہ بالقصد اتلاف عین پر واقع نہیں ہوتا اور دودھ بھی ایک شی عین ہے تو اس کے پینے پر اجارہ نہیں ہو سکتا۔ جیسے مکان بیچ کھانے پر اجارہ نہیں ہوتا بلکہ انتفاع پر ہوتا ہے۔ اگر اجارہ دودھ پر ہو تو ایسا ہوگا جیسے کوئی گائے دودھ پینے کے لئے اجارہ پر لے کہ یہ جائز نہیں ہے۔ رہا بکری کا دودھ پلانے سے اجرت کا مستحق نہ ہونا سو اس کی وجہ آئندہ قول لانها لم تأت بعمل مستحق علیھا میں آرہی ہے۔
Then he said: In the ijarah of a wet nurse, what is the subject matter? Is it her milk or her services? There is disagreement among the mashayikh. Some said the subject matter is her services, i.e., taking care of the child, looking after its affairs, etc.; as for the milk, it is subsidiary and owed only as a consequence, like dye in a cloth. The authors of al-Idah, al-Dhakhirah, some followers of Imam Ahmad and Imam al-Shafi'i, the author of al-Hidayah, and Hafiz al-Din al-Kafi chose this view. Others said the ijarah contract actually occurs on the milk; the service is subsidiary. This is why if the wet nurse feeds the child with goat's milk, she is not entitled to wage. Muhqiq Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi chose this, and the authors of al-Nihayah and Allamah Ayni deemed it preferred. He said: The first view is closer to the principles of fiqh; ijarah is essentially on service, and milk is subsidiary. Because the ijarah contract is not intentionally for consuming an entity ('ayn), and milk is an entity; thus it cannot be leased for drinking, just as a house is not leased for eating but for usufruct. If ijarah were on milk, it would be like renting a cow for drinking its milk, which is invalid. As for not being entitled to wage when feeding goat's milk, its reason will come in the later statement 'because she did not perform the required work'.
Source pages p. 68

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute about the subject matter (معقود علیہ) of the ijarah contract for a wet nurse. Two opinions are presented: (1) the contract is on the service (khidmah) of taking care of the child, and the milk is merely a subsidiary benefit akin to dye in cloth; (2) the contract is on the milk itself, and the service is subsidiary. The author of al-Hidayah and many others prefer the first view, as it aligns with the general principle that ijarah is on usufruct (manafi') not on entities ('ayn). The reasoning is that consuming milk involves destroying an 'ayn, which is not the purpose of ijarah. An analogy is drawn with renting a house: one does not rent it for eating the structure but for benefiting from its space. Similarly, renting a cow for its milk would be invalid. The opposing view is attributed to al-Sarakhsi and others, who argue that the contract is on the milk, as shown by the case where she feeds goat's milk and gets no wage. However, the text notes that the reason for that ruling will be explained later (as 'not performing the required work'). Thus, the preferred Hanafi position is that ijarah is on service, not the milk.

Key Terms
معقود علیہ (ma'qud 'alayh): The subject matter of the contract; what the contract is concluded upon.
منافع (manafi'): Usufructs; services or benefits derived from an asset or person.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the preferred Hanafi view, what is the subject matter (ma'qud 'alayh) of the ijarah contract for a wet nurse?
A) The milk of the wet nurse
B) The service (khidmah) of caring for the child, with milk subsidiary
C) Both equally
D) The child itself

Key Takeaway
The ijarah of a wet nurse is valid and its subject is her service, not her milk; the milk is a subsidiary benefit.

Ijarah — Hire and Lease
intermediate
8 min
Hiring a Wet Nurse for Food and Clothing: Istihsan Overrides Qiyas
Ruling with proof: istihsan over qiyas

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why Abu Hanifa validates hiring a wet nurse for food and clothing by istihsan and contrast this with qiyas.

Core Idea
Jahalah is excused when custom prevents dispute — istihsan permits what qiyas forbids.

This passage addresses a specific ijarah scenario: paying a wet nurse with food and clothing rather than fixed wages. Abu Hanifa rules it valid by istihsan, while the Sahibayn and Imam al-Shafi'i invalidate it by qiyas. The key is whether the uncertainty (jahalah) in the wage leads to dispute. Understanding this istihsan argument is essential for grasping how Hanafi law balances textual rules with practical custom.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Note that the act is hiring a wet nurse (al-dha'r) for her food and clothing. Abu Hanifa says it is permissible (ja'iz) by istihsan.
2
Recognize the qiyas objection
The Sahibayn and al-Shafi'i argue that the wage is majhul (unknown), analogous to hiring for baking and cooking, which is invalid.
3
Analyze Abu Hanifa's istihsan proof
The jahalah here does not lead to dispute (niza') because custom makes people generous towards wet nurses out of compassion for children. This is compared to selling a qafiz from a pile, where slight uncertainty is tolerated.
4
Distinguish from baking and cooking
In baking and cooking, ignorance about the quantity actually leads to dispute, so the analogy (qiyas) fails and istihsan overrides it.
5
Consider the consensus option
If the food is specified in dirhams and clothing described with type, term, and yards, the contract becomes valid by consensus (ijma'). This shows a clear pathway to avoid any uncertainty.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كھانے اور کپڑے کے عوض انا کو اجارہ پر لینا بھی جائز ہے
قال ويجوز بطعامها وكسوتها استحسانا عند ابي حنيفة وقالا لايجوز لان الاجرة مجهولة فصار كما اذا استاجرها للخبز والطبخ وله ان الجهالة لا تفضى الى المنازعة لان فى العادة التوسعة على الأظار شفقة على الاولاد فصار كبيع قفيز من صبرة بخلاف الخبز والطبخ لان الجهالة فيه تفضى الى المنازعة وفي الجامع الصغير فان سمى الطعام دراهم ووصف جنس الكسوة واجلها وذروعها فهو جائز يعنى بالاجماع ومعنى تسمية الطعام دراهم ان يجعل الاجرة دراهم ثم يدفع الطعام مكانها وهذا لا جهالة فيه
ترجمہ اور جائز ہے اس کی خوراک پوشاک کے عوض استحسانا امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک صاحبین فرماتے ہیں کہ جائز نہیں۔ کیونکہ اجرت مجہول ہے پس ایسا ہو گیا۔ جیسے عورت کو روٹی سالن پکانے کے لئے اجارہ پر لیا۔ امام ابوحنیفہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ یہ جہالت جھگڑے تک نہیں پہنچائے گی ۔ کیونکہ عادت یہی ہے کہ دودھ پلانے والی عورتوں پر وسعت و کشائش ہوتی ہے۔ اولا د پر شفقت کے پیش نظر پس یہ ڈھیری میں سے ایک فیز فروخت کرنے کے مانند ہو گیا۔ بخلاف روٹی سالن پکانے کے کیونکہ یہ جہالت جھگڑے تک پہنچائے گی۔

كتاب الاجارات
YA
اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد ۱۲ جامع صغیر میں ہے کہ اگر طعام کے درہم اور پوشاک کی جنس اس کی مدت اور اس کے گز بیان کر دیئے تو یہ جائز ہے یعنی بالا جماع اور طعام کے درہم بیان کرنے کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ اجرت کے درہم مقرر کرے پھر اس کے بجائے طعام دے دے اور اس میں در حقیقت
کوئی جہالت نہیں ہے۔ تشريح .. قوله ويجوز بطعا مها .... الخ امام ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک بدلیل استحسان النا کو اس کی خوراک پوشاک کے عوض اجرت پر لینا بھی جائز ہے۔ امام مالک اور امام احمد بھی اس کے قائل ہیں ۔ چنانچہ حاوی حنابلہ میں ہے
ويصح استيجار الظرُ بطعامها و كسوتها ولها الوسط
صاحبین اور امام شافعی کے یہاں جائز نہیں مقتضائے قیاس بھی یہی ہے۔ کیونکہ اجرت مجہول ہے تو ایسا ہو گیا جیسے عورت کو روٹی اور کھانا پکانے کیلئے اجرت پر لیا اور کہا کہ ہر روز دس سیر آٹا اور دس سیر گوشت پکا جس کی اجرت کھانا اور کپڑا ہوگا ۔ حالانکہ یہ جائز
نہیں ہے۔
قوله وله ان الجهالة .. الخ - امام ابو حنیفہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ یہ جہالت موجب منازعت نہیں ہے ۔ کیونکہ بچہ کی ابوحنیفہ محبت و شفقت کی وجہ سے انا پر خوراک و پوشاک میں کشائش کی عام عادت ہے۔ پس یہ ایسا ہو گیا۔ جیسے ڈھیری میں سے ایک قفیز کو فروخت کرنا کہ اس میں بھی کوئی منازعت پیش نہیں آتی بلکہ بائع جس طرف سے چاہے دے دے۔ بخلاف روٹی سالن پکانے کے اجارہ کے کہ اس میں اجرت مجہول ہونے سے جھگڑے تک نوبت پہنچے گی۔
غلہ کا نام لے کر اس کی مقدار بیان کرنا اجارہ کے جواز کے لئے کافی ہے
ولو سمى الطعام وبين قدره جاز ايضا لما قلنا ولا يشترط تاجيله لان اوصافها اثمان ويشترط بيان مكان الايفاء عند ابي حنيفة خلافا لهما وقد ذكرناه في البيوع وفي الكسوة يشترط بيان الاجل ايضا مع بيان القدر والجنس لانه انما يصير دينا في الذمة اذا صار مبيعا وانما يصير مبيعا عند الاجل كما في السلم قال وليس للمستاجر أن يمنع زوجها من وطيها لان الوطى حق الزوج فلا يتمكن من ابطال حقه الا ترى ان له ان يفسخ الاجارة اذا لم يعلم به صيانة لحقه الا ان المستاجر يمنعه عن غشيانها في منزله لان المنزل حقه. فان حبلت كان لهم ان يفسخوا الاجارة اذا خافوا على الصبى من لبنها لان لبن الحامل يفسد الصبي فلهذا كان لهم الفسخ اذا مرضت ايضا وعليها ان تصلح طعام الصبى لان العمل عليها والحاصل انه يعتبر فيما لا نص عليه العرف فى مثل هذا الباب فما جرى به العرف من غسل ثياب الصبي واصلاح الطعام وغیر ذالک فهو على الظئر اما الطعام فعلى والد الولد وما ذكر محمد ان الدهن والريحان على الظئر فذالك من عادة اهل الكوفة وان ارضعته في المدة بلبن شاة فلا اجر لها لانها لم تات بعمل مستحق عليها وهو الارضاع فان هذا ايجار وليس بارضاع فانما لم يجب الاجر لهذا المعنى انه اختلف العمل. توضیح اللغة تسا جیل مہلت دینا ۔ اثمان جمع شمن ۔ ایفاء پورا کرنا ۔ کسو لباس ۔ اجل مدت - صيانة حفاظت ۔ غشيان ڈھانپنا ۔ مراد جماع کرنا ، حبلت (س) حبلاً حاملہ ہوتا ، لبن دودھ ظئر انا ، ومن تیل۔ ریحان خوشبو، ارضعته ارضاعاً روده
And it is permissible to hire her for her food and clothing by istihsan according to Abu Hanifa, but the Two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said it is not permissible because the wage is unknown, so it becomes like hiring her for baking and cooking. Abu Hanifa's proof is that this ignorance does not lead to dispute because it is customary to be generous to wet nurses out of compassion for the children; thus it becomes like selling a qafiz from a stack, unlike baking and cooking where ignorance leads to dispute. In al-Jami' al-Saghir: if he specifies the food in dirhams, and describes the type of clothing, its term, and its yards, it is valid by consensus. The meaning of specifying food in dirhams is to set the wage in dirhams and then give food instead; this has no ignorance. Explanation: Ibn al-Humam, etc. The Two and al-Shafi'i say it is not permissible, and qiyas also indicates this. The text 'and his proof that ignorance does not lead to dispute' is Abu Hanifa's proof. Stating the grain and its quantity is sufficient for permissibility. And if he specifies the food and clarifies its quantity, it is valid as we said. Deferment of the wage is not required because its descriptions are like prices. Specifying the place of delivery is required according to Abu Hanifa, contrary to them. For clothing, specifying the term is also required along with quantity and type, because it becomes a debt in the dhimmah only when it becomes a sold item, and it becomes a sold item at the term like salam. He said: The hirer may not prevent her husband from intercourse with her because intercourse is the husband's right; he cannot nullify his right. But the hirer prevents him from covering her in his house because the house is his right. If she becomes pregnant, they may cancel the ijarah if they fear for the child from her milk, because the milk of a pregnant woman harms the child. Similarly, if she falls ill. She must prepare the child's food, as the work is upon her. In summary, custom is considered in matters where there is no text. Whatever customarily falls upon the wet nurse, like washing the child's clothes and preparing food, is on her; as for the food, it is on the child's father. What Muhammad mentioned that oil and perfume are on the wet nurse is the custom of the people of Kufa. If during the term she feeds the child with goat's milk, she gets no wage because she did not perform the required work, which is breastfeeding; this is ijarah not breastfeeding, so wage is not due for this reason, because the work differed.
Source pages p. 68

Commentary
This passage discusses the permissibility of hiring a wet nurse in exchange for food and clothing, a specific application of ijarah. Abu Hanifa rules it valid by istihsan (juristic preference), while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) deem it invalid by qiyas because the wage is unknown. Abu Hanifa's istihsan relies on two factors: (1) the ignorance (jahalah) here does not lead to dispute due to the customary generosity towards wet nurses out of compassion for children, analogized to selling a qafiz from a pile; and (2) the contract can be made precise by specifying the food in dirhams and describing the clothing's type, term, and measurement, as mentioned in al-Jami' al-Saghir, making it valid by consensus. The text then elaborates conditions: for food, specifying quantity suffices; place of delivery must be specified per Abu Hanifa; for clothing, term (ajal) is also required, as it becomes a salam-like debt. Further subsidiary rulings: the hirer cannot prevent the husband from intercourse (the husband's right), but can prevent it in the hirer's house (his right). The ijarah may be canceled if the wet nurse becomes pregnant or ill, due to harm to the child. Custom determines incidental duties (washing, etc.), but food is on the father. If she feeds with goat's milk, no wage is due as she did not perform the required breastfeeding. The passage concludes with a vocabulary list.

Key Terms
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference that overrides qiyas due to custom, necessity, or preventing hardship.
جهالة (jahalah): Ignorance or uncertainty in a contract term that could lead to dispute.
قفيز (qafiz): A unit of measurement for grain; here used in the example of selling a qafiz from a pile (ja'iz).
الظئر (al-dha'r): The wet nurse.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary reason for Abu Hanifa's ruling that hiring a wet nurse for food and clothing is valid?
A) Qiyas on baking and cooking
B) The ignorance does not lead to dispute due to custom
C) It is explicitly mentioned in the Quran
D) All scholars agree on it

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school validates hiring a wet nurse for food and clothing by istihsan because custom prevents dispute, overriding qiyas.

Ijarah — Hire and Lease

Conditions and Subsidiary Rulings in Wet Nurse Ijarah
Detailed conditions and subsidiary rulings for ijarah al-dha'r

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for a valid wet nurse ijarah contract and apply subsidiary rulings regarding the husband's rights, cancellation, and the wet nurse's duties.

Core Idea
Custom fills the gaps in ijarah contracts, but key terms must be specified to avoid dispute.

While the core ruling permits the contract, al-Hidayah then lays out detailed conditions and exceptions. These ensure that the contract is fair and that neither party suffers. Conditions include specifying the food, clothing, term, and place; subsidiary rulings address the husband's right to intercourse, cancellation due to pregnancy/illness, and the wet nurse's duties based on custom.

Guided Path
1
List the conditions for the wage (food and clothing)
The text mentions that specifying the food in dirhams, or at least the quantity and type, and for clothing the type, term, and measurement, are required for a valid contract by consensus.
2
Identify the dispute on place of delivery
Abu Hanifa requires specifying the place of delivery (makan al-ifa'), while the Sahibayn do not. This is analogous to the rules for sales (buyu').
3
Understand the husband's right to intercourse
The hirer cannot prevent the husband from intercourse because it is his right, but the hirer can prevent it in his own house because that is his right.
4
Recognize grounds for cancellation
The ijarah may be canceled if the wet nurse becomes pregnant or falls ill, because her milk may harm the child.
5
Determine duties based on custom
Custom determines the wet nurse's duties (washing clothes, preparing food) beyond breastfeeding; the father provides the food itself.

غلہ کا نام لے کر اس کی مقدار بیان کرنا اجارہ کے جواز کے لئے کافی ہے
ولو سمى الطعام وبين قدره جاز ايضا لما قلنا ولا يشترط تاجيله لان اوصافها اثمان ويشترط بيان مكان الايفاء عند ابي حنيفة خلافا لهما وقد ذكرناه في البيوع وفي الكسوة يشترط بيان الاجل ايضا مع بيان القدر والجنس لانه انما يصير دينا في الذمة اذا صار مبيعا وانما يصير مبيعا عند الاجل كما في السلم قال وليس للمستاجر أن يمنع زوجها من وطيها لان الوطى حق الزوج فلا يتمكن من ابطال حقه الا ترى ان له ان يفسخ الاجارة اذا لم يعلم به صيانة لحقه الا ان المستاجر يمنعه عن غشيانها في منزله لان المنزل حقه. فان حبلت كان لهم ان يفسخوا الاجارة اذا خافوا على الصبى من لبنها لان لبن الحامل يفسد الصبي فلهذا كان لهم الفسخ اذا مرضت ايضا وعليها ان تصلح طعام الصبى لان العمل عليها والحاصل انه يعتبر فيما لا نص عليه العرف فى مثل هذا الباب فما جرى به العرف من غسل ثياب الصبي واصلاح الطعام وغیر ذالک فهو على الظئر اما الطعام فعلى والد الولد وما ذكر محمد ان الدهن والريحان على الظئر فذالك من عادة اهل الكوفة وان ارضعته في المدة بلبن شاة فلا اجر لها لانها لم تات بعمل مستحق عليها وهو الارضاع فان هذا ايجار وليس بارضاع فانما لم يجب الاجر لهذا المعنى انه اختلف العمل. توضیح اللغة تسا جیل مہلت دینا ۔ اثمان جمع شمن ۔ ایفاء پورا کرنا ۔ کسو لباس ۔ اجل مدت - صيانة حفاظت ۔ غشيان ڈھانپنا ۔ مراد جماع کرنا ، حبلت (س) حبلاً حاملہ ہوتا ، لبن دودھ ظئر انا ، ومن تیل۔ ریحان خوشبو، ارضعته ارضاعاً روده
And it is permissible to hire her for her food and clothing by istihsan according to Abu Hanifa, but the Two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said it is not permissible because the wage is unknown, so it becomes like hiring her for baking and cooking. Abu Hanifa's proof is that this ignorance does not lead to dispute because it is customary to be generous to wet nurses out of compassion for the children; thus it becomes like selling a qafiz from a stack, unlike baking and cooking where ignorance leads to dispute. In al-Jami' al-Saghir: if he specifies the food in dirhams, and describes the type of clothing, its term, and its yards, it is valid by consensus. The meaning of specifying food in dirhams is to set the wage in dirhams and then give food instead; this has no ignorance. Explanation: Ibn al-Humam, etc. The Two and al-Shafi'i say it is not permissible, and qiyas also indicates this. The text 'and his proof that ignorance does not lead to dispute' is Abu Hanifa's proof. Stating the grain and its quantity is sufficient for permissibility. And if he specifies the food and clarifies its quantity, it is valid as we said. Deferment of the wage is not required because its descriptions are like prices. Specifying the place of delivery is required according to Abu Hanifa, contrary to them. For clothing, specifying the term is also required along with quantity and type, because it becomes a debt in the dhimmah only when it becomes a sold item, and it becomes a sold item at the term like salam. He said: The hirer may not prevent her husband from intercourse with her because intercourse is the husband's right; he cannot nullify his right. But the hirer prevents him from covering her in his house because the house is his right. If she becomes pregnant, they may cancel the ijarah if they fear for the child from her milk, because the milk of a pregnant woman harms the child. Similarly, if she falls ill. She must prepare the child's food, as the work is upon her. In summary, custom is considered in matters where there is no text. Whatever customarily falls upon the wet nurse, like washing the child's clothes and preparing food, is on her; as for the food, it is on the child's father. What Muhammad mentioned that oil and perfume are on the wet nurse is the custom of the people of Kufa. If during the term she feeds the child with goat's milk, she gets no wage because she did not perform the required work, which is breastfeeding; this is ijarah not breastfeeding, so wage is not due for this reason, because the work differed.
Source pages p. 68

Commentary
This passage discusses the permissibility of hiring a wet nurse in exchange for food and clothing, a specific application of ijarah. Abu Hanifa rules it valid by istihsan (juristic preference), while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) deem it invalid by qiyas because the wage is unknown. Abu Hanifa's istihsan relies on two factors: (1) the ignorance (jahalah) here does not lead to dispute due to the customary generosity towards wet nurses out of compassion for children, analogized to selling a qafiz from a pile; and (2) the contract can be made precise by specifying the food in dirhams and describing the clothing's type, term, and measurement, as mentioned in al-Jami' al-Saghir, making it valid by consensus. The text then elaborates conditions: for food, specifying quantity suffices; place of delivery must be specified per Abu Hanifa; for clothing, term (ajal) is also required, as it becomes a salam-like debt. Further subsidiary rulings: the hirer cannot prevent the husband from intercourse (the husband's right), but can prevent it in the hirer's house (his right). The ijarah may be canceled if the wet nurse becomes pregnant or ill, due to harm to the child. Custom determines incidental duties (washing, etc.), but food is on the father. If she feeds with goat's milk, no wage is due as she did not perform the required breastfeeding. The passage concludes with a vocabulary list.

Key Terms
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference that overrides qiyas due to custom, necessity, or preventing hardship.
جهالة (jahalah): Ignorance or uncertainty in a contract term that could lead to dispute.
قفيز (qafiz): A unit of measurement for grain; here used in the example of selling a qafiz from a pile (ja'iz).
الظئر (al-dha'r): The wet nurse.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what happens if the wet nurse feeds the child goat's milk during the contract term?
A) She gets full wage
B) She gets no wage because she did not perform breastfeeding
C) She gets half wage
D) The contract is invalid

Key Takeaway
The wet nurse ijarah contract is valid with specific conditions; custom defines many duties, but failure to perform breastfeeding forfeits the wage.

Ijarah — Hire and Lease
intermediate
6 min
Hiring a Wet Nurse with Food and Clothing
Ruling on hiring a wet nurse with food and clothing, with proofs and conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school permits hiring a wet nurse with food and clothing as wages despite the uncertainty (jahala), and state the conditions for the contract's validity.

Core Idea
Uncertainty in wages is tolerated when custom prevents disputes, making the wet nurse hire valid.

Hiring a wet nurse is a common practice, but when the wages are paid in food and clothing rather than fixed dirhams, a legal question arises: is the contract valid despite the uncertainty? The Hanafi school, led by Abu Hanifa, permits it by istihsan due to custom, while the Sahibayn and al-Shafi'i object by qiyas. This lesson unpacks the dispute and the conditions that make the contract sound.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling: Abu Hanifa permits hiring a wet nurse with food and clothing as wages. Note that this is based on istihsan, not qiyas.
Contrast with the opposing view.
2
Identify the opponent and their proof
The two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) and Imam al-Shafi'i argue by qiyas: since the wage is unknown, the contract is invalid, like hiring a cook with food and clothing.
Understand the analogy.
3
Analyse the Hanafi response
Abu Hanifa responds that the jahala here does not cause dispute because custom ensures the father provides generously. He analogizes to selling a qafiz from a heap.
Note the role of custom.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: Hanafis uphold the contract; others require exact specification. What does this mean in everyday life?
Also note that Malik and Hanbal agree with Abu Hanifa.
5
List the conditions for validity
For food: specify type and quantity (or dirhams). For clothing: specify type, quantity, and term. Place of delivery must be specified per Abu Hanifa. Customary duties of the wet nurse are also defined.
These conditions make the contract free from harmful uncertainty.
