اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد ۱۲ پلانا ۔ ایجاد منہ میں دوا ڈالنا۔
۶۹
كتاب الاجارات
ترجمہ اور اگر طعام بیان کر کے اس کی مقدار بیان کر دی تب بھی جائز ہے۔ اسی وجہ سے جو ہم نے بیان کی اور اس کی مدت کا بیان شرما نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ طعام کے اوصاف تو شمن ہیں۔ ہاں ادائیگی کی جگہ کا بیان شرط ہے۔ امام ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک برخلاف صاحبین کے اور ہم اس کو بیوع میں ذکر کر چکے اور پوشاک میں بیان مدت بھی شرط ہے بیان مقدار و جنس کے ساتھ اس لئے کہ پوشاک آدمی کے ذمہ اسی وقت لازم ہوگی جب وہ میچ ہو جائے اور مبیع بوقت میعاد ہی ہوگی جیسے سلم میں ہوتا ہے اور حق نہیں مستاجر کو اس کا مرد کے اس کے شوہر کو اس کے ساتھ صحبت کرنے سے کیونکہ صحبت تو شوہر کا حق ہے تو مستاجر اس کے حق کو توڑنے پر قابو نہیں پاسکتا۔ کیا نہیں دیکھتے کہ شو ہر کو فسخ اجارہ کا اختیار ہے۔ جب کہ اس کو اجارہ کا علم نہ ہو اپنے حق کی حفاظت کی خاطر ، ہاں مستاجر اپنے گھر میں اس کے شوہر کو ولی کرنے سے روک سکتا ہے۔ کیونکہ مکان اس کا حق ہے۔ پھر اگر وہ حاملہ ہو جائے تو انہیں اجارہ فسخ کرنے کا حق ہے جب انہیں بچہ کے متعلق اندیشہ ہو اس کے دودھ سے۔ کیونکہ حاملہ کا دودھ بچہ کے لئے نقصان دہ ہوتا ہے اسی لئے ان کو فسخ کرنے کا اختیار ہوتا ہے۔ جب کہ انا بیمار ہو جائے اور اس پر لازم ہے بچہ کی غذا کا درست کرنا ۔ کیونکہ مفید عمل اس کے ذمہ لازم ہے۔ حاصل یہ کہ جس امر میں نص وارد نہیں اس میں عرف معتبر ہے ایسے معاملات میں پس جس بات کا عرف جاری ہو۔ جیسے بچہ کے کپڑے دھونا اس کے کھانے کی اصلاح کرنا وغیرہ تو یہ انا کے ذمہ ہوگا۔ رہا طعام سو وہ بچہ کے باپ پر ہوگا۔ اور یہ جو امام محمد نے ذکر کیا ہے کہ تیل اور خوشبواتا پر لا زم ہے تو یہ اہل کوفہ کی عادت پر ہے۔ اور اگر اس نے مدت اجارہ میں بکری کا دودھ پلایا تو اس کے لئے کچھ اجرت نہ ہوگی ۔ کیونکہ جو کام اس پر واجب ہوا تھا یعنی دودھ پلانا وہ اس نے نہیں کیا اس لئے کہ یہ تو منہ میں ڈال دینا ہے نہ کہ دودھ پلانا ۔ پس اسی وجہ سے کہ عمل بدل گیا۔ اجرت واجب نہیں ہوئی۔
تشریح .. ولو سمى الطعام .... الخ اور اگر زیر بحث مسئلہ میں طعام بیان کر کے اس کی مقدار بیان کر دی تو یہ بھی جائز ہے کیونکہ جنس و وصف کے ساتھ اس کی مقدار بیان کرنے کے بعد کوئی جہالت نہیں ہے پھر ادا ئیگی طعام کی مدت بیان کرنا شرط نہیں ہے۔ اس واسطے کہ طعام کے اوصاف تو اوصاف شمن ہیں۔ یعنی جو طعام معین و مشار الیہ نہ ہو بلکہ اس کا وصف بیان کر کے اپنے ذمہ رکھا گیا ہوتو وہ ثمن ہوتا ہے اور یہی ہر کیلی و وزنی چیز کا حال ہے۔ پس یہ بیچ نہیں ہے کہ اس میں میعاد کی ضرورت ہو ۔ بخلاف کپڑے کے وہ سلم کے علاوہ کسی صورت میں دین ہو کر ذمہ میں ثابت نہیں ہوتا بلکہ ہمیشہ مبیع ہوتا ہے اور سلم میں بیان میعاد شرط ہے تو ایسے ہی اگر شیاب موصوفہ کے عوض انا کو اجرت پر لیا تو بیان میعاد شرط ہو گا جیسا کہ آگے آرہا ہے۔ البتہ امام ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک ادا ئیگی طعام کی جگہ بیان کرنا شرط ہے جب کہ اس میں بار برداری ہو۔ برخلاف قول صاحبین کے جیسا که کتاب البیوع کے باب السلم میں گزر چکا۔ قوله لان اوصافها .... الخ - عام شراح نے اوصافھا کی ضمیر مؤنث کا مرجع طعام بتاویل حطہ قرار دیا ہے۔ لیکن صاحب نتائج کہتے ہیں کہ اس مسئلہ میں طعام سے مراد وہ ہے جو حطہ اور غیر حطہ سب کو عام ہے پس اس عام پر استدلال کے مقام میں خاص کے ساتھ تاویل کرنا نام نہیں ہو سکتا لہذا حق بات یہ ہے کہ ضمیر کا مرجع طعام ہے مگر یہاں اس کے اجرت ہونے کی تاویل پر
Book of Ijarat. Ashraf al-Hidayah Urdu commentary on Hidayah, vol. 12. In Jami' al-Saghir it is stated: if the dirhams of food and the type of clothing, its duration, and its yardage are specified, then it is permissible — that is, with consensus. The meaning of specifying the dirhams of food is that he fixes the dirhams as wages, then gives food in lieu thereof, and in reality there is no ignorance in that. Commentary: His statement: 'And it is permissible with its food...' etc. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, by way of istihsan, hiring a wet nurse in exchange for her food and clothing is also permissible. Imam Malik and Imam Ahmad also subscribe to this. As in al-Hawi al-Hanabila: 'It is valid to hire a wet nurse with her food and clothing, and she gets the moderate (level).' According to the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) and Imam al-Shafi'i, it is not permissible, and the requirement of qiyas is the same. Because the wage is unknown, so it becomes like hiring a woman to cook bread and food, saying: every day cook ten seers of flour and ten seers of meat, the wage being food and clothing — yet this is not permissible. His statement: 'And his (Abu Hanifa's) argument is that this ignorance does not cause dispute...' etc. Abu Hanifa's proof is that this ignorance does not lead to dispute. Because, due to the father's love and affection for the child, the general custom is that the wet nurse is given ample food and clothing. So it becomes like selling one qafiz from a heap, where no dispute arises, but the seller may give from whichever side he wishes. Unlike the hire for cooking bread and curry, where due to the unknown wage, it leads to quarrels. Specifying the name and quantity of grain is sufficient for the validity of the hire. 'And if he specifies the food and states its quantity, it is also valid for what we said, and it is not necessary to specify its term, because its attributes are prices (athman). And the place of delivery must be specified according to Abu Hanifa, contrary to the two companions, and we have mentioned this in the book of sales. In the case of clothing, specifying the term is also necessary along with specifying the quantity and type, because it only becomes a debt in the liability when it becomes a sold commodity, and it becomes a sold commodity at the specified time as in salam. He said: The hirer does not have the right to prevent her husband from having intercourse with her, because intercourse is the husband's right, so he cannot annul his right. Do you not see that he (the husband) has the right to rescind the hire if he was unaware of it, to protect his right? However, the hirer can prevent him from approaching her in his (the hirer's) house, because the house is his right. If she becomes pregnant, they have the right to rescind the hire if they fear for the child from her milk, because the milk of a pregnant woman spoils the child. For this reason they have the right to rescind also if she falls ill. And she must prepare the child's food, because the work is upon her. The outcome is that in matters where there is no text, custom is considered in such matters. So what custom dictates, such as washing the child's clothes, preparing food, etc., are upon the wet nurse. As for food, it is upon the child's father. And what Muhammad mentioned — that oil and perfume are upon the wet nurse — that is from the custom of the people of Kufa. If she breastfeeds the child during the period with the milk of a goat, she has no wage, because she did not perform the work that was obligatory upon her, namely breastfeeding. This is because (that) is merely pouring (into the mouth) and not breastfeeding. So wages are not obliged because the act changed. Explanation: 'and if he specifies the food...' etc. And if in the matter under discussion he specifies the food and states its quantity, this is also permissible because after specifying the type, description, and quantity, there is no ignorance. Then specifying the term for delivering the food is not a condition, because the attributes of food are attributes of a price (thaman). That is, food that is not specific or pointed to, but is placed as a liability by describing it, is a price, and this is the case for every measurable or weighable item. So this is not a sale requiring a term. Unlike clothing, which cannot be established as a debt in the liability except in salam, but is always a sold commodity, and in salam specifying the term is a condition. So similarly, if a wet nurse is hired in exchange for described items, specifying the term becomes a condition, as will come later. However, according to Abu Hanifa, specifying the place of delivery of food is a condition when there is transportation involved, contrary to the statement of the two companions, as passed in the chapter on salam in the book of sales. His statement: 'because its attributes...' etc. General commentators have taken the feminine pronoun in 'attributes' as referring to food by way of interpreting it as 'grain'. But the author of Nata'ij says that in this issue, 'food' means what is common to both grain and non-grain. So it is not proper to interpret it with the specific in the place of deduction from the general. Therefore, the correct view is that the pronoun refers to food, but here it is on the interpretation of it being the wage.
Source pages p. 69

Commentary
This passage is a detailed legal discussion on the permissibility and conditions of hiring a wet nurse (za'r) with food and clothing as wages. It is from the commentary (sharh) of Ashraf al-Hidayah on the Hidayah, dealing with the Book of Ijara (hire). The passage first states the ruling from al-Jami' al-Saghir: if the food and clothing are specified in terms of dirhams (i.e., the monetary equivalent), type, duration, and yardage, then the contract is valid by consensus. The commentary then explains the disagreement: Imam Abu Hanifa, Imam Malik, and Imam Ahmad consider it permissible based on istihsan (juristic preference), because the custom is that the father provides generously, so the uncertainty (jahala) does not lead to dispute. Imam Abu Yusuf, Imam Muhammad (the Sahibayn), and Imam al-Shafi'i consider it invalid by qiyas, because the wage is unknown, analogous to hiring a cook with food and clothing as wages, which is invalid. Abu Hanifa's proof is that the jahala here is non-contentious, unlike the cooking hire. The passage then discusses conditions for validity: for food, specifying type and quantity suffices; no term is needed because food can be a price (thaman) and is not a salam sale. For clothing, specifying type, quantity, and term is necessary because clothing can only become a deferred debt through salam. The place of delivery for food must be specified according to Abu Hanifa. Additionally, the hirer cannot prevent the husband from marital relations, but can prevent him in the hirer's own house. If the wet nurse becomes pregnant or ill, the contract can be rescinded due to harm to the child. The wet nurse must prepare the child's food and perform customary duties like washing clothes. The father provides the food itself. If she breastfeeds with animal milk, she gets no wage because the required act (breastfeeding) was not performed. The commentary concludes with a note on the interpretation of the pronoun in 'attributes' (awsafiha), where some commentators interpret it as referring to food as grain, but the preferred view is that it refers to food as the wage.

Key Terms
ظئر (za'r): A wet nurse hired to breastfeed a child.
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference that overrides qiyas due to custom, necessity, or other considerations.
جہالت (jahala): Uncertainty or ignorance regarding the subject matter or wage in a contract.
قفیز (qafiz): A dry measure of volume, used here as an example of selling from a heap without precise measurement.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why is hiring a wet nurse with food and clothing as wages permissible despite the uncertainty?
A) Because the wage is precisely specified in dirhams.
B) Because custom ensures the father provides generously, preventing disputes.
C) Because the Quran explicitly permits it.
D) Because the Sahibayn agreed with Abu Hanifa.

Key Takeaway
Hiring a wet nurse with food and clothing is valid in the Hanafi school when custom prevents dispute, and conditions like specifying type, quantity, and term ensure the contract is sound.

Food as Hire for a Wet Nurse: Ruling and Conditions
Ruling with proof and intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when food is specified as hire for a wet nurse, explain why time is not required, and identify the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding place of delivery.

Core Idea
Food specified as hire is treated as a price, not a commodity; time not required but place may be.

In Hanafi fiqh, the contract to hire a wet nurse (ijara al-ana) is valid even if the payment is food rather than money, provided the food is sufficiently described by type, quantity, and quality. This lesson explores the conditions for such a contract, focusing on an intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two disciples (Sahibayn) regarding whether the place of delivery must be specified.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is hiring a wet nurse (ana) with specified food as payment. The contract is valid (sahih) if food is specified by type and quantity.
This is the main ruling.
2
Locate the dalil
The author analogizes food to a price (thaman) in a sale; price does not require a delivery time, only place may be needed to avoid ignorance (gharar).
Proof is qiyas to sale and salam.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Food described as a liability (dayn) becomes thaman; thaman in a sale can be delayed without specifying time. Clothing is analogized to a sold commodity (mabi') which in salam requires time.
Distinction between thaman and mabi'.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Imam Abu Hanifa requires specifying place of delivery if carriage is involved; Sahibayn do not.
This is an established difference within the school.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The author implies preference for Abu Hanifa's view, as it is consistent with the previous discussion in Kitab al-Buyu'.
Mufta bihi follows Abu Hanifa.

Source pages p. 70

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof and an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning the hire of a wet nurse (ana) where the payment is food. The passage begins by stating the ruling: if the food is specified by type and quantity, the contract is valid. It then explains that specifying the time for delivery of the food is not required because food, when described and made a liability, functions as a price (thaman) in the contract, not as a sold commodity (mabi'). Prices do not require a delivery time. However, specifying the place of delivery is a condition according to Imam Abu Hanifa, because if carriage is involved, ignorance of the place leads to dispute. This is contrary to the view of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn), who do not require specifying the place. The author notes this dispute was already discussed in the Book of Sales (Kitab al-Buyu'). The passage then contrasts this with clothing as hire: if clothing is the payment, it must follow the rules of salam (advance sale), requiring specification of all attributes including delivery time, because clothing cannot be established as a debt except through salam. Next, the passage addresses the husband's rights: the hirer cannot prevent the husband from sexual intercourse, as that is the husband's absolute right. However, the hirer can prevent the husband from entering the hired house because the house is the hirer's usufruct. Furthermore, the husband has the right to rescind the hire if he was unaware of it, to protect his conjugal rights. If the wet nurse becomes pregnant, the employer may rescind the contract fearing harm to the child from her milk, as pregnant women's milk is considered deleterious. If the wet nurse falls ill, she is still obliged to arrange for the child's nourishment; specific tasks like washing clothes and preparing food fall on her according to custom (urf), while the child's food expenses are on the father. Imam Muhammad's mention of oil and perfumes being mandatory is specific to Kufan custom. Finally, if the wet nurse substitutes goat's milk for her own milk, she is not entitled to payment because she changed the required service. The commentary section reinforces these points and clarifies the pronoun reference in the matn, noting that the feminine pronoun 'uwsafiha' refers to the hire (al-ujrah) taken as food, not to the food itself as a commodity. This distinction is crucial for understanding that food in this context is treated as a price.

Key Terms
طعام (ta'am): Food specified by type and quantity as payment for the wet nurse.
شمن (thaman): Price or consideration in a contract; here it describes food when it is a liability rather than a specific item.
صاحبین (sahibayn): Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, the two chief disciples of Abu Hanifa.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The time of delivery must be stated.
B) The place of delivery must be stated if there is carriage.
C) The food must be measured in a specific container.
D) The wet nurse must accept the food at the time of contract.

Key Takeaway
Food specified as hire is treated as a price, so time is not required; but place may be required per Abu Hanifa to avoid gharar.

Ancillary Rulings on Wet Nurse Hire: Rights, Pregnancy, Illness, and Custom
Series of subsidiary rulings on wet nurse hire

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the husband's right to intercourse and rescission, the employer's right to rescind due to pregnancy, the wet nurse's obligations during illness, and the role of custom in defining her duties.

Core Idea
Husband's conjugal rights override hire; pregnancy/illness may justify rescission; custom governs unspecified duties.

This lesson continues the discussion of hiring a wet nurse, addressing several practical issues that arise during the contract. These include the limits of the hirer's authority over the nurse's personal life, the effect of her pregnancy or illness on the contract, and how custom (urf) fills gaps left by the contract. Understanding these ancillary rules is essential for sound contracting and avoiding disputes.

Guided Path
1
Identify the husband's right to intercourse
The hirer cannot prevent the husband from sexual intercourse because it is his exclusive right.
This is a strong right; the hire contract does not override it.
2
State the husband's rescission option
If the husband was unaware of the hire, he can rescind it to protect his conjugal rights.
This protects the husband's rights against contracts made without his knowledge.
3
Recognize the employer's rescission right
If the wet nurse becomes pregnant, the employer may rescind due to potential harm from her milk.
Pregnant women's milk is considered harmful to the nursing child.
4
Determine obligations during illness
If she falls ill, she must arrange for the child's food; custom defines tasks like washing and preparing food.
Beneficial actions are obligatory on her; expenses on father.
5
Apply custom to specific duties
In Kufa, oil and perfumes were considered part of her duties; elsewhere, custom determines.
Custom (urf) is authoritative in matters not specified by text.

بیان شرما نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ طعام کے اوصاف تو شمن ہیں۔ ہاں ادائیگی کی جگہ کا بیان شرط ہے۔ امام ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک برخلاف صاحبین کے اور ہم اس کو بیوع میں ذکر کر چکے اور پوشاک میں بیان مدت بھی شرط ہے بیان مقدار و جنس کے ساتھ اس لئے کہ پوشاک آدمی کے ذمہ اسی وقت لازم ہوگی جب وہ میچ ہو جائے اور مبیع بوقت میعاد ہی ہوگی جیسے سلم میں ہوتا ہے اور حق نہیں مستاجر کو اس کا مرد کے اس کے شوہر کو اس کے ساتھ صحبت کرنے سے کیونکہ صحبت تو شوہر کا حق ہے تو مستاجر اس کے حق کو توڑنے پر قابو نہیں پاسکتا۔ کیا نہیں دیکھتے کہ شو ہر کو فسخ اجارہ کا اختیار ہے۔ جب کہ اس کو اجارہ کا علم نہ ہو اپنے حق کی حفاظت کی خاطر ، ہاں مستاجر اپنے گھر میں اس کے شوہر کو ولی کرنے سے روک سکتا ہے۔ کیونکہ مکان اس کا حق ہے۔ پھر اگر وہ حاملہ ہو جائے تو انہیں اجارہ فسخ کرنے کا حق ہے جب انہیں بچہ کے متعلق اندیشہ ہو اس کے دودھ سے۔ کیونکہ حاملہ کا دودھ بچہ کے لئے نقصان دہ ہوتا ہے اسی لئے ان کو فسخ کرنے کا اختیار ہوتا ہے۔ جب کہ انا بیمار ہو جائے اور اس پر لازم ہے بچہ کی غذا کا درست کرنا ۔ کیونکہ مفید عمل اس کے ذمہ لازم ہے۔ حاصل یہ کہ جس امر میں نص وارد نہیں اس میں عرف معتبر ہے ایسے معاملات میں پس جس بات کا عرف جاری ہو۔ جیسے بچہ کے کپڑے دھونا اس کے کھانے کی اصلاح کرنا وغیرہ تو یہ انا کے ذمہ ہوگا۔ رہا طعام سو وہ بچہ کے باپ پر ہوگا۔ اور یہ جو امام محمد نے ذکر کیا ہے کہ تیل اور خوشبواتا پر لا زم ہے تو یہ اہل کوفہ کی عادت پر ہے۔ اور اگر اس نے مدت اجارہ میں بکری کا دودھ پلایا تو اس کے لئے کچھ اجرت نہ ہوگی ۔ کیونکہ جو کام اس پر واجب ہوا تھا یعنی دودھ پلانا وہ اس نے نہیں کیا اس لئے کہ یہ تو منہ میں ڈال دینا ہے نہ کہ دودھ پلانا ۔ پس اسی وجہ سے کہ عمل بدل گیا۔ اجرت واجب نہیں ہوئی۔ تشریح .. ولو سمى الطعام .... الخ اور اگر زیر بحث مسئلہ میں طعام بیان کر کے اس کی مقدار بیان کر دی تو یہ بھی جائز ہے کیونکہ جنس و وصف کے ساتھ اس کی مقدار بیان کرنے کے بعد کوئی جہالت نہیں ہے پھر ادا ئیگی طعام کی مدت بیان کرنا شرط نہیں ہے۔ اس واسطے کہ طعام کے اوصاف تو اوصاف شمن ہیں۔ یعنی جو طعام معین و مشار الیہ نہ ہو بلکہ اس کا وصف بیان کر کے اپنے ذمہ رکھا گیا ہوتو وہ ثمن ہوتا ہے اور یہی ہر کیلی و وزنی چیز کا حال ہے۔ پس یہ بیچ نہیں ہے کہ اس میں میعاد کی ضرورت ہو ۔ بخلاف کپڑے کے وہ سلم کے علاوہ کسی صورت میں دین ہو کر ذمہ میں ثابت نہیں ہوتا بلکہ ہمیشہ مبیع ہوتا ہے اور سلم میں بیان میعاد شرط ہے تو ایسے ہی اگر شیاب موصوفہ کے عوض انا کو اجرت پر لیا تو بیان میعاد شرط ہو گا جیسا کہ آگے آرہا ہے۔ البتہ امام ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک ادا ئیگی طعام کی جگہ بیان کرنا شرط ہے جب کہ اس میں بار برداری ہو۔ برخلاف قول صاحبین کے جیسا که کتاب البیوع کے باب السلم میں گزر چکا۔ قوله لان اوصافها .... الخ - عام شراح نے اوصافھا کی ضمیر مؤنث کا مرجع طعام بتاویل حطہ قرار دیا ہے۔ لیکن صاحب نتائج کہتے ہیں کہ اس مسئلہ میں طعام سے مراد وہ ہے جو حطہ اور غیر حطہ سب کو عام ہے پس اس عام پر استدلال کے مقام میں خاص کے ساتھ تاویل کرنا نام نہیں ہو سکتا لہذا حق بات یہ ہے کہ ضمیر کا مرجع طعام ہے مگر یہاں اس کے اجرت ہونے کی تاویل پر فالمعنى ان هذه الاجرة اوصافها اوصاف اثمان
Translation and if food is specified and its quantity stated, then it is also permissible. For the reason we stated, and its time period is not required to be stated. Because the attributes of food are attributes of price. Yes, specifying the place of delivery is a condition, according to Imam Abu Hanifa, contrary to the two companions. And we have mentioned this in the book of sales. And in clothing, specifying the period is also a condition along with specifying quantity and type, because clothing only becomes obligatory in one's liability when it is the sold item, and the sold item only occurs at a specified time, as happens in salam. And the hirer has no right to prevent the husband from intercourse, because intercourse is the husband's right, so the hirer cannot break his right. Do you not see that the husband has the right to rescind the hire if he was unaware of it, to protect his right? Yes, the hirer can prevent the husband from entering his (the hirer's) house, because the house is his right. Then if she becomes pregnant, they have the right to rescind the hire out of fear for the child regarding her milk, because the pregnant woman's milk is harmful to the child, so they have the authority to rescind. When the wet nurse falls ill, it is incumbent upon her to correct the child's food, because beneficial action is obligatory upon her. The conclusion is that in matters where no text is transmitted, custom is authoritative in such transactions. So whatever custom is prevalent, like washing the child's clothes, preparing his food, etc., that is the wet nurse's responsibility. As for food, it is upon the child's father. And what Imam Muhammad mentioned that oil and perfumes are obligatory upon her, that is according to the custom of the people of Kufa. And if during the hire period she fed goat's milk, then she gets no payment, because the task that was obligatory upon her, i.e., breastfeeding, she did not perform, because this is just pouring into the mouth, not breastfeeding. Therefore, because the action changed, payment is not obligatory. Commentary: 'And if he specified the food...' etc. If in the issue under discussion food is specified and its quantity stated, then this is also permissible, because after specifying type, description, and quantity, there is no ignorance. Then specifying the time for delivery of food is not a condition, because the attributes of food are attributes of price. That is, food that is not specific or pointed to, but rather its description is given and it is placed as a liability, it becomes a price, and this is the case for every measurable and weighable item. So this is not a sale that requires a time period. Unlike clothing, which cannot be established as a debt in liability except through salam, but is always a sold item, and in salam specifying the time is a condition. So similarly, if the wet nurse is hired for the price of described clothing, then specifying the time is a condition, as will come later. However, according to Imam Abu Hanifa, specifying the place of delivery of food is a condition when there is carriage involved, contrary to the saying of the two companions, as passed in the chapter of salam in the book of sales. His saying: 'Because its attributes...' etc. The general commentators have taken the feminine pronoun's referent as 'food' with the interpretation of 'hattah' (something). But the author of Nata'ij says: 'In this issue, the intended meaning of food is that which is general to hattah and non-hattah. So in a place of deduction from this general, interpretation with specific is not possible. Therefore the correct view is that the pronoun's referent is 'food', but here it is interpreted as it being the hire.' So the meaning is that this hire's attributes are attributes of prices.
Source pages p. 70

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof and an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning the hire of a wet nurse (ana) where the payment is food. The passage begins by stating the ruling: if the food is specified by type and quantity, the contract is valid. It then explains that specifying the time for delivery of the food is not required because food, when described and made a liability, functions as a price (thaman) in the contract, not as a sold commodity (mabi'). Prices do not require a delivery time. However, specifying the place of delivery is a condition according to Imam Abu Hanifa, because if carriage is involved, ignorance of the place leads to dispute. This is contrary to the view of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn), who do not require specifying the place. The author notes this dispute was already discussed in the Book of Sales (Kitab al-Buyu'). The passage then contrasts this with clothing as hire: if clothing is the payment, it must follow the rules of salam (advance sale), requiring specification of all attributes including delivery time, because clothing cannot be established as a debt except through salam. Next, the passage addresses the husband's rights: the hirer cannot prevent the husband from sexual intercourse, as that is the husband's absolute right. However, the hirer can prevent the husband from entering the hired house because the house is the hirer's usufruct. Furthermore, the husband has the right to rescind the hire if he was unaware of it, to protect his conjugal rights. If the wet nurse becomes pregnant, the employer may rescind the contract fearing harm to the child from her milk, as pregnant women's milk is considered deleterious. If the wet nurse falls ill, she is still obliged to arrange for the child's nourishment; specific tasks like washing clothes and preparing food fall on her according to custom (urf), while the child's food expenses are on the father. Imam Muhammad's mention of oil and perfumes being mandatory is specific to Kufan custom. Finally, if the wet nurse substitutes goat's milk for her own milk, she is not entitled to payment because she changed the required service. The commentary section reinforces these points and clarifies the pronoun reference in the matn, noting that the feminine pronoun 'uwsafiha' refers to the hire (al-ujrah) taken as food, not to the food itself as a commodity. This distinction is crucial for understanding that food in this context is treated as a price.

Key Terms
طعام (ta'am): Food specified by type and quantity as payment for the wet nurse.
شمن (thaman): Price or consideration in a contract; here it describes food when it is a liability rather than a specific item.
صاحبین (sahibayn): Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, the two chief disciples of Abu Hanifa.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if a wet nurse becomes pregnant during the hire, what option does the employer have?
A) Continue paying full hire.
B) Reduce the hire due to potential milk harm.
C) Rescind the contract out of fear for the child.
D) Force her to terminate the pregnancy.

Key Takeaway
Husband's conjugal rights are protected, pregnancy justifies rescission, illness requires alternate food arrangement, and custom fills unspecified duties.

Clothing as Hire Requires Salam Delivery Time
Ruling that clothing as hire requires salam conditions including delivery time

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the additional condition required when clothing is used as payment in a hire contract, and explain why based on salam rules.

Core Idea
Clothing as hire payment must include a delivery time because it is treated as a deferred salam commodity.

In Hanafi fiqh, the payment for hiring a wet nurse can be in various forms: cash, food, or clothing. This lesson examines a specific ruling from the commentary on Al-Hidayah regarding clothing as payment. Unlike food, which is treated as a price, clothing falls under the rules of salam (forward sale) and thus requires a delivery time to avoid uncertainty.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling
Read the passage to determine what is being ruled upon. It states that when a wet nurse is hired in exchange for clothing, all conditions of salam apply.
2
Parse the Conditions Mentioned
Identify the specific conditions required: specification of type (jins), quantity (qadr), and importantly delivery time (mi'ad). The passage emphasizes that delivery time is a condition because clothing becomes obligatory only through a salam sale.
3
Understand the Reason
The passage explains the legal reasoning: clothing cannot be established as a debt (dayn) in one's liability except through a salam contract, which always requires a delivery time to avoid gharar.
Compare with food which can be a price (thaman) and does not require delivery time.
4
Apply to a Scenario
Consider a case where a wet nurse is hired for clothing worth 500 dirhams but no delivery date is mentioned. According to this ruling, the contract is invalid because the payment is not properly specified.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله و فى الكسوة يشترط ..... الخ - اگر انا کو اس کی پوشاک کے عوض اجرت پر لیا تو اس میں جمیع شروط اسلم کا اعتبار ہوگا۔ پس بیان جنس و مقدار کے ساتھ بیان میعاد بھی شرط ہو گا اس واسطے کہ کپڑا آدمی کے ذمہ اسی وقت لازم ہوتا ہے جب وہ مبیع ہو اور وہ بیع اس وقت ہو گا جب اس میں میعاد بیان کر دی جائے جیسے بیع سلم میں ہوتا ہے۔
His saying: 'And in clothing, it is a condition...' etc. - If the wet nurse is hired in exchange for her clothing, then all the conditions of salam are considered. So with the specification of type and quantity, specification of the time period is also a condition, because clothing becomes obligatory in one's liability only when it is the sold item, and that sale occurs only when a time period is specified, as occurs in a salam sale.
Source pages p. 71

Commentary
This is a ruling statement from the commentary on Al-Hidayah. It addresses a specific scenario in hiring a wet nurse: when the payment is clothing (al-kiswah) rather than cash or food. The ruling states that such a payment must fulfill all the conditions of a salam contract (advance sale). This means that the clothing must be fully specified by type (jins), quality (wasf), and quantity (qadr), and additionally the delivery time (mi'ad) must be clearly stated. The reason provided is that clothing, unlike food, cannot be established as a debt (dayn) in someone's liability except through a salam contract. In salam, the delivery time is an essential condition (shart) because the sold item is deferred. Therefore, when clothing is used as payment for the wet nurse's services, it is treated as a deferred commodity, and the time of delivery must be fixed to avoid uncertainty (gharar). This ruling reinforces the principle that different types of payment have different legal requirements in hire contracts.

Key Terms
كسوة (kiswah): Clothing given as payment for the wet nurse's services.
سلم (salam): A forward sale where the price is paid in advance and the commodity is delivered later; here its conditions are applied to clothing as hire.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does clothing as payment for a wet nurse require specifying the delivery time?
A) Because clothing is perishable and must be delivered quickly.
B) Because clothing can only be a debt through salam, which requires a time.
C) Because the wet nurse needs to receive clothing immediately.
D) Because the employer might change his mind about the clothing.

Key Takeaway
When clothing is used as payment in a hire contract, the delivery time must be specified because it is treated as a deferred salam commodity.

Hirer Cannot Prevent Husband's Conjugal Right
Ruling that hirer cannot prevent intercourse, with rescission and location conditions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that the hirer of a wet nurse cannot prevent the husband's conjugal right, explain the proof, and apply the exception for rescission.

Core Idea
The husband's conjugal right is absolute and cannot be extinguished by a hire contract.

This lesson examines the balance between a husband's marital rights and a hirer's contractual rights when a wife works as a wet nurse. The Hanafi school upholds the husband's right to intercourse as inviolable, but places limits based on location.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Ruling
The act is hiring a wet nurse. The ruling: the hirer cannot prevent the husband from intercourse with his wife.
This is a negative prohibition on the hirer.
2
Locate the Proof (Dalil)
The proof is that intercourse is the husband's absolute right (haqq) which the hirer cannot extinguish.
This is a general principle derived from Sharia, not a specific textual citation.
3
Note the Exception: Rescission
If the husband was unaware of the hire, he can rescind the contract to protect his right.
This is a remedy for ignorance (jahl).
4
Note the Limitation: Location
The hirer can prevent intercourse in his house because the usufruct of the house belongs to him.
The husband must use his own home for intercourse.
5
Compare with Imam Malik
Imam Malik holds that the husband needs the hirer's consent for intercourse. The Hanafi position is shared by Shafi'i and Hanbali.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله وليس للمستاجر ان يمنع .... الخ مستاجرانا کے خاوند کو وطی کرنے سے نہیں روک سکتا کیونکہ وہی اس کا حق ہے جس کو مستاجر نہیں مٹا سکتا۔ امام شافعی اور امام احمد بھی اسی کے قائل ہیں (امام مالک کے یہاں شوہر کو رضاء مستاجر کے بغیر ولی کرنے کا اختیار نہیں ہے) چنانچہ شوہر کو اگر بی بی کا نوکری کر لینا معلوم نہ ہو تو وہ اپنے حق کی حفاظت کی خاطر اجارہ فسخ کر سکتا ہے۔ ہاں اپنے گھر میں وطی کرنے سے روک سکتا ہے کیونکہ یہ مستاجر کا حق ہے۔
His saying: 'And the hirer has no right to prevent...' etc. The hirer of the wet nurse cannot prevent the husband from intercourse, because that is his right which the hirer cannot extinguish. Imam al-Shafi'i and Imam Ahmad also hold this view. (Imam Malik: the husband does not have the authority to have intercourse without the hirer's consent.) Accordingly, if the husband is unaware of the wife's employment, he can rescind the hire to protect his right. Yes, he can prevent intercourse in his (the hirer's) house, because that is the hirer's right.
Source pages p. 71

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling with proof concerning the rights of the husband when his wife works as a wet nurse. The key ruling: the hirer (the person who hired the wet nurse) cannot prevent the husband from having sexual intercourse with his wife. The proof given is that intercourse is the husband's exclusive right (haqq), and the hirer has no authority to nullify it. This ruling is supported by Imam al-Shafi'i and Imam Ahmad. The passage notes an exception: according to Imam Malik, the husband does not have the right to intercourse without the hirer's permission. However, the Hanafi position aligns with Shafi'i and Hanbali. The passage further states that if the husband was unaware of the hire contract, he has the option to rescind (faskh) the contract to protect his right of intercourse. However, the hirer can prevent the husband from entering the hired house (the wet nurse's workplace) for intercourse, because the usufruct of the house belongs to the hirer during the contract period. This illustrates the balance between the husband's personal right and the hirer's property right.

Key Terms
فسخ اجارہ (faskh al-ijarah): The husband's right to terminate the hire contract if he was unaware of it, to protect his conjugal right.
مستاجر (musta'jir): The hirer who employs the wet nurse; here has rights to the house but not over the husband's intercourse.
حق (haqq): The husband's absolute right to intercourse, which cannot be extinguished by the hirer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, can the hirer of a wet nurse prevent the husband from having intercourse?
A) Yes, because the hirer pays for her services.
B) No, because intercourse is the husband's absolute right.
C) Yes, but only if the husband agreed in the contract.
D) No, but the husband must notify the hirer in advance.

Key Takeaway
The hirer cannot prevent the husband's conjugal right, but the location is subject to the hirer's property rights, and the husband may rescind if unaware.

Prohibition of Qafiz al-Tahhan: Fee as Part of the Product is Void
Ruling that contracts where fee is part of the work product are fasid, with proof from hadith

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the ruling of qafiz al-tahhan and apply the principle of gharar to identify void hire contracts where the fee is part of the product.

Core Idea
You cannot pay a worker with a share of his own product — the contract is void and market wage is due.

This lesson examines a fundamental principle in Hanafi contract law: the prohibition of paying a hired worker with a portion of the product he produces or carries. Known as qafiz al-tahhan (the miller's measure), this ruling is based on a Prophetic prohibition and applies to many similar transactions. Understanding this principle helps you identify hidden forms of gharar in modern hire agreements.

Guided Path
1
Identify the prohibited transaction
Qafiz al-tahhan is a contract where the fee is a measure (qafiz) of the product that the worker himself produces, such as flour from grinding wheat. The Prophet explicitly prohibited this.
The term 'qafiz' is a unit of measure.
2
Analyze the examples given
The text gives three examples: (1) hiring a weaver to weave yarn for half the cloth, (2) hiring a donkey to carry grain for a qafiz of that grain, (3) the original case of hiring an ox to grind wheat for a qafiz of flour. All are ruled void.
In each case, the fee does not exist at the time of contract.
3
Trace the proof from hadith
The Prophet's prohibition is the direct evidence. The illa (legal cause) is that the hirer cannot deliver the fee at contract time because it comes into existence only through the worker's labor, leading to uncertainty (gharar) and potential dispute.
The hadith is narrated but its exact chain is not given; its meaning is relied upon.
4
Apply the principle to new cases
Using qiyas, any contract where the fee is a part of the worker's output is fasid. The remedy is ujr al-mithl (market wage) if work has been performed.
This is a great principle (asl kabir) especially relevant in contexts like artisan work or transportation.

قفیز الطحان کی بحث قال ومن دفع الى حائك غزلا لينسجه بالنصف فله اجر مثله وكذا اذا استاجر حمارا يحمل عليه طعاما بقفيز منه فالاجارة فاسدة لانه جعل الاجر بعض ما يخرج من عمله فيصير فى معنى قفيز الطحان وقد نهى النبي عليه السلام عنه وهو ان يستاجر ثورا ليطحن له حنطة بقفيز من دقيقه وهذا اصل كبير يعرف به فساد كبير من الاجارات لا سيما في ديارنا والمعنى فيه ان المستاجر عاجز عن تسليم الاجر وهو بعض المنسوج او المحمول او حصوله بفعل الاجير فلا يعد هو قادرا بقدرة غيره توضیح اللغة .. مالک جولا با، غزل کا تا ہوا، لینسجه (ن، ض) نسبحاً کپڑا بنا۔ طحان چکی پینے والا ،ٹور بیل لیطحن (ف) طحناً پینا۔ دقیق آتا۔ منسوج بنا ہوا۔ ترجمہ کسی نے جولا ہے کو سوت دیا تا کہ اس کو آدھے پر بن دے تو جولا ہے کے لئے اجر مثل ہوگا ۔ اسی طرح اگر گدھا اجارہ پر لیا کہ اس پر طعام لا دے اسی طعام میں سے ایک قفیز کے عوض تو اجارہ فاسد ہے کیونکہ اس نے اجرت اس چیز کا ایک جز ٹھہرایا ہے جو اس کے عمل سے حاصل ہوگی تو یہ قضیز الملحان کے معنی میں ہو گیا ۔ حالانکہ نبی نے اس سے منع فرمایا ہے۔ اور وہ یہ ہے کہ اجارہ پر لے ایک بیل تا کہ اس کے لئے گیہوں پیسے اس کے آٹے کے ایک قفیز کے عوض ۔ اور یہ اصل عظیم ہے۔ جس سے بہت سے اجارات کا فاسد ہونا معلوم ہو جاتا ہے خصوصا ہمارے دیار میں ، اور اس کے اندر بھید یہ ہے کہ مستاجر عقد اجارہ کے وقت اجرت سپرد کرنے سے عاجز ہے اور وہ بنے ہوئے کپڑے کا یا جولا دلایا ہے اس کا ایک حصہ ہے جس کا حصول اجیر کے فعل سے ہوگا تو مستاجر کو دوسرے کی قدرت سے قادر شمار نہیں کیا جائے گا۔ تشریح قوله و من دفع الخ- زید نے ایک جولا ہے کو کپڑا اپننے کے لئے سوت دیا۔ اور بنائی میں آدھا کپڑا جو بن کر تیار ہوا اس کو اجرت قرار دیا تو یہ اجارہ فاسد ہے۔ لہذا جولا ہے کو اس کا اجر مثل ملے گا کہ کہ اجارہ فاسدہ کا یہی حکم ہے۔ اسی طرح اگر ایک گدھا غلہ کی مخصوص مقدار اٹھانے کے لئے اجرت پر لیا اور اسی غلہ سے ایک تغیز مزدوری طے ہوئی تو یہ اجارہ بھی فاسد ہے۔ احناف، امام مالک،
Discussion of Qafiz al-Tahhan. He said: And whoever gives yarn to a weaver to weave it for half, then he is entitled to the equivalent wage. Likewise, if he hires a donkey to carry food in exchange for a qafiz of that food, then the hire is void because he made the fee a part of what comes out of his work, so it falls into the meaning of Qafiz al-Tahhan. And the Prophet (peace be upon him) prohibited it, which is that one hires an ox to grind wheat in exchange for a qafiz of its flour. And this is a great principle by which the voidness of many hires is known, especially in our lands. And the meaning therein is that the hirer is incapable of delivering the fee at the time of contract, as it is part of the woven cloth or the carried load, and its acquisition occurs through the act of the hired worker, so the hirer is not considered capable by the capability of another. Language explanation: ... Translation: Someone gave yarn to a weaver to weave it for half, so the weaver is entitled to the equivalent wage. Similarly, if he hires a donkey to carry food in exchange for a qafiz of that food, then the hire is void because he made the fee a part of what comes out of his work, so it becomes in the meaning of Qafiz al-Tahhan, although the Prophet prohibited it. And that is to hire an ox to grind wheat in exchange for a qafiz of its flour. And this is a great principle by which the voidness of many hires is known, especially in our lands. And the secret in it is that the hirer at the time of the contract is incapable of delivering the fee, and it is part of the woven cloth or the carried load, and its acquisition is through the act of the hired worker, so the hirer is not considered capable by the capability of another. Commentary on his saying 'and whoever gives...': Zaid gave yarn to a weaver to weave cloth for himself, and made half the woven cloth as the fee, so this hire is void. Therefore, the weaver gets his market wage (ujr al-mithl), as is the ruling for a void hire. Similarly, if a donkey is hired to carry a specific amount of grain and the wage is set as a qafiz of that same grain, then this hire is also void. The Hanafis, Imam Malik...
Source pages p. 71

Commentary
This passage presents a fundamental ruling and proof concerning prohibited hire contracts known as 'qafiz al-tahhan' (the miller's measure). The ruling: any contract where the fee (ujr) is a portion of the product that the hired worker produces or carries is void (fasid). The examples given: (1) giving yarn to a weaver to weave with the agreement that he receives half the woven cloth; (2) hiring a donkey to carry grain with the payment being a qafiz (a measure) of that grain; (3) the classic case of hiring an ox to grind wheat with the payment being a qafiz of the flour. The proof is a hadith: the Prophet (peace be upon him) prohibited this type of transaction. The legal reasoning ('illa): the hirer is incapable of delivering the fee at the time of contract because the fee does not yet exist; it comes into existence only through the worker's labor. The hirer cannot be considered capable of delivery by relying on another's action. Therefore, such contracts are void due to uncertainty (gharar) and the risk of dispute (niza'). The consequence: the worker is entitled to his market wage (ujr al-mithl), not the agreed portion, because the contract is void. This principle is described as a great principle (asl kabir) that reveals the voidness of many similar hire contracts, especially in contexts where fee is part of the product. The commentary reiterates these points and confirms that the Hanafi madhhab, along with Imam Malik (and implicitly others), hold this ruling.

Key Terms
قفیز الطحان (qafiz al-tahhan): A prohibited contract where the payment is a measure (qafiz) of the product, such as flour from grinding.
اجر مثل (ujr al-mithl): The market-equivalent wage that must be paid in a void hire contract.
اجارہ فاسدہ (ijarah fasidah): A void hire contract that still entails ujr al-mithl if work is done.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on hiring a weaver with the agreement that he receives half the woven cloth as his fee?
A) Valid, because the weaver consented.
B) Void, because the fee is part of the product and uncertain.
C) Valid, but must add a delivery time.
D) Void, but the weaver gets nothing.

Key Takeaway
Hiring someone for a share of the product is void; the worker receives market wage.

The Conditions of Hiring for Clothing: An Application of Salam Rules
States conditions for hiring for clothing

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three conditions required for a valid hire contract where the wage is clothing, and explain why they are derived from salam.

Core Idea
Hiring for clothing is treated as a salam sale — type, quantity, and time must all be specified.

This passage from the commentary addresses a specific type of ijara where the wage takes the form of clothing. The author explains that such a contract is valid only if it meets the conditions of salam (forward sale). This analogy may seem surprising, but it follows from the nature of the obligation: clothing becomes a debt on the hirer, and debts in sale require precise specification. Let's examine the exact conditions required.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contract type
Recognize that hiring for clothing is a form of ijara where the wage is a specific commodity (clothing).
This is not a standard rental; the wage is a physical item.
2
Apply the salam analogy
Understand why the commentator likens this to salam — because the clothing becomes a debt (dayn) on the hirer, and salam is the standard contract for deferred delivery of commodities.
The key connection: a debt requires specification to avoid gharar.
3
List the required conditions
Identify the three conditions: type (jins), quantity (miqdar), and time (ajal/mi'ad). All three must be specified for the contract to be valid.
Failure to specify any condition renders the contract fasid (invalid).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله و فى الكسوة يشترط ..... الخ - اگر انا کو اس کی پوشاک کے عوض اجرت پر لیا تو اس میں جمیع شروط اسلم کا اعتبار ہوگا۔ پس بیان جنس و مقدار کے ساتھ بیان میعاد بھی شرط ہو گا اس واسطے کہ کپڑا آدمی کے ذمہ اسی وقت لازم ہوتا ہے جب وہ مبیع ہو اور وہ بیع اس وقت ہو گا جب اس میں میعاد بیان کر دی جائے جیسے بیع سلم میں ہوتا ہے۔
His statement: 'And regarding clothing, it is required...' - if a person hires [someone] in exchange for his clothing, then all the conditions of salam are considered. So specifying the type, quantity, and also specifying the time are conditions, because clothing becomes obligatory on a person's liability only when it is sold, and that sale occurs only when the time is specified, as is the case in salam sale.
Source pages p. 71

Commentary
This passage explains the ruling on hiring someone for clothing as wages. The commentator clarifies that hiring for clothing is treated like a salam (forward sale) contract. Therefore, all conditions of salam apply: the type (jins), quantity (miqdar), and time (mi'ad) must be specified. This is because the clothing becomes a debt on the hirer's liability only when it is sold (i.e., the contract is effectively a sale of clothing to the worker). Without specifying the time, the contract is invalid. This is based on qiyas to salam.

Key Terms
سلم (salam): A forward sale where the price is paid in advance and the goods are delivered later.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The hirer's consent
B) The worker's skill level
C) Specifying the time of delivery
D) The cloth's color

Key Takeaway
Hiring for clothing requires the same conditions as salam: type, quantity, and time must be specified.

Hirer Cannot Prevent Husband's Right to Intercourse
States that hirer cannot prevent husband's right to intercourse

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the hirer's power over marital relations and explain the thamarah al-khilaf between Hanafi and Maliki schools.

Core Idea
The hirer cannot invalidate the husband's personal right to intercourse.

When a married woman is hired, the hirer gains certain rights over her labor but not over her marital obligations. This lesson examines a conflict between the hire contract and conjugal rights. You will learn how the Hanafi school balances these interests and where other schools differ.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling: the hirer cannot prevent the husband from intercourse. This is the Hanafi view.
Also held by Shafi'i and Ahmad.
2
Identify the opposing school
Imam Malik holds that the husband requires the hirer's consent for intercourse.
The passage does not detail Maliki proof.
3
Analyze the Hanafi proof
The husband's right to intercourse is a personal right (haqq nafsi) that the hirer cannot invalidate through the hire contract.
This is a rationale, not a textual proof.
4
Note the exception
The hirer can prevent intercourse in his own house, because that is his right over his property.
Balances both rights.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
In Hanafi school, husband retains full conjugal rights; in Maliki, the hire restricts those rights.
The husband may rescind the hire if unaware, to protect his right.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله وليس للمستاجر ان يمنع .... الخ مستاجرانا کے خاوند کو وطی کرنے سے نہیں روک سکتا کیونکہ وہی اس کا حق ہے جس کو مستاجر نہیں مٹا سکتا۔ امام شافعی اور امام احمد بھی اسی کے قائل ہیں (امام مالک کے یہاں شوہر کو رضاء مستاجر کے بغیر ولی کرنے کا اختیار نہیں ہے) چنانچہ شوہر کو اگر بی بی کا نوکری کر لینا معلوم نہ ہو تو وہ اپنے حق کی حفاظت کی خاطر اجارہ فسخ کر سکتا ہے۔ ہاں اپنے گھر میں وطی کرنے سے روک سکتا ہے کیونکہ یہ مستاجر کا حق ہے۔
His statement: 'And the hirer cannot prevent...' - The hirer cannot prevent the husband of the hired woman from having intercourse, because that is his right which the hirer cannot invalidate. Imam al-Shafi'i and Imam Ahmad also hold this view. (In Imam Malik's view, the husband does not have the right to have intercourse without the hirer's consent.) Thus, if the husband was unaware that his wife had taken employment, he can rescind the hire to protect his right. However, he can prevent intercourse in the hirer's house, because that is the hirer's right.
Source pages p. 71

Commentary
This passage discusses the interaction between a hire contract and the marital rights of a husband. If a married woman is hired as a worker, the hirer cannot prevent her husband from having sexual intercourse with her, because the husband's right to intercourse is a personal right that the hirer cannot eliminate. This is the position of the Hanafi school, and also of Imam al-Shafi'i and Imam Ahmad. Imam Malik, however, holds that the husband does not have the right to intercourse without the hirer's consent. The commentator adds a practical point: if the husband was unaware that his wife had taken employment, he can rescind the hire to protect his right. However, he cannot insist on intercourse within the hirer's premises, because the hirer has the right to control his own house.

Key Terms
مستأجر (musta'jir): Hirer; the person who hires the woman (employer).
وطء (wat'): Sexual intercourse.
فسخ (faskh): Rescission; annulment of a contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what can the hirer of a married woman do?
A) Prevent the husband from intercourse entirely
B) Prevent intercourse only in the hirer's house
C) Prevent intercourse outside the hirer's house
D) Not interfere with the husband's right at all

Key Takeaway
The hirer cannot invalidate the husband's personal right to intercourse, but may restrict it on his own premises.

Qafiz al-Tahhan: Prohibition of Hiring with a Share of Output
Defines and proves prohibition of qafiz al-tahhan

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on qafiz al-tahhan, identify the underlying principle, and explain why the contract is fasid with reference to the hadith and the inability to deliver the wage.

Core Idea
Hiring a worker for a share of the output is fasid because the wage is uncertain and the hirer cannot deliver it at contract time.

The prohibition of qafiz al-tahhan is a key principle in Hanafi ijara law. This lesson examines the ruling and its evidence, exploring the classic example of hiring an ox to mill wheat in exchange for flour. You will learn why such contracts are invalid and how to identify them.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is qafiz al-tahhan? The classic example is hiring an ox to grind wheat in exchange for a qafiz of the flour. The Hanafi ruling is that this hire is invalid (fasid).
2
Locate the dalil
The primary evidence is the hadith: 'He prohibited the stud fee of the stallion and qafiz al-tahhan.' This is narrated in Sunan al-Dar Qutni, al-Bayhaqi, etc.
The hadith is ahad, zanni al-thubut.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The explicit prohibition (nahy) indicates the invalidity of such contracts. The wage depends on the worker's output, so the hirer cannot deliver it at the time of the contract, leading to gharar (uncertainty).
This is supported by the principle that the hirer's ability is not established by another's power.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some early scholars and Imam Ahmad permit such contracts, seeing no harm. Some later Hanafis also gave fatwa of permissibility.
The text upholds the prohibition as the sounder view (al-mukhtar).
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The prohibition is from Zahir al-Riwayah and the majority of Hanafis. The hadith is defended as authentic despite criticism from Ibn Taymiyyah and others.
Induction: many common hiring practices in the commentator's region are fasid under this principle.

تشریح قوله و من دفع الخ- زید نے ایک جولا ہے کو کپڑا اپننے کے لئے سوت دیا۔ اور بنائی میں آدھا کپڑا جو بن کر تیار ہوا اس کو اجرت قرار دیا تو یہ اجارہ فاسد ہے۔ لہذا جولا ہے کو اس کا اجر مثل ملے گا کہ کہ اجارہ فاسدہ کا یہی حکم ہے۔ اسی طرح اگر ایک گدھا غلہ کی مخصوص مقدار اٹھانے کے لئے اجرت پر لیا اور اسی غلہ سے ایک تغیز مزدوری طے ہوئی تو یہ اجارہ بھی فاسد ہے۔ احناف، امام مالک، امام شافعی لیث بن سعد حسن ابو ثور اسی کے قائل ہیں۔ ابن المنذ راور ابن عقیل نے بھی اسی کو اختیار کیا ہے۔ اور بقول ابن حزم ، ابراہیم نخعی نے اس کو مکروہ کہا ہے۔ اس کے برخلاف ابن سیرین ، عطاء، یعلی بن حکیم، زہری ، قتادہ، اسحاق ، ایوب سختیانی، ابن ابی لیلی اور امام احمد کے نزدیک اس میں کوئی مضائقہ نہیں ۔ مبسوط میں ہے کہ شمس الائمہ حلوانی نے اپنے استاد قاضی ابوعلی نسفی سے نقل کیا ہے کہ وہ شہر نسف میں اس کے جواز کا فتوی دیتے تھے۔ مشائخ بلخ ( نصر بن بھی محمد بن سلمہ وغیرہ) کا فتویٰ بھی جواز پر ہے۔ پھر کہا ہے کہ میرے نزدیک اصبح وہی ہے۔ جو کتاب میں مذکور ہے۔ قوله لانه جعل الاجر .... الخ - ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ صورت مذکور میں اجرت وہی ہے جو اجیر سے عمل سے پیدا ہوگی تو یہ قفیز الطحان کے معنی میں ہوئی۔ جس کی بابت سنن دار قطنی و بیہقی اور مسند ابو یعلی موصلی میں حضرت ابوسعید خدری سے مرفوعاً مروی ہے
نهى عن عسب الفحل و عن قفيز الطحان
صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ قفیز الطحان کی تغییر یہ ہے کہ ایک بیل اجارہ پر لے تاکہ چکی میں جوت کر اس کے ذریعہ سے گیہوں وغیرہ پیسے اور جو آٹا حاصل ہو اس میں سے ایک قفیز اجرت طے ہو۔
تنبیہ حافظ بن تیمیہ نے حدیث نہی عن قفیز الطحان کو باطل قرار دیا ہے۔ شیخ موفق المغنی میں کہتے ہیں
هذا الحديث لا نعرفه ولا يثبت عندنا صحته
جواب یہ ہے کہ اول تو محدث جلیل علامہ ابن عقیلی، دار قطنی، بہتی، امام طحاوی اور شیخ عبدالحق اس حدیث سے بخوبی واقف ہیں وكفى بهم قدورة والعارف حجة على من لم يعرف
دوسرے یہ کہ ابن تیمیہ کے جدامجد نے اس حدیث کی تخریج منتقی الاخبار میں کی ہے اور خود موفق حنبلی نے المغنی میں علامہ ابن عقیل کی بابت لکھا ہے کہ وہ بھی اس حدیث کو صحیح اور قابل استدلال سمجھتے تھے اور وہ باوجود حنبلی ہونے کے اس مسئلہ میں حنفیہ، شافعیہ اور مالکیہ کے ساتھ تھے۔ تو کیا باطل و موضوع احادیث ایسی ہی ہوتی ہیں؟
سوال شیخ ذہبی نے میزان میں حدیث مذکور کے راوی ہشام ابوکلیب کے بارے میں لا یعرف کہا ہے۔
جواب اول تو حافظ ابن حجر نے لسان میں کہا ہے کہ ہشام کو ابن حبان نے ثقات میں ذکر کیا ہے نیل الاوطار میں شیخ مغلطائی کا قول منقول ہے کہ ہشام ثقہ راوی ہے۔ نیز دار قطنی نے بطریق ہشام تخریج حدیث کے بعد سکوت کیا ہے۔ دوسرے یہ کہ ہشام اس حدیث کی روایت میں منفرد بھی نہیں ہے بلکہ عطاء بن السائب نے اس کی متابعت کی ہے چنانچہ امام طحاوی کی مشکل الآثار میں عطاء کی روایت جید سند کے ساتھ موجود ہے۔ سوال... ابن القطان کا بیان ہے کہ میں نے سنن دار قطنی میں حدیث کی روایات کو تبع کے بعد یونہی پایا ہے۔
نهى عن عسب الفحل و قفيز الطحان پس حدیث کا رفع ثابت نہیں ہوتا ۔
جواب امام طحاوی نے اس حدیث کو دو طریق سے مسند و مرفوع روایت کیا ہے۔ چنانچہ طریق عطاء بن السائب عن ابن ابی نعم میں
Discussion of Qafiz al-Tahhan. He said: Whoever gives wool to a weaver to weave for half [the product], then he gets the equivalent wage. Similarly, if one hires a donkey to carry food in exchange for a qafiz of that food, the hire is invalid because he made the wage a part of what comes out of his work, so it becomes like qafiz al-tahhan, and the Prophet (peace be upon him) prohibited it. It is to hire an ox to grind wheat in exchange for a qafiz of its flour. This is a great principle by which many hires are known to be invalid, especially in our lands. The meaning is that the hirer is unable to deliver the wage at the time of the contract, as it is part of the woven or carried item, or its attainment depends on the worker's action, so he is not considered capable by another's ability. ... Translation: Someone gave a weaver thread to weave for half, so the weaver gets the equivalent wage. Similarly, if a donkey is hired to carry food for a qafiz of that food, the hire is invalid. ... Explanation: Zaid gave a weaver thread to weave cloth, making half the cloth the wage. This hire is invalid. The weaver gets the equivalent wage. The Hanafis, Imam Malik, Imam Shafi'i, Layth, Hasan, Abu Thawr hold this. Ibn al-Mundhir and Ibn Aqil also chose it. Ibrahim al-Nakha'i said it was makruh. In contrast, Ibn Sirin, Ata, etc. and Imam Ahmad see no harm. In al-Mabsut, Shams al-A'imma al-Halwani narrated from al-Qadi Abu Ali al-Nasafi that he gave fatwa of permissibility in Nasaf. The mashayikh of Balkh also gave fatwa of permissibility. Then it was said that according to me, the soundest is what is in the book. ... Our evidence is that in the mentioned case, the wage is what comes from the worker's action, so it falls under qafiz al-tahhan. Regarding this, it is narrated marfu'an from Abu Sa'id al-Khudri in Sunan al-Dar Qutni, al-Bayhaqi, and Musnad Abi Ya'la al-Mawsili: 'He prohibited the stud fee of the stallion and qafiz al-tahhan.' ... The author of al-Hidayah says the explanation of qafiz al-tahhan is to hire an ox to grind wheat in exchange for a qafiz of the resulting flour. ... Warning: Ibn Taymiyyah declared the hadith 'prohibition of qafiz al-tahhan' as false. ... Response: First, prominent muhaddithun like Ibn Aqil, Dar Qutni, etc. are well aware of this hadith. Second, Ibn Taymiyyah's own grandfather included it in al-Muntaqa. And Imam Ahmad's follower Ibn Aqil considered it authentic. ... Objection: Al-Dhahabi in al-Mizan said about the narrator Hisham Abu Kalib: 'not known.' Response: Ibn Hajar in al-Lisan said Ibn Hibban listed him in al-Thiqat. Also Dar Qutni remained silent after narrating through him. Also, Hisham is not alone; Ata ibn al-Sa'ib followed him. ... Another objection: Ibn al-Qattan said he found the hadith in Sunan al-Dar Qutni without a complete chain. Response: Imam al-Tahawi narrated the hadith through two chains as musnad and marfu', such as through Ata ibn al-Sa'ib from Ibn Abi Na'm.
Source pages p. 71

Commentary
This passage is a detailed discussion of the prohibition known as 'qafiz al-tahhan' (the miller's qafiz). The commentator begins by presenting the legal ruling from the matn: if a person gives wool to a weaver to weave for half the product, or hires a donkey to carry food in exchange for a qafiz of that food, the hire contract is invalid (fasid). The reason is that the wage is a part of the output of the worker's own effort, which makes the contract resemble qafiz al-tahhan, which the Prophet (peace be upon him) prohibited. The classic example is hiring an ox to grind wheat in exchange for a qafiz of the resulting flour. This serves as a foundational principle (asl kabir) to identify the invalidity of many hire contracts, especially common in the commentator's region. The underlying meaning is that the hirer is unable to deliver the wage at the time of the contract because it is contingent on the worker's action; the hirer's ability depends on another's power, which is not sufficient. The passage then lists the scholars who hold the prohibition (Hanafis, Malik, Shafi'i, etc.) and those who permit it (including Imam Ahmad and several early scholars). There is also a mention that some later Hanafi authorities, like the mashayakh of Balkh, gave fatwa of permissibility, but the text upholds the prohibition as stated in the book. The hadith evidence is cited: 'He prohibited the stud fee of the stallion and qafiz al-tahhan.' The commentator then engages in a defense of the hadith against criticism by Ibn Taymiyyah and others, arguing for its authenticity through chains, narrators, and the acceptance of prominent muhaddithun. The discussion includes refutations of objections regarding the narrator Hisham Abu Kalib and the chain's completeness, citing al-Tahawi's multiple chains.

Key Terms
قفیز الطحان (qafiz al-tahhan): A prohibited form of hire where the wage is a share of the output of the worker's own labor, such as hiring an ox to grind wheat in exchange for a qafiz of the flour.
اجر مثل (ajr mithl): The equivalent wage, i.e., the market rate for similar work, paid when a contract is invalid but work has been done.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi ruling on hiring a weaver to weave cloth in exchange for half the cloth?
A) Valid (sahih)
B) Invalid (fasid) with equivalent wage
C) Invalid (batil) with no wage
D) Permissible (ja'iz)

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school prohibits hiring where the wage is a share of the output, considering it fasid due to uncertainty (gharar) and the hirer's inability to deliver the wage.

Ijarah — Hire and Lease
intermediate
12 min
The Great Principle: Prohibition of Qafiz al-Tahan and Invalid Ijarah
Explaining hadith prohibition and deriving the great principle

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi principle that a wage consisting of part of the worker's product renders an ijarah contract fasid, and apply it to new examples.

Core Idea
An ijarah contract is invalid if the wage is part of the very thing the worker produces.

The Prophet (ﷺ) prohibited the miller's measure (qafiz al-tahan) — taking a portion of ground grain as payment. This seemingly specific prohibition yields a great principle in Hanafi fiqh: any ijarah where the wage is part of the worker's own product is invalid (fasid). In this lesson, we examine the hadith, the extracted principle, and several classic examples, building the skill to identify this defect in hire contracts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hadith Prohibition
Locate the hadith and its key terms: 'qafiz al-tahan', 'kasb al-hajjam', 'asb al-tays'. Note that the prohibition is explicit and is narrated via multiple chains.
The hadith is ahad but accepted in the school.
2
Extract the Great Principle
From the prohibition of qafiz al-tahan, the Hanafi jurists deduce a general rule: any ijarah where the wage is part of the item produced by the worker's labor is fasid. This is because the wage does not exist at the time of contract and will only come into existence through the worker's own act.
The wage is not deliverable at contract formation.
3
Apply to Classic Examples
Work through the three examples given: hiring to press oil with part of the oil, giving land for planting in exchange for joint ownership, hiring to bake bread with a portion of the bread. Confirm that each falls under the principle.
In all examples, the wage is part of the ma'qud 'alayh (the subject matter).
4
Distinguish Valid from Invalid
Contrast with a valid ijarah: e.g., hiring a miller to grind grain for a fixed amount of gold. Here the wage is separate and known, not part of the product. Understand that the prohibition is specific to the wage being an uncertain, future part of the worker's output.
If the wage is a separate, existing item, the contract is valid.
5
Recall the Usul Basis
The Hanafi usul principle 'al-nahy yufidu al-fasad' makes the contract fasid. Understand that the prohibition indicates invalidity, not mere dislike.
This is a key distinction from other schools that may treat it as makruh.

" اور طریق سفیان ثوری عن ہشام ابی کلیب عن ابن ابی انعم میں ہے نهی رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم عن عسب الفحل وعن قفيز الطحان نیز محدث شہیر عبدالحق نے بھی الاحکام میں دار قطنی کے طریق سے یونہی ذکر کیا ہے۔

۲) کسی نے اپنی زمین اس لئے دی تا کہ اس میں درخت لگائے اور زمین اور درخت ان دونوں میں مشترک ہوں ۔
