قوله والمعنى فيه .... الخ یعنی نہی عن قفیز الطحان کا بھید یہ ہے کہ مستاجر بوقت عقد اجارہ تسلیم اجرت سے عاجز ہے۔ کیونکہ اجرت تو مسئلہ حائک میں بنے ہوئے کپڑے کا اور مسئلہ استیجار حمار میں جو لا دلایا جائے اس کا ایک حصہ ہے اور یہ اجرت اجیر کے فعل سے حاصل ہوگی تو اجیر کے قادر ہونے سے مستاجر قادر نہ ہوگا۔
حمال کو اجارہ پر لیا نصف غلہ نصف غلے کے عوض اٹھا کر پہنچانے پر اجرت واجب نہ ہوگی
وهذا بخلاف ما اذا استاجره ليحمل نصف طعامه بالنصف الآخر حيث لا يجب له الاجر لان المستاجر ملك الاجر في الحال بالتعجيل فصار مشتركا بينهما ومن استاجر رجلا لحمل طعام مشترك بينهما لا يجب الاجر لان ما من جزء يحمله الا وهو عامل لنفسه فيه فلا يتحقق تسليم المعقود عليه ولا يجاوز بالاجر قفيزا لانه لما فسدت الاجارة فالواجب الاقل مما سمى ومن اجر المثل لانه رضى بحط الزيادة وهذا بخلاف ما اذا اشتركا في الاحتطاب حيث يجب الاجر بالغا ما بلغ عند محمد لان المسمى هناک غیر معلوم فلم يصح الحط.
ترجمہ اور یہ اس کے برخلاف ہے۔ جب جمال کو اجارہ پر لیا تا کہ اس اناج کا آدھا بعوض باقی آدھے کے اٹھا کر پہنچائے کہ اس کے لئے اجرت واجب نہ ہوگی ۔ کیونکہ مستاجر نے اس کو فی الحال پیشگی اجرت کا مالک کر دیا تو طعام ان دونوں میں مشترک ہو گیا ۔ اور جو شخص اپنے شریک کو مشترک طعام اٹھانے کے لئے اجارہ پر لے تو اجرت واجب نہیں ہوتی کیونکہ کوئی جز نہیں جس کو وہ اٹھائے مگر یہ کہ وہ اس میں اپنی ذات کے لئے بھی عامل ہے۔ پس معقود علیہ کی تسلیم متحقق نہ ہوگی ۔ اور اجرت ایک قفیز سے زیادہ نہیں دی جائے گی ۔ اس لئے کہ جب اجارہ فاسد ہوا تو اجر ش سے جو کم ہو وہ واجب ہوگا ۔ کیونکہ زیادتی گھٹانے پر وہ خود ہی راضی ہو گیا ہے۔ اور یہ اس کے برخلاف ہے۔ جب دو آدمیوں نے لکڑیاں چننے میں شرکت کی کہ اجرت واجب ہو گی ۔ جہاں تک بھی پہنچے امام محمد کے نزدیک کیونکہ یہاں اجر سمی غیر معلوم ہے تو گھٹا نا صحیح نہ ہوا۔
اشرف البدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد ۱۲
تشریح قوله وهذا بخلاف ما اذا استاجره .. الخ - سابق میں جو یہ مسئلہ مذکور ہوا کہ اگر ایک گدھا اس لئے اجارہ پر لیا تا کہ اس پر اناج لا دے جس کی اجرت اسی اناج میں سے ایک قفیز ہوگی تو اجارہ فاسد ہے۔ یہ حکم اس صورت کے خلاف ہے جب کسی جمال کو اس طرح اجارہ پر لیا کہ اس اناج کا آدھا باقی آدھے کے عوض اٹھا کر پہنچا دے کہ اس صورت میں کچھ اجرت واجب نہ ہوگی۔ نہ اجر سمی اور نہ اجر مثل ۔ اس لئے کہ یہاں مستاجر نے اجیر کو فی الحال پیشگی اجرت کا مالک کر دیا۔
لان تسليم الاجرة بحكم التعجيل يوجب الملك في الاجرة
پس وہ طعام ان دونوں میں مشترک ہو گیا اور جو شخص اپنے شریک کو مشترک طعام اٹھانے کے لئے اجارہ پر لے تو کوئی اجرت واجب نہیں ہوتی۔ کیونکہ اناج کا جو جز بھی وہ لاد کر لائے اس میں اپنی ذات کے لئے بھی عامل ہوگا۔ پس معقود علیہ کی تسلیم متفق نہ ہوگی ۔ کیونکہ اس نے اپنی ذاتی منفعت کو سپر دنہیں کیا۔ وفیہ خلاف الشافعی۔
علامہ زیلعی نے شرح کنز میں یہ مسئلہ مع دلیل ذکر کرنے کے بعد کہا ہے کہ اس میں دو اشکال ہیں۔
اول یہ کہ اجارہ فاسد ہے اور حال یہ ہے کہ ہمارے یہاں اجارہ صحیحہ میں بھی نفس عقد کے ذریعہ سے اجرت کا مالک نہیں ہوتا خواہ وہ عین ہو یا دین ہو۔ تو پھر یہاں بلا تسلیم و بلاشرط تعجیل کیسے مالک ہو گیا ؟
دوم یه که لان المستاجر ملک الاجیر فی الحال اور لا يجب له الاجر دونوں قولوں میں منافات ہے اس لئے کہ اجیر بھی اس کا مالک ہوگا ۔ وہ بطریق اجرت ہی ہوگا۔ اور جب اس کے لئے اجرت واجب ہی نہ ہوئی تو پھر کیسے اور کس سبب سے مالک ہوگا ؟
پہلے اشکال کا جواب یہ ہے کہ مسئلہ کی وضع اس صورت میں ہے جب مستاجر نے کل طعام اجیر کو سپرد کر دیا ہو جیسا کہ صاحب نہایہ و صاحب معراج الدرایہ وغیرہ نے نفس مسئلہ کی تحریر میں و رفع الیہ کلہ ولا اجملہ کی تصریح کی ہے۔
اور دوسرے اشکال کا جواب ..... یہ ہے کہ بین القولین منافات غیر مسلم ہے اس لئے کہ ملک الاجیر فی الحال کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ اجیر کی ملک ابتداء بموجب عقد ہے اور تسلیم اجرت بطریق تقبیل اور لا یجب لہ الاجر کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ وہ قبل از عمل بطلان عقد کی وجہ سے مستحق اجر نہیں ہے بعد ازاں کہ وہ بذریعہ تسلیم مالک ہو گیا بایں سبب کے معقود علیہ کے ایفاء سے پہلے طعام میں شریک ہو چکا ولا تنافی بين هذين المعنيين
قوله ولا يجاوز بالاجر .... الخ " يقول سابق و كذا اذا استاجر حماراً ليحمل طعاماً بقفيز منہ سے وابستہ ہے۔ مطلب یہ ہے کہ مسئلہ استیجار حمار میں اجرت ایک قفیز سے زیادہ نہیں دی جائے گی۔ یعنی جو اجر مثل واجب ہو اگر وہ ایک قفیز سے کم ہو یا ایک قفیز ہو تو یہی دیا جائے گا اور اگر ایک قفیز سے زیادہ ہو تو زائد مقدار نہیں دی جائے گی۔ اس لئے کہ جب اجارہ فاسد ہوا تو بیان کردہ اجرت اور اجر مثل میں سے جو کم ہو وہ واجب ہوتا ہے۔ کیونکہ کرایہ پر دینے والا ایک قفیز سے زیادتی گھٹانے پر خود ہی راضی ہو گیا ہے۔ حيث رضی با لقفیز
Book of Ijarah. Ashraf al-Hidayah Urdu commentary on Hidayah vol 12. From the Prophet (ﷺ) that he prohibited the stud fee of the goat, the earnings of the cupper, and the miller's measure. And via the way of Sufyan al-Thawri from Hisham Abi Kulayb from Ibn Abi An'am: the Messenger of Allah (ﷺ) prohibited the stud fee of the stallion and the miller's measure. Also the famous muhaddith Abd al-Haqq mentioned the same in al-Ahkam via al-Daraqutni's chain. His statement: 'And this is a great principle...' The author of Hidayah says: Making part of the thing produced by the miller or the worker the wage is a great principle from which the invalidity of many ijarahs is known. For example: (1) Employing someone to press oil and setting a part of the oil as wage. (2) Giving land to plant trees and sharing the land and trees. (3) Hiring someone to bake bread or card wool and setting a ratl of the bread or wool as wage. All these are impermissible. His statement: 'And the meaning in it...' That is, the secret of the prohibition of the miller's measure is that the employer at the time of contract is unable to deliver the wage because the wage in the weaver case is part of the woven cloth, and in the donkey hire case is part of the grain brought, and this wage will be obtained by the worker's act, so the employer will not be able to deliver it when the worker is able. If a porter is hired to carry half the grain in exchange for the other half, no wage is due. And this is contrary to the case where he hired him to carry half his food for the other half: no wage is due because the employer made the wage owner instantly by advance payment, so it became shared between them. And whoever hires a person to carry food shared between them, no wage is due because there is no part he carries except that he is working for himself in it, so delivery of the contracted object is not realized. And the wage will not exceed a qafiz because when the ijarah becomes fasid, the lesser of the named wage and the like wage is due, because he agreed to the reduction of the excess. And this is contrary to the case where they share in fuelwood: wage is due whatever it reaches according to Muhammad because the named wage there is unknown, so the reduction is not valid. Translation: And this is contrary to the case where he hired a porter to carry half this grain in exchange for the other half: no wage is due because the employer made him owner of the wage instantly in advance, so the food became shared between them. And whoever hires his partner to carry shared food, no wage is due because there is no part he carries except that he is working for himself in it. So delivery of the contracted object is not realized. And the wage will not exceed a qafiz because when the ijarah became fasid, what is less than the named wage and the like wage is due, because he agreed to reduce the excess. And this is contrary to the case where two people share in collecting firewood: wage is due whatever it reaches according to Imam Muhammad because the named wage there is unknown, so reduction is not valid. Ashraf al-Bidayah Urdu commentary on Hidayah vol 12. Elaboration of his statement: 'And this is contrary to the case where he hired him...' Previously the ruling was mentioned that if a donkey is hired to bring grain with the wage being a qafiz of that same grain, the ijarah is fasid. This ruling is contrary to the case where a porter is hired to carry half the grain in exchange for the other half: in that case no wage is due, neither the named nor the like. Because here the employer made the worker owner of the wage immediately in advance. 'Because delivery of the wage by virtue of acceleration necessitates ownership of the wage.' So the food became shared between them, and whoever hires his partner to carry shared food, no wage is due because any part he loads and brings, he is working for himself in it. So delivery of the contracted object is not realized because he did not surrender his own benefit. And in it is a difference with al-Shafi'i. Allamah Zaylai mentioned this case with its proof in Sharh al-Kanz and then said there are two objections. First: the ijarah is fasid while in our school even in a valid ijarah, the wage is not owned by the contract itself whether it is a specific thing or a debt. So how here without delivery and without condition of acceleration did he become owner? Second: the statements 'because the employer made the worker owner instantly' and 'no wage is due' are contradictory because the worker becomes owner of it in the manner of wage, and when no wage is due, how and for what reason will he become owner? The answer to the first objection is that the case is when the employer handed over all the food to the worker, as clarified by Sahib al-Nihayah, Sahib al-Miraj al-Dirayah, etc. 'and he handed over all of it, not part of it.' The answer to the second objection is that the contradiction is not conceded because 'ownership of the worker instantly' means the worker's ownership initially by virtue of the contract and delivery of wage by way of handing over, and 'no wage is due' means before the work due to the invalidity of the contract he is not entitled to wage, after he became owner by delivery, he becomes a partner in the food before completing the work. And there is no contradiction between these two meanings. His statement: 'And it will not exceed the wage...' 'Qayl Sabaq' and similarly if he hires a donkey to carry food with a qafiz from it is connected. The meaning is that in the donkey hire case, the wage will not be given more than a qafiz. That is, if the like wage is less than a qafiz or equal to a qafiz, that is given, and if it is more than a qafiz, the excess is not given. Because when the ijarah is fasid, the lesser of the named wage and the like wage is due. Because the lessor agreed to reduce the excess, since he was satisfied with the qafiz.
Source pages p. 73

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah, an Urdu commentary on al-Hidayah, addresses a key principle in the Hanafi law of ijarah (hire/lease). The passage opens with the hadith of the Prophet (صلى الله عليه وسلم) prohibiting three specific transactions: the stud fee of a goat, the earnings of a cupper, and the measure of the miller (i.e., taking a portion of the ground grain as payment). The commentator then cites additional narrations reinforcing the prohibition. The core of the passage is the explanation that this hadith establishes a 'great principle': any ijarah contract where the wage consists of part of the very thing produced by the worker's labor is invalid (fasid). Examples include: hiring someone to press sesame oil and giving him part of the oil; giving land for planting trees and sharing the land and trees; hiring someone to bake bread or card wool and giving a portion of the product. The rationale (ma'na) given is that at the time of contract, the employer cannot deliver the wage because it does not yet exist; it will only come into existence through the worker's own act. Thus, the employer is unable to fulfill his obligation immediately. The passage then discusses a contrasting case: if a porter is hired to carry half of a grain stock in exchange for the other half, no wage is due at all. This is because the employer paid the wage in advance by giving the porter ownership of half the grain instantly, making the porter a co-owner of the grain. Consequently, when the porter carries the grain, he is carrying his own property, and the condition of delivering the subject matter (the service) is not fulfilled. The commentator notes that this differs from Imam al-Shafi'i's view. A significant portion of the passage deals with two objections raised by Allamah Zaylai: first, how can the porter own the wage instantly without delivery or an express condition of acceleration, when even in a valid ijarah ownership of the wage is not established by the contract alone? Second, how can the statements 'the employer made the worker owner instantly' and 'no wage is due' coexist without contradiction? The answers clarify that the case presupposes that the employer actually handed over all the grain to the worker, and that 'ownership instantly' refers to the initial transfer by delivery, while 'no wage is due' means the worker is not entitled to a specific wage for the service due to the contract's invalidity; he already became a partner through delivery. Finally, the passage explains that in the case of the invalid donkey hire, the worker receives only up to the named wage (one qafiz) even if the fair wage (ujrat al-mithl) is higher, because the employer consented to reduce any excess by agreeing to the qafiz. However, in a case of joint wood-collecting, Imam Muhammad holds that the worker gets the full fair wage because the named wage was unknown, so no reduction is applicable. This passage illustrates the Hanafi school's strict approach to ensuring that the wage is clearly known and deliverable at the time of contract, and that the worker does not end up working for himself under the guise of a hire.

Key Terms
قفيز الطحان (qafīz al-ṭaḥḥān): The measure of grain taken by a miller as payment for grinding; prohibited.
إجارة فاسدة (ijārah fāsidah): A hire contract that is invalid due to a defect in its essential elements, such as uncertainty in wage.
أجر المثل (ajr al-mithl): The fair market wage for similar work, used when the named wage is invalid or unknown.
نهى (nahy): Prohibition; in Hanafi usul, a prohibition indicates invalidity (fasad) of the contract unless specified otherwise.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is an example of a fasid ijarah under the great principle of qafiz al-tahan?
A) Hiring a gardener for a fixed monthly salary.
B) Hiring a cook and giving him 10% of the restaurant's daily earnings.
C) Hiring a driver to transport goods for a fixed fee per trip.
D) Hiring a painter to paint your house for a lump sum of $1000.

Key Takeaway
The hadith prohibiting qafiz al-tahan establishes a general Hanafi principle: any ijarah where the wage is part of the worker's own product is fasid because the wage is uncertain and not deliverable at contract formation.

Ijarah — Hire and Lease
intermediate
15 min
The Porter Case: No Wage When Advance Delivery Makes a Co-Owner
Explaining the porter case and its implications

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling that a porter hired to carry half the grain for the other half receives no wage when the grain is delivered in advance, and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
If the wage is delivered in advance, the worker becomes a co-owner, and no wage is due for carrying his own property.

The Hidayah presents a critical nuance: when the employer hands over the grain to the porter before any work, the porter becomes a co-owner. Consequently, carrying the grain is working for himself, and the condition of delivering the service (taslim al-ma'qud alayh) is not fulfilled. This ruling leads to a significant difference with Imam al-Shafi'i and raises important questions about the nature of ownership in fasid contracts.

Guided Path
1
State the Specific Case and Ruling
A porter is hired to carry half of a grain stock to a destination. The wage is the other half of the grain. The employer hands over all the grain to the porter instantly before the work. Ruling: no wage is due, neither the named half nor the like wage.
This is not the same as the general fasid ijarah rule where ujrat al-mithl is due.
2
Understand the Reasoning: Advance Delivery Creates Co-Ownership
By delivering the entire grain stock to the porter immediately, the employer transfers ownership of half the grain as the wage. The porter becomes a co-owner of the grain. Thus, when he carries the grain, every part he lifts is partly his own property. Hence, he works for himself, not for the employer.
The key act is ta'jil (advance payment) which causes immediate ownership.
3
Identify the Condition Not Met: Delivery of Service
In a valid ijarah, the worker must deliver his service to the employer. Here, because the porter is carrying his own property, he never surrenders his personal benefit. Thus, taslim al-ma'qud alayh (delivery of the contracted subject matter) is not realized.
The service (the carrying) is not performed for the employer but for the worker himself.
4
Address the Objections Raised by Allamah Zaylai
Two objections: (1) How can ownership occur without express acceleration condition? (2) How can 'made him owner instantly' and 'no wage is due' coexist? Resolution: (1) The case assumes full handover of grain. (2) Ownership occurs by the contract and delivery, but entitlement to wage is separate and is defeated by the invalidity and the worker's self-interest.
The resolution clarifies that ownership and wage entitlement are not contradictory.
5
Compare with the Shafi'i Position
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that some wage is due. The Hanafi school disagrees based on the co-ownership reasoning. This is a thamarah al-khilaf: practical difference in courts.
Understanding this ikhtilaf helps in legal analysis.

وهذا بخلاف ما اذا استاجره ليحمل نصف طعامه بالنصف الآخر حيث لا يجب له الاجر لان المستاجر ملك الاجر في الحال بالتعجيل فصار مشتركا بينهما ومن استاجر رجلا لحمل طعام مشترك بينهما لا يجب الاجر لان ما من جزء يحمله الا وهو عامل لنفسه فيه فلا يتحقق تسليم المعقود عليه ولا يجاوز بالاجر قفيزا لانه لما فسدت الاجارة فالواجب الاقل مما سمى ومن اجر المثل لانه رضى بحط الزيادة وهذا بخلاف ما اذا اشتركا في الاحتطاب حيث يجب الاجر بالغا ما بلغ عند محمد لان المسمى هناک غیر معلوم فلم يصح الحط.

تشریح قوله وهذا بخلاف ما اذا استاجره .. الخ - سابق میں جو یہ مسئلہ مذکور ہوا کہ اگر ایک گدھا اس لئے اجارہ پر لیا تا کہ اس پر اناج لا دے جس کی اجرت اسی اناج میں سے ایک قفیز ہوگی تو اجارہ فاسد ہے۔ یہ حکم اس صورت کے خلاف ہے جب کسی جمال کو اس طرح اجارہ پر لیا کہ اس اناج کا آدھا باقی آدھے کے عوض اٹھا کر پہنچا دے کہ اس صورت میں کچھ اجرت واجب نہ ہوگی۔ نہ اجر سمی اور نہ اجر مثل ۔ اس لئے کہ یہاں مستاجر نے اجیر کو فی الحال پیشگی اجرت کا مالک کر دیا۔

اول یہ کہ اجارہ فاسد ہے اور حال یہ ہے کہ ہمارے یہاں اجارہ صحیحہ میں بھی نفس عقد کے ذریعہ سے اجرت کا مالک نہیں ہوتا خواہ وہ عین ہو یا دین ہو۔ تو پھر یہاں بلا تسلیم و بلاشرط تعجیل کیسے مالک ہو گیا ؟
دوم یه که لان المستاجر ملک الاجیر فی الحال اور لا يجب له الاجر دونوں قولوں میں منافات ہے اس لئے کہ اجیر بھی اس کا مالک ہوگا ۔ وہ بطریق اجرت ہی ہوگا۔ اور جب اس کے لئے اجرت واجب ہی نہ ہوئی تو پھر کیسے اور کس سبب سے مالک ہوگا ؟
پہلے اشکال کا جواب یہ ہے کہ مسئلہ کی وضع اس صورت میں ہے جب مستاجر نے کل طعام اجیر کو سپرد کر دیا ہو جیسا کہ صاحب نہایہ و صاحب معراج الدرایہ وغیرہ نے نفس مسئلہ کی تحریر میں و رفع الیہ کلہ ولا اجملہ کی تصریح کی ہے۔
اور دوسرے اشکال کا جواب ..... یہ ہے کہ بین القولین منافات غیر مسلم ہے اس لئے کہ ملک الاجیر فی الحال کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ اجیر کی ملک ابتداء بموجب عقد ہے اور تسلیم اجرت بطریق تقبیل اور لا یجب لہ الاجر کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ وہ قبل از عمل بطلان عقد کی وجہ سے مستحق اجر نہیں ہے بعد ازاں کہ وہ بذریعہ تسلیم مالک ہو گیا بایں سبب کے معقود علیہ کے ایفاء سے پہلے طعام میں شریک ہو چکا ولا تنافی بين هذين المعنيين
قوله ولا يجاوز بالاجر .... الخ " يقول سابق و كذا اذا استاجر حماراً ليحمل طعاماً بقفيز منہ سے وابستہ ہے۔ مطلب یہ ہے کہ مسئلہ استیجار حمار میں اجرت ایک قفیز سے زیادہ نہیں دی جائے گی۔ یعنی جو اجر مثل واجب ہو اگر وہ ایک قفیز سے کم ہو یا ایک قفیز ہو تو یہی دیا جائے گا اور اگر ایک قفیز سے زیادہ ہو تو زائد مقدار نہیں دی جائے گی۔ اس لئے کہ جب اجارہ فاسد ہوا تو بیان کردہ اجرت اور اجر مثل میں سے جو کم ہو وہ واجب ہوتا ہے۔ کیونکہ کرایہ پر دینے والا ایک قفیز سے زیادتی گھٹانے پر خود ہی راضی ہو گیا ہے۔ حيث رضی با لقفیز
Book of Ijarah. Ashraf al-Hidayah Urdu commentary on Hidayah vol 12. From the Prophet (ﷺ) that he prohibited the stud fee of the goat, the earnings of the cupper, and the miller's measure. And via the way of Sufyan al-Thawri from Hisham Abi Kulayb from Ibn Abi An'am: the Messenger of Allah (ﷺ) prohibited the stud fee of the stallion and the miller's measure. Also the famous muhaddith Abd al-Haqq mentioned the same in al-Ahkam via al-Daraqutni's chain. His statement: 'And this is a great principle...' The author of Hidayah says: Making part of the thing produced by the miller or the worker the wage is a great principle from which the invalidity of many ijarahs is known. For example: (1) Employing someone to press oil and setting a part of the oil as wage. (2) Giving land to plant trees and sharing the land and trees. (3) Hiring someone to bake bread or card wool and setting a ratl of the bread or wool as wage. All these are impermissible. His statement: 'And the meaning in it...' That is, the secret of the prohibition of the miller's measure is that the employer at the time of contract is unable to deliver the wage because the wage in the weaver case is part of the woven cloth, and in the donkey hire case is part of the grain brought, and this wage will be obtained by the worker's act, so the employer will not be able to deliver it when the worker is able. If a porter is hired to carry half the grain in exchange for the other half, no wage is due. And this is contrary to the case where he hired him to carry half his food for the other half: no wage is due because the employer made the wage owner instantly by advance payment, so it became shared between them. And whoever hires a person to carry food shared between them, no wage is due because there is no part he carries except that he is working for himself in it, so delivery of the contracted object is not realized. And the wage will not exceed a qafiz because when the ijarah becomes fasid, the lesser of the named wage and the like wage is due, because he agreed to the reduction of the excess. And this is contrary to the case where they share in fuelwood: wage is due whatever it reaches according to Muhammad because the named wage there is unknown, so the reduction is not valid. Translation: And this is contrary to the case where he hired a porter to carry half this grain in exchange for the other half: no wage is due because the employer made him owner of the wage instantly in advance, so the food became shared between them. And whoever hires his partner to carry shared food, no wage is due because there is no part he carries except that he is working for himself in it. So delivery of the contracted object is not realized. And the wage will not exceed a qafiz because when the ijarah became fasid, what is less than the named wage and the like wage is due, because he agreed to reduce the excess. And this is contrary to the case where two people share in collecting firewood: wage is due whatever it reaches according to Imam Muhammad because the named wage there is unknown, so reduction is not valid. Ashraf al-Bidayah Urdu commentary on Hidayah vol 12. Elaboration of his statement: 'And this is contrary to the case where he hired him...' Previously the ruling was mentioned that if a donkey is hired to bring grain with the wage being a qafiz of that same grain, the ijarah is fasid. This ruling is contrary to the case where a porter is hired to carry half the grain in exchange for the other half: in that case no wage is due, neither the named nor the like. Because here the employer made the worker owner of the wage immediately in advance. 'Because delivery of the wage by virtue of acceleration necessitates ownership of the wage.' So the food became shared between them, and whoever hires his partner to carry shared food, no wage is due because any part he loads and brings, he is working for himself in it. So delivery of the contracted object is not realized because he did not surrender his own benefit. And in it is a difference with al-Shafi'i. Allamah Zaylai mentioned this case with its proof in Sharh al-Kanz and then said there are two objections. First: the ijarah is fasid while in our school even in a valid ijarah, the wage is not owned by the contract itself whether it is a specific thing or a debt. So how here without delivery and without condition of acceleration did he become owner? Second: the statements 'because the employer made the worker owner instantly' and 'no wage is due' are contradictory because the worker becomes owner of it in the manner of wage, and when no wage is due, how and for what reason will he become owner? The answer to the first objection is that the case is when the employer handed over all the food to the worker, as clarified by Sahib al-Nihayah, Sahib al-Miraj al-Dirayah, etc. 'and he handed over all of it, not part of it.' The answer to the second objection is that the contradiction is not conceded because 'ownership of the worker instantly' means the worker's ownership initially by virtue of the contract and delivery of wage by way of handing over, and 'no wage is due' means before the work due to the invalidity of the contract he is not entitled to wage, after he became owner by delivery, he becomes a partner in the food before completing the work. And there is no contradiction between these two meanings. His statement: 'And it will not exceed the wage...' 'Qayl Sabaq' and similarly if he hires a donkey to carry food with a qafiz from it is connected. The meaning is that in the donkey hire case, the wage will not be given more than a qafiz. That is, if the like wage is less than a qafiz or equal to a qafiz, that is given, and if it is more than a qafiz, the excess is not given. Because when the ijarah is fasid, the lesser of the named wage and the like wage is due. Because the lessor agreed to reduce the excess, since he was satisfied with the qafiz.
Source pages p. 73

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah, an Urdu commentary on al-Hidayah, addresses a key principle in the Hanafi law of ijarah (hire/lease). The passage opens with the hadith of the Prophet (صلى الله عليه وسلم) prohibiting three specific transactions: the stud fee of a goat, the earnings of a cupper, and the measure of the miller (i.e., taking a portion of the ground grain as payment). The commentator then cites additional narrations reinforcing the prohibition. The core of the passage is the explanation that this hadith establishes a 'great principle': any ijarah contract where the wage consists of part of the very thing produced by the worker's labor is invalid (fasid). Examples include: hiring someone to press sesame oil and giving him part of the oil; giving land for planting trees and sharing the land and trees; hiring someone to bake bread or card wool and giving a portion of the product. The rationale (ma'na) given is that at the time of contract, the employer cannot deliver the wage because it does not yet exist; it will only come into existence through the worker's own act. Thus, the employer is unable to fulfill his obligation immediately. The passage then discusses a contrasting case: if a porter is hired to carry half of a grain stock in exchange for the other half, no wage is due at all. This is because the employer paid the wage in advance by giving the porter ownership of half the grain instantly, making the porter a co-owner of the grain. Consequently, when the porter carries the grain, he is carrying his own property, and the condition of delivering the subject matter (the service) is not fulfilled. The commentator notes that this differs from Imam al-Shafi'i's view. A significant portion of the passage deals with two objections raised by Allamah Zaylai: first, how can the porter own the wage instantly without delivery or an express condition of acceleration, when even in a valid ijarah ownership of the wage is not established by the contract alone? Second, how can the statements 'the employer made the worker owner instantly' and 'no wage is due' coexist without contradiction? The answers clarify that the case presupposes that the employer actually handed over all the grain to the worker, and that 'ownership instantly' refers to the initial transfer by delivery, while 'no wage is due' means the worker is not entitled to a specific wage for the service due to the contract's invalidity; he already became a partner through delivery. Finally, the passage explains that in the case of the invalid donkey hire, the worker receives only up to the named wage (one qafiz) even if the fair wage (ujrat al-mithl) is higher, because the employer consented to reduce any excess by agreeing to the qafiz. However, in a case of joint wood-collecting, Imam Muhammad holds that the worker gets the full fair wage because the named wage was unknown, so no reduction is applicable. This passage illustrates the Hanafi school's strict approach to ensuring that the wage is clearly known and deliverable at the time of contract, and that the worker does not end up working for himself under the guise of a hire.

Key Terms
تعجيل (ta'jīl): Advance payment of the wage, which in this context makes the worker a co-owner of the subject matter.
تسليم المعقود عليه (taslīm al-ma'qūd 'alayh): Delivery of the contracted subject matter (the service); a condition for the worker's entitlement to wage.
أجر المثل (ajr al-mithl): Fair market wage for similar work.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the porter case, why does the Hanafi school rule that no wage is due?
A) Because the porter did not complete the work.
B) Because the ijarah is fasid and no compensation is ever due for fasid contracts.
C) Because the porter became a co-owner of the grain through advance delivery, so he works for himself.
D) Because the named wage was unknown.

Key Takeaway
Advance delivery of the wage in a fasid ijarah can transfer ownership to the worker, making him a co-owner and voiding any wage claim, as he works for himself.

Hiring a Donkey to Carry Grain with Payment from the Grain
Ruling on fasid ijarah when payment is from the object carried.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on hiring a donkey with wage from the carried grain, explain why it is fasid, and distinguish the camel exception, applying the principles of jahalah and ownership transfer.

Core Idea
Hiring with wage from the carried grain is fasid due to uncertainty; only equivalent wage is due.

This passage expands on a ruling from Al-Hidayah regarding a specific ijarah case: hiring a donkey to carry grain where the wage is a measure from that grain. The Hanafi school deems such a contract fasid (voidable) because of fundamental uncertainty (jahalah) in the wage. The passage also records an exception when the grain is made shared property in advance, and it addresses internal objections raised by later scholars like Zayla'i to clarify the legal reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the basic ruling and its exception
First, note the ruling: hiring a donkey to carry grain with a wage from that grain is fasid. Then, identify the exception: hiring a camel where the hirer gives half the grain immediately as ownership, making them partners.
The exception leads to no wage due, not even ujrat al-mithl.
2
Understand the Hanafi rationale for fasid
The wage is part of the carried goods, unknown at contract time – this is jahalah. A valid ijarah requires the wage to be known and certain.
The camel exception works because ownership is transferred immediately, removing uncertainty.
3
Examine Zayla'i's objections and their answers
Zayla'i raises two objections: (1) ownership of wage should not be immediate in a fasid contract; (2) contradiction between immediate ownership and no wage due. The answers clarify that delivery of the entire grain causes ownership, and ownership is not as wage but as a shared property.
These answers refine the Hanafi position without changing the ruling.
4
Distinguish from the Shafi'i position and note practical consequence
The Shafi'i school considers the contract valid. The practical difference: Hanafi requires ujrat al-mithl if work is done; Shafi'i enforces the specified wage.
The Hanafi view is mufta bihi in the school.

Commentary on his saying 'And this is contrary to the case when he hired him...' - Previously mentioned is the ruling that if a donkey is hired to carry grain, with the wage being one qafiz from that grain, the ijarah is fasid. This ruling is contrary to the case when a camel is hired such that he carries half of the grain for the remaining half; in that case no wage is due, neither named wage nor equivalent wage. This is because the hirer has made the hired person the owner of the wage in advance. Because the delivery of wage by way of advance induces ownership of the wage. So the food becomes shared between them, and if someone hires his partner to carry shared food, no wage is due. Because whatever part of the grain he loads and brings, he is also an agent for himself in it. Thus the delivery of the subject matter is not achieved, because he did not give up his own benefit. And in this there is a disagreement with al-Shafi'i. After mentioning this ruling with its proof in Sharh al-Kanz, Allama Zayla'i said there are two objections. First: The ijarah is fasid, whereas with us, even in a valid ijarah, one does not become owner of the wage through the contract itself, whether it is a specific thing or a debt. So how did he become owner here without delivery and without condition? Second: The statement 'the hirer made the hired person owner immediately' and 'no wage is due to him' are contradictory, because the hired person would also be its owner, and that would be by way of wage. And when no wage is due to him, then how and by what cause would he become owner? The answer to the first objection is that the situation of the ruling is when the hirer handed over all the food to the hired person, as the authors of al-Nihaya and Ma'raj al-Diraya etc. have clarified in writing the ruling itself: 'and he handed over all of it, not some of it'. The answer to the second objection is that the contradiction between the two statements is not admitted, because 'the hired person being owner immediately' means that the hired person's ownership is initially by the contract, and 'delivery of wage by way of giving possession', and 'no wage is due to him' means that before the work, due to the invalidity of the contract, he is not entitled to the wage. After he becomes owner by delivery, before the fulfillment of the subject matter, he has become a partner in the food. There is no contradiction between these two meanings.
Source pages p. 74

Commentary
This passage is an expansion and critical refinement of a ruling from the Hidayah. It discusses the case of hiring a donkey to carry grain where the wage is part of that grain. The ruling is that such an ijarah is fasid (invalid) because of jahalah (uncertainty). The exception is when the grain is shared in advance: if the hirer gives half the grain to the hired party as immediate ownership, then the hired party carries the other half for the wage of his own share. In that case, no wage is due because the hired party is acting for himself as well. The passage then records a disagreement with Shafi'i (who validifies such a contract) and then presents Zayla'i's two objections to the Hanafi reasoning. The first objection: in a valid ijarah, ownership of wage is not established by the contract alone; so how can it be here? The answer: the ruling assumes that the entire grain was handed over to the hired party as a wage in advance, thus establishing ownership. The second objection: there is contradiction between saying the hired party becomes owner immediately and that no wage is due. The answer: ownership here is by the contract as a gift or transfer, not as a wage; the entitlement to wage is suspended due to the invalidity. There is no contradiction because ownership is independent. This passage carefully defends the Hanafi position against internal critiques.

Key Terms
اجارہ فاسد (ijarah fasid): An invalid contract of hire due to an imperfection that can be rectified if the defect is removed before completion.
اجر مثل (ujrat al-mithl): The market rate wage for similar services, due when the named wage is not valid.
معقود علیہ (ma'qud 'alayh): The subject matter of the contract; here, the benefit of carrying.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the case of hiring a camel to carry grain with payment being half of the grain (the camel owner carries the other half for the wage of his own share), what is the ruling according to Hanafi fiqh?
A) The ijarah is valid and the named wage is due.
B) The ijarah is fasid and only equivalent wage is due.
C) No wage is due because the hired party is acting for himself as a partner.
D) The ijarah is batil and no compensation is due.

Key Takeaway
Hiring with wage from the carried object is fasid ijarah because of uncertainty; if the hired party becomes a partner through immediate ownership, no wage is due.

Wage in Fasid Ijarah Is Limited to the Named Wage
Ruling that in fasid ijarah, the wage is limited to the named amount if less.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the rule for wage in a fasid ijarah contract and apply it to determine the due amount.

Core Idea
In fasid ijarah, the lesser of the named wage and the market rate is due.

When a hire contract is defective (fasid), the wage is not automatically the market rate. This lesson explores a key Hanafi principle from al-Hidayah: the wage is capped at the named amount when it is lower than the equivalent wage. We will examine the case of hiring a donkey for a qafiz of grain and why the lessor's consent limits liability.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contract and its defect
Recognize that the ijarah is fasid, meaning it lacks a condition for validity but the transaction has occurred.
2
State the default rule for fasid ijarah
Normally, ujrat al-mithl (equivalent wage) is due because the named wage is void.
3
Apply the exception: named wage as cap
Note that the ruling says the wage should not exceed the named wage. This overrides the default only when the named wage is lower.
4
Understand the rationale (illah)
The lessor agreed to the named wage, so imposing a higher market rate would go beyond his consent.
5
Determine the operational ruling
The wage due is the lesser of the named wage and ujrat al-mithl.

قوله ولا يجاوز بالاجر .... الخ " يقول سابق و كذا اذا استاجر حماراً ليحمل طعاماً بقفيز منہ سے وابستہ ہے۔ مطلب یہ ہے کہ مسئلہ استیجار حمار میں اجرت ایک قفیز سے زیادہ نہیں دی جائے گی۔ یعنی جو اجر مثل واجب ہوا گر وہ ایک قفی: سے کم ہو یا ایک قفیز ہو تو یہی دیا جائے گا اور اگر ایک قفیز سے زیادہ ہو تو زائد مقدار نہیں دی جائے گی۔ اس لئے کہ جب اجارہ فاسد مظہر اتو بیان کردہ اجرت اور اجر مثل میں سے جو کم ہو وہ واجب ہوتا ہے۔ کیونکہ کرایہ پر دینے والا ایک قفیز سے زیادتی گھٹانے پر خود ہی راضی ہو گیا ہے۔ حيث رضی با لقفیز

فائدہ نہا یہ میں ہے کہ " لا يجاوز بالا جر قفیزا میں لفظ قفیز کا انتصاب ان لوگوں کے قول پر ہے جو فعل کی اسناد کو جار مجرور کی طرف جائز کہتے ہیں اور یہ قول ضعیف ہے۔ شرح رضی میں ہے کہ یہ کوفین اور بعض متاخرین کا مذہب ہے۔
His saying 'And the wage should not exceed a qafiz...' is connected to what was said earlier: 'And likewise if he hires a donkey to carry grain for a qafiz from it.' The meaning is that in the issue of hiring a donkey, the wage will not be given more than one qafiz. That is, if the equivalent wage is less than or equal to one qafiz, that will be given; and if it is more than one qafiz, the extra amount will not be given. Because when the ijarah is fasid, of the named wage and the equivalent wage, the lesser is due. Because the lessor has agreed to the qafiz, being satisfied with it. Benefit: In al-Nihayah it is said that in 'la yujawizu bi al-ajri qafizan', the accusative case of the word qafiz is according to those who permit assigning the verb to the prepositional phrase, and this view is weak. In Sharh Radi it is said that this is the madhhab of the Kufans and some later scholars.
Source pages p. 74

Commentary
This passage explains a sub-rule in fasid ijarah: the wage that must be paid is the lesser of the named wage and the equivalent wage. The background is the case of hiring a donkey for carrying grain with a named wage of one qafiz. The ijarah is fasid, so normally ujrat al-mithl would be due. However, the text rules that the wage should not exceed the named qafiz. The reasoning: since the owner (hirer) agreed to pay one qafiz, he is satisfied with that amount. If market rate is higher, the extra is not forced on him because he consented only to one qafiz. This is a mercy to the hirer. The passage then notes a grammatical issue: the word 'qafizan' is in the accusative case, which is a construction used by Kufan grammarians (weak according to Basrans). This shows the depth of analysis in commentaries.

Key Terms
اجر مثل (ujrat al-mithl): The market rate wage for the same service in the same place and time.
قفیز (qafiz): A measure of grain, approximately 8 to 12 liters, used as a unit of volume in Iraq.
اجارہ فاسد (ijarah fasid): A hire contract that is defective due to missing a condition of validity, but not void ab initio.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a fasid ijarah where the named wage is 1 qafiz and the market equivalent wage is 2 qafiz, how much wage is due according to the passage?
A) 2 qafiz
B) 1 qafiz
C) Nothing
D) 1.5 qafiz

Key Takeaway
In fasid ijarah, the wage is the lesser of the named wage and the market equivalent, based on the lessor's consent.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Wage Cap in Wood-Collecting Partnership
Intra-Hanafi dispute on wage cap for bundle-tier in wood partnership.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two positions of Imam Muhammad and Imam Abu Yusuf regarding the limit on ujrat al-mithl for a partner who only ties bundles, and explain the thamarah al-khilaf.

Core Idea
No named wage means full compensation; partnership intent caps wage at half the property value.

This passage presents a nuanced case within the Hanafi school: two people cooperate to collect wood, but one does only the tying while the other does the gathering. Who owns the wood, and what is the bundle-tieer entitled to? The Hanafi masters differ on whether his wage is unlimited or capped by the implicit partnership share. Understanding this dispute clarifies how intention and agreement shape remuneration in cooperative work.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
Two persons cooperate in collecting wood. One gathers the wood; the other only ties bundles. Determine who becomes the owner of the wood and what the bundle-tieer should receive.
The passage states the collector owns the wood.
2
State the baseline ruling
The collector is the owner. The bundle-tieer is entitled to ujrat al-mithl (equivalent wage). This is agreed upon.
3
Analyze Imam Muhammad's position
Imam Muhammad holds that the full ujrat al-mithl is due without cap, because no named wage was agreed. Thus reduction is not justified.
4
Analyze Imam Abu Yusuf's position
Imam Abu Yusuf argues that due to the partnership, the bundle-tieer implicitly agreed to share half the wood's value, so his wage cannot exceed half.
5
Compare and determine thamarah al-khilaf
Compare the practical consequences: under Imam Muhammad, the wage may exceed half the wood's value; under Abu Yusuf, it cannot. Note that the text does not give a tarjih; both views are recognized.

Source Text

قوله وهذا بخلاف ما اذا اشتركا .. الخ - حکم مذکور اس صورت کے خلاف ہے جب دو شخصوں نے لکڑیاں چننے میں شرکت کی پھر ایک نے جنگل میں لکڑیاں چنیں اور دوسرے نے صرف گٹھے باندھے۔ تو لکڑیوں کا مالک چننے والا ہوگا۔ اور گٹھے باندھنے والے کو صرف اجر مثل ملے گا۔ لیکن یہ اجرت امام محمد کے نزدیک جتنی بھی ہو پوری ملے گی ۔ کیونکہ یہاں کوئی اجرت مسمی معلوم نہیں ہے تو گھٹانا صیح نہ ہوا۔ اور امام ابو یوسف کے نزدیک شرکت کی وجہ سے وہ لکڑیوں کی آدھی قیمت پر راضی ہو گیا تھا۔ تو اجر مثل ان لکڑیوں کی آدھی قیمت سے زیادہ نہیں دیا جائے گا اور اگر ان دونوں نے لکڑیاں چنیں اور دونوں نے گٹھے بھی باندے تو دونوں برابر کے شریک ہوں گے۔
His saying 'And this is contrary to the case when they cooperated...' - The mentioned ruling is contrary to the case when two persons cooperate in collecting wood, then one collects wood in the forest, and the other only ties the bundles. Then the wood will be owned by the collector, and the bundle-tieer will receive only the equivalent wage. But this wage, according to Imam Muhammad, will be given in full whatever it may be, because there is no named wage known here, so reduction is not correct. And according to Imam Abu Yusuf, because of the partnership, he had agreed to half the value of the wood, so the equivalent wage will not exceed half the value of the wood. And if both collect wood and both tie bundles, then both are equal partners.
Source pages p. 75

Commentary
This passage discusses a scenario where two people agree to cooperate in collecting wood, but then one does the actual gathering while the other only ties bundles. The ruling: the one who collects is the owner of the wood; the bundle-tieer is only entitled to ujrat al-mithl (market wage for his labor). However, there is an intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Muhammad and Imam Abu Yusuf regarding the cap on this wage. Imam Muhammad says the full equivalent wage is due because there was no named wage, so no limit. Imam Abu Yusuf says the bundle-tieer implicitly agreed to half the value of the wood (since partnership was intended), so his wage cannot exceed half the wood's value. This is a practical application of the principle that when parties cooperate with intent to share, the wage is limited by the share they implicitly agreed to. The passage also clarifies that if both do both tasks, they are equal partners.

Key Terms
شرکت (shirkah): Partnership in collecting wood; here an informal cooperation, not a formal business contract.
اجر مثل (ujrat al-mithl): Market rate wage for the work of tying bundles.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Half the value of the wood
B) Full equivalent wage (ujrat al-mithl) regardless of the wood's value
C) Nothing, because he did not collect
D) A share in the wood depending on his labor

Key Takeaway
In cooperative work without a named wage, the Hanafi school has two positions on whether the wage is capped by an implied partnership share.

Hiring a Baker for Ten Sa' Today: Abu Hanifa vs. Sahibayn
Ruling on hiring a baker with time specification; dispute among Hanafi imams.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the validity of an ijarah contract when the time specification 'al-yawm' creates ambiguity, and identify the thamarah al-khilaf between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
The word 'al-yawm' in a hire contract can be ambiguous: does it specify the time of the benefit or the work? That ambiguity invalidates the contract for Abu Hanifa but not for the Sahibayn.

This passage examines a detailed intra-Hanafi dispute about the validity of hiring a baker to bake ten sa' of flour 'today' for one dirham. The disagreement hinges on the interpretation of the word 'al-yawm' and whether it creates uncertainty (jahalah) in the subject matter of the contract. Understanding this dispute clarifies how Hanafi jurists resolve ambiguity in ijarah contracts and the practical difference in rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contract and its terms
The contract: hiring a baker to bake ten sa' of flour. Wage: one dirham. Time: 'al-yawm' (today). Note the ambiguity: does 'today' refer to the time when the work must be done, or the period of the benefit (use of oven)?
The term 'makhtum' means a sealed measure; equivalent to qafiz.
2
State the two opposing positions
Abu Hanifa: the contract is fasid because of uncertainty in the subject matter. Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad): it is valid because 'today' indicates urgency and the work is the subject matter.
The Sahibayn interpret 'al-yawm' as a time for urgency, removing ambiguity.
3
Analyze the reasoning of each side
Abu Hanifa argues that 'al-yawm' could refer either to the time of the benefit (using the oven) or the time of the work (baking). No preponderance. Sahibayn interpret the phrase as specifying the time for the work, making it clear.
Abu Hanifa's response: no preponderance; thus jahalah remains.
4
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference)
Under Abu Hanifa, the contract is fasid, so only ujrat al-mithl (fair wage) is due. Under Sahibayn, the contract is valid, and the named wage is due.
This affects the compensation: named wage vs. fair wage.
5
Note the exception narrated from Abu Hanifa
If the wording is 'fi al-yawm' (within the day), Abu Hanifa accepts validity because the preposition clarifies that time is a container for the work, not the subject matter.
This is similar to a rule in divorce cases, as mentioned in the text.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال ومن استاجر رجلا ليخبز له هذه العشرة المخاتيم اليوم بدرهم فهو فاسد وهذا عند ابي حنيفة وقال ابویوسف ومحمد فى الاجارات هو جائز لانه يجعل المعقود عملا ويجعل ذكر الوقت للاستعجال تصحيحا للعقد فترتفع الجهالة وله ان المعقود عليه مجهول لان ذكر الوقت يوجب كون المنفعة معقودا عليها وذكر العمل يوجب كونه معقودا عليه ولا ترجيح ونفع المستاجر في الثاني ونفع الأجير في الأول فیفضى الى المنازعة وعن ابي حنيفة انه يصح الاجارة اذا قال فى اليوم وقد سمّى عملا لانه للظرف فكان عقود عليه العمل بخلاف قوله اليوم وقد مر مثله في الطلاق
ترجمہ جس نے اجارہ پر لیا کسی کو تا کہ پکائے اس کے لئے یہ دس صاع آٹا آج کے دن ایک درہم کے عوض تو یہ فاسد ہے۔ اور یہ امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک ہے اور صاحبین نے اجارت میں کہا ہے کہ یہ جائز ہے کیونکہ عمل کو معقود علیہ اور ذکر وقت کو برائے استعمال ٹھہر الیا جائے گا۔ عقد کو صحیح کرنے کے لئے پس جہالت اٹھ جائے گی۔ امام ابو حنیفہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ معقود علیہ مجہول ہے۔ اس لئے کہ بیان وقت واجب کرتا ہے منفعت کے معقود علیہ ہونے کو اور ذکر عمل واجب کرتا ہے کام کے معقود علیہ ہونے کو اور کسی کو ترجیح ہے نہیں اور مستاجر کا نفع دوسری صورت میں ہے اور اجیر کا نفع پہلی صورت میں ہے۔ پس یہ جھگڑے تک پہنچائے گا۔ اور امام ابوحنیفہ سے روایت ہے کہ اجارہ صحیح ہوگا۔ جب اس نے فی الیوم کہا ہو اور کام بیان کر دیا ہو۔ کیونکہ یہ ظرف کے لئے پس معقود علیہ عمل ہوا۔ بخلاف اس کے قول الیوم کے اور اسکے مثل طلاق میں گزر چکا۔
تشریح قوله ومن استاجر رجلا .. الخ - مخا تیم مختوم کی جمع ہے صاع کو کہتے ہیں ۔ جس کی شاہد حدیث ابوسعید خدری الوسق ستون مختوما صاع کو مختوم اس لئے کہتے ہیں کہ اس کے منہ کو مہر زد کر دیا جاتا ہے تا کہ بڑھے گھئے نہیں ۔ مبسوط میں ہے کہ مختوم اور قفیز ایک ہی چیز ہے۔ قول میں لفظ هذه ليخبر فعل کا مفعول ہے۔ اور العشرۃ اس کی صفت ہے۔ اور الخا تیم مجرور بالا ضافہ ہے جیسے الخمسة الا ثواب میں اثواب کو فین کی رائے پر مجرور ہے اور الیوم بناء بر ظرفیت منصوب ہے اور بدرھم استاجر سے متعلق ہے۔
He said: And whoever hires a man to bake for him these ten sa' (measure) of flour today for one dirham, it is fasid, and this is according to Abu Hanifa. And Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (al-Shaybani) said in the book of Ijarat that it is valid, because he makes the work the subject matter, and makes the mentioning of time for the purpose of haste to validate the contract, so ignorance is removed. And (Abu Hanifa's) proof is that the subject matter is unknown, because mentioning time requires that the benefit is the subject matter, and mentioning work requires that the work is the subject matter, and there is no preponderance. The benefit to the hirer is in the second (i.e., benefit as subject), and the benefit to the hired is in the first (i.e., work as subject), so it leads to dispute. And it is narrated from Abu Hanifa that the ijarah is valid if he said 'fi al-yawm' and he specified a work, because 'fi' is for the container, so the work becomes the subject matter, unlike his saying 'al-yawm'. And a similar example has passed in divorce. Translation: Whoever hires a man to bake for him these ten sa' of flour today for one dirham, then it is fasid, and this is according to Abu Hanifa. The Sahibayn said in the book of Ijarat that it is valid, because they make the work the subject matter and the mention of time for haste to validate the contract, so ignorance is removed. Abu Hanifa's proof is that the subject matter is unknown because mentioning time requires the benefit to be the subject matter, and mentioning work requires the work to be the subject matter, and there is no preponderance. The hirer's benefit is in the second and the hired's benefit in the first, so it leads to dispute. And from Abu Hanifa it is narrated that the ijarah is valid if he says 'fi al-yawm' and he specified a work, because 'fi' indicates container, so the work becomes the subject matter, unlike his saying 'al-yawm'. And a similar example has passed in divorce. Commentary on his saying 'And whoever hires a man...' - Makhatim is the plural of makhtum, which refers to a sa' (measure). Evidence from hadith of Abu Sa'id al-Khudri: 'al-wasaq sittun makhtuman' - a sa' is called makhtum because its mouth is sealed so that it does not increase. In al-Mabsut it is said that makhtum and qafiz are the same thing. In the phrase 'li-yakhbiza lahu hadhihi al-ashrata al-makhatim', the word 'hadhihi' is the object of the verb 'yakhbiza', and 'al-ashrata' is its adjective, and 'al-makhatim' is in the genitive case due to idafa, like 'al-khamsata al-thawabi' where 'athwab' is genitive according to the Basrans' view, and 'al-yawm' is accusative as an adverb of time, and 'bi-dirham' is attached to 'ista'jara'.
Source pages p. 75

Commentary
This passage presents a classical intra-Hanafi dispute over a specific ijarah: hiring a baker to bake ten sa' of flour 'today' (al-yawm) for one dirham. The issue is jahalah: does the word 'al-yawm' specify the time of the work or the benefit? If it specifies the time of the benefit (that the oven's benefit is for one day), then the contract is for benefit, and the work is not specified. If it specifies the time when the work must be done, then the work is the subject matter. Abu Hanifa's position (with his student) that the contract is fasid because there is ambiguity: 'al-yawm' could refer to either the time of the work or the time of the benefit, leading to potential dispute. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) argue that 'al-yawm' is mentioned to indicate urgency, and the work is the subject matter, so the contract is valid. There is also a narration from Abu Hanifa that if the phrase is 'fi al-yawm' (within the day) and the work is specified, then the contract is valid because 'fi' makes it clear that the work is the subject matter and time is only a container. This nuance is similar to a divorce case. The commentary also explains the term 'makhatim' as a sealed measure of grain.

Key Terms
مختوم (makhtum): A sealed measure (sa') used for grain; same as qafiz.
جہالت (jahalah): Uncertainty or ambiguity in the subject matter or wage that renders a contract invalid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, why is the ijarah to bake ten sa' of flour 'today' for one dirham considered fasid?
A) Because the wage is unknown.
B) Because the time reference 'today' is impossible to fulfill.
C) Because 'today' could refer either to the time of the benefit (using the oven) or the time of the work (baking), creating ambiguity.
D) Because the baker did not specify the type of bread.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi ijarah, the precise wording of time specifications can determine validity; 'al-yawm' may be ambiguous in some constructions, while 'fi al-yawm' removes ambiguity.

Partnership in Wood Collection: Wage for Tying Bundles
Intra-Hanafi dispute on bundle-tier wage.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Imam Muhammad and Imam Abu Yusuf on the wage for a partner who only ties bundles in a wood-collection partnership and explain the practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf).

Core Idea
Fair wage without cap (Muhammad) vs. capped at half wood value (Abu Yusuf) — a core Hanafi intra-madhab dispute.

This lesson examines a classic intra-Hanafi dispute on partnership compensation. Two partners agree to collect wood: one collects, the other only ties bundles. The wood belongs to the collector. The bundle-tier is entitled to a fair wage (ujrat al-mithl), but how much? Imam Muhammad says the full fair wage without cap; Imam Abu Yusuf argues it cannot exceed half the wood's value because the partner implicitly consented to that limit. Understanding this disagreement sharpens your ability to apply principles of implied consent and unspecified wages.

Guided Path
1
Identify the partnership scenario
Two people agree to collect wood. One actually collects the wood, the other only ties bundles. Determine who owns the wood and what the bundle-tier is entitled to.
Wood belongs to the collector; bundle-tier gets a wage, not a share.
2
State the two positions
Imam Muhammad: full ujrat al-mithl without cap. Imam Abu Yusuf: ujrat al-mithl capped at half the wood's value.
Both agree on ujrat al-mithl but differ on the cap.
3
Trace each imam's proof
Muhammad: no specified wage (ujrat musamma), so reduction is not justified. Abu Yusuf: entering a partnership implies agreement to share the output, so the bundle-tier implicitly consented to half the wood's value.
Muhammad relies on the absence of a specified wage; Abu Yusuf on implicit consent from the partnership agreement.
4
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf
If the fair wage exceeds half the wood's value, Muhammad gives more than half; Abu Yusuf caps it at half. The practical consequence depends on the market rate for bundle-tying.
The difference only appears when ujrat al-mithl > half wood value.
5
Note the tarjih
The text does not specify which position is relied upon (mufta bihi). Both are recorded as valid Hanafi views.
In later fatwa practice, one may be preferred depending on context.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله وهذا بخلاف ما اذا اشتركا .. الخ - حکم مذکور اس صورت کے خلاف ہے جب دو شخصوں نے لکڑیاں چننے میں شرکت کی پھر ایک نے جنگل میں لکڑیاں چنیں اور دوسرے نے صرف گٹھے باندھے۔ تو لکڑیوں کا مالک چننے والا ہوگا۔ اور گٹھے باندھنے والے کو صرف اجر مثل ملے گا۔ لیکن یہ اجرت امام محمد کے نزدیک جتنی بھی ہو پوری ملے گی ۔ کیونکہ یہاں کوئی اجرت مسمی معلوم نہیں ہے تو گھٹانا صیح نہ ہوا۔ اور امام ابو یوسف کے نزدیک شرکت کی وجہ سے وہ لکڑیوں کی آدھی قیمت پر راضی ہو گیا تھا۔ تو اجر مثل ان لکڑیوں کی آدھی قیمت سے زیادہ نہیں دیا جائے گا اور اگر ان دونوں نے لکڑیاں چنیں اور دونوں نے گٹھے بھی باندے تو دونوں برابر کے شریک ہوں گے۔
He said: And this is contrary to the case where two people participated in gathering wood... etc. - The mentioned ruling is contrary to the case when two persons partnered in collecting wood, then one collected wood in the forest and the other only tied bundles. So the owner of the wood will be the one who collected, and the one who tied bundles will receive only the fair wage. But this wage, according to Imam Muhammad, will be given in full whatever it is, because here there is no specified wage known, so reduction is not correct. According to Imam Abu Yusuf, due to the partnership, he had agreed to half the value of the wood, so the fair wage will not exceed the half value of that wood. And if both collected wood and both tied bundles, then both will be equal partners.
Source pages p. 75

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Muhammad and Imam Abu Yusuf regarding a partnership in wood collection. The case: two people agree to collect wood together. One actually collects the wood, the other only ties the bundles. The wood belongs to the collector. The bundle-tier is entitled to a fair wage (ujrat al-mithl). Imam Muhammad holds he gets the full fair wage regardless, because no specific wage was agreed and reducing it is not justified. Imam Abu Yusuf argues that by entering the partnership, the bundle-tier implicitly agreed to half the value of the wood, so his fair wage cannot exceed that amount. If both had collected and both tied bundles, they are equal partners. The text is a commentary on a brief matn.

Key Terms
اجر مثل (ujrat al-mithl): The fair wage determined by the market for similar work, without any agreed amount
اجرت مسمی (ujrat al-musammā): A specifically agreed-upon wage stated in the contract

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the wood-collecting partnership, if one collects and the other only ties bundles, what is the ruling on the wage for the bundle-tier according to Imam Muhammad?
A) He gets nothing because he didn't collect
B) He gets a fair wage without cap
C) He gets half the value of the wood
D) He gets the same share as the collector

Key Takeaway
In a partnership where one party works and the other only services, the service provider receives a fair wage; whether it is capped depends on the imam's view on implied consent from partnership.

Ijarah — Hire and Lease
intermediate
10 min
Hiring to Bake Ten Sa' Today for One Dirham: Fasid or Sahih?
Intra-Hanafi dispute on validity of hiring with time condition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why Abu Hanifa considers this ijara fasid while the Sahibayn deem it sahih, and identify the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf).

Core Idea
Ambiguity in subject matter invalidates ijara; interpreting time as haste cures it.

When a hirer says 'bake today for a dirham', the contract's subject matter becomes unclear: is it the baker's time or the baked goods? Abu Hanifa sees fatal ambiguity; Sahibayn see a permissible acceleration clause. This lesson unpacks their reasoning and its practical effect.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Scenario and Core Dispute
The contract combines a specific work (baking 10 sa') and a specific time (today), causing potential conflict in determining the subject matter (ma'qud alayh).
2
State Abu Hanifa's Position and His Dalil
Abu Hanifa rules the contract fasid because the mention of time suggests the subject matter is the benefit (manfa'ah), while the mention of work suggests it is the labor. This conflict creates jihalah (ambiguity) leading to inevitable dispute.
He also narrates an exception for 'fi al-yawm' (within the day).
3
State the Sahibayn's Position and Their Dalil
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad rule the contract sahih by taking the work as the subject matter and interpreting the time mention as isti'jal (acceleration) to validate the contract, thus removing jihalah.
The three imams (non-Hanafi) agree with the Sahibayn.
4
Analyze the Narration from Abu Hanifa Allowing 'fi al-yawm'
When the phrase 'fi al-yawm' is used, time is treated as a mere container (zarf) for the work, so the subject matter is clearly the work, making the contract valid even according to Abu Hanifa.
This shows that wording matters: 'al-yawm' vs 'fi al-yawm'.
5
Apply the Rule of Order: Mention of Wage First
Later scholars derived that if the wage is mentioned before the time and work, the contract is valid; if the time or work comes before the wage, it is fasid. This rule is extracted from examples like 'ista'jartuka al-yawm bidirham...' vs '...al-yawm bidirham'.
The order resolves the apparent conflict between work and time.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ایک آدمی کو اجارہ پر لیا تا کہ وہ دس صاع آٹا پکائے ایک درہم کے عوض اجارہ فاسد ہے
قال ومن استاجر رجلا ليخبز له هذه العشرة المخاتيم اليوم بدرهم فهو فاسد وهذا عند ابي حنيفة وقال ابویوسف ومحمد فى الاجارات هو جائز لانه يجعل المعقود عليه عملا ويجعل ذكر الوقت للاستعجال تصحيحا للعقد فترتفع الجهالة وله ان المعقود عليه مجهول لان ذكر الوقت يوجب كون المنفعة معقودا عليها وذكر العمل يوجب كونه معقودا عليه ولا ترجيح ونفع المستاجر في الثاني ونفع الأجير في الأول فیفضى الى المنازعة وعن ابي حنيفة انه يصح الاجارة اذا قال فى اليوم وقد سمّى عملا لانه للظرف فكان عقود عليه العمل بخلاف قوله اليوم وقد مر مثله في الطلاق
ترجمہ جس نے اجارہ پر لیا کسی کو تا کہ پکائے اس کے لئے یہ دس صاع آٹا آج کے دن ایک درہم کے عوض تو یہ فاسد ہے۔ اور یہ امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک ہے اور صاحبین نے اجارت میں کہا ہے کہ یہ جائز ہے کیونکہ عمل کو معقود علیہ اور ذکر وقت کو برائے استعمال ٹھہر الیا جائے گا۔ عقد کو صحیح کرنے کے لئے پس جہالت اٹھ جائے گی۔ امام ابو حنیفہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ معقود علیہ مجہول ہے۔ اس لئے کہ بیان وقت واجب کرتا ہے منفعت کے معقود علیہ ہونے کو اور ذکر عمل واجب کرتا ہے کام کے معقود علیہ ہونے کو اور کسی کو ترجیح ہے نہیں اور مستاجر کا نفع دوسری صورت میں ہے اور اجیر کا نفع پہلی صورت میں ہے۔ پس یہ جھگڑے تک پہنچائے گا۔ اور امام ابوحنیفہ سے روایت ہے کہ اجارہ صحیح ہوگا۔ جب اس نے فی الیوم کہا ہو اور کام بیان کر دیا ہو۔ کیونکہ یہ ظرف کے لئے پس معقود علیہ عمل ہوا۔ بخلاف اس کے قول الیوم کے اور اسکے مثل طلاق میں گزر چکا۔
تشریح قوله ومن استاجر رجلا .. الخ - مخا تیم مختوم کی جمع ہے صاع کو کہتے ہیں ۔ جس کی شاہد حدیث ابوسعید خدری الوسق ستون مختوما صاع کو مختوم اس لئے کہتے ہیں کہ اس کے منہ کو مہر زد کر دیا جاتا ہے تا کہ بڑھے گھئے نہیں ۔ مبسوط میں ہے کہ مختوم اور قفیز ایک ہی چیز ہے۔ قول میں لفظ هذه ليخبر فعل کا مفعول ہے۔ اور العشرۃ اس کی صفت ہے۔ اور الخا تیم مجرور بالا ضافہ ہے جیسے الخمسة الا ثواب میں اثواب کو فین کی رائے پر مجرور ہے اور الیوم بناء بر ظرفیت منصوب ہے اور بدرھم استاجر سے متعلق ہے۔
مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ زید نے کسی نان بائی کو اس لئے اجرت پر لیا تا کہ وہ آج کے دن ایک درہم کے عوض میں دس صاع آٹے کی روٹی پکا دے تو امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک یہ اجارہ فاسد ہے اور مبسوط کی کتاب الاجارات میں صاحبین کے نزدیک جائز ہے ائمہ ثلاثہ بھی اسی کے قائل ہیں۔
قوله لانه يجعل المعقود عليه ... الخ - صاحبین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ اس عقد کو صحیح کرنے کے لئے عمل کو معقود علیہ ٹھہرالیا جائے گا۔ یہاں تک کہ اگر وہ آدھے دن میں بھی کام سے فارغ نہ ہوا تو آئندہ کل کے دن اس کو کام کرنا لازم ہوگا۔ بہر کیف معقود علیہ اس کا عمل ہے اور عمل معلوم ہے تو عقد جائز ہوگا ۔ کیونکہ اب یہ اشتباہ نہیں رہا کہ معقود علیہ عمل ہے یا وقت اس لئے کہ ہم نے اس کے عمل کو معقود علیہ قرار دے کر بیان وقت کو صرف جلدی کی غرض سے رکھا ہے یعنی یہ کام بعجلت تمام ایک ہی دن میں کر دے۔
قوله وله ان المعقود علیہ الخ - امام ابو حنیفہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ یہاں معقود علیہ مجہول ہے۔ اور معقود علیہ کا مجبول ہو نا مفسد عقد ہوتا ہے۔ لہذا عقد اجارہ صحیح نہ ہو گا جہالت معقود علیہ کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ مستاجر نے عمل اور وقت دونوں کو جمع کر دیا اب وقت کا مذکور ہونا تو یہ ثابت کرتا ہے کہ معقود علیہ منفعت ہے اور عمل کا مذکور ہونا یہ بتلاتا ہے کہ معقود علیہ عمل ہے۔ اور ان دونوں پر عمل کرنا ناممکن ہے اس لئے کہ معقود علیہ اگر عمل ہو تو کام کئے بغیر اجرت واجب نہ ہوگی۔ اور اگر معقود علیہ منفعت ہو تو اسیر جب خود کو پیش کر دے تو اجرت واجب ہوگی۔ اگر چہ اس نے کچھ کام نہ کیا ہو۔ اور اس سلسلہ میں لوگوں کے مقاصد مختلف ہوتے ہیں تو وقت و عمل میں سے کوئی ایک معقود علیہ ہونے کے لئے متعین نہیں ہوسکتا۔ کیونکہ تعارض موجود ہے اور ترجیح مفقود، پھر عمل کے معقود علیہ ہونے میں مستاجر کا نفع ہے اور منفعت کے معقود علیہ ہونے میں اجیر کا نفع ہے تو یقیناً بعد میں منازعت پیش آئے گی۔ اس واسطے کہ دن گزرنے پر نان پز اپنی پوری اجرت طلب کرے گا۔ اگر چہ دس صاع آٹا پکانے کا کام پورا نہ ہوا ہو۔ اور مستاجر اس کام کو معقود علیہ ہرا کر کام پورا ہوئے بغیر اجرت دینے سے انکار کرے گا تو جھگڑا ہوگا۔
قوله لان ذكر الوقت ..... الخ - جانا چاہیئے کہ اگر نان پر کو ایک من آٹا پکانے کے لئے بائیں شرط اجارہ پر لیا کہ اس کام سے آج ہی فارغ ہو جائے تو یہ اجارہ بالا لجماع جائز ہے کیونکہ اسمیں وقت شرط ہے نہ کہ معقود علیہ، اور اگر کسی درزی کو بایں طورا چارہ پر لیا کہ اگر تو اس کو آج ہی سی دے تو ایک درہم ملے گا۔ اور اگر کل سیئے گا تو نصف درہم ملے گا تو امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک شرط اول جائز ہوگی۔ اور وقت کا بیان صرف استعمال ( جلدی) کے لئے ہو گا بقرینہ شرط دوم۔
پھر بعض حضرات نے ذکر وقت کے برائے استعمال اور براے بیان وقت ہونے کا ضابطہ یہ بیان کیا ہے کہ وقت و عمل دونوں کو ذکر کرنے سے عقد اس وقت فاسد ہو گا جب ان کو بیان اجرت سے پہلے ذکر کرے اوراگر ان میں سے کسی ایک کو ذکر کر کے اسی کے ساتھ اجرت ذکر کر دی ( حتی تم العقد ) اس کے بعد دوسرے کو ذکر کیا تو عقد فاسد نہ ہوگا۔ مثلاً اگر اس نے یوں کہا۔ ”استاجر تك اليوم بدرهم على ان تخبز لى هذا القفيز من الدقیق تو عقد جائز ہوگا اور اگر اس نے یہ کہا ۔ استاجر تك لتخبز لى هذا القفيز من الدقيق اليوم بدهم یا یوں کہا۔ استاجر تك اليوم لتخبز لي هذا الدقيق بدرهم تو اس صورت میں عقد فاسد ہوگا۔
Literal: A man hired someone to bake ten sa' of flour today for one dirham; the hiring is fasid. This is according to Abu Hanifa. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad in Kitab al-Ijarat say it is valid because they consider the work as the subject matter and consider the mention of time as for acceleration to validate the contract, so ignorance is removed. And for him (Abu Hanifa) the subject matter is unknown because mentioning time necessitates benefit being the subject matter, and mentioning work necessitates work being the subject matter, and there is no preference. The benefit of the hirer is in the second, and the benefit of the hired is in the first, so it leads to dispute. And from Abu Hanifa it is reported that the hire is valid if he said "in the day" and specified work, because it is for the container, so the subject matter is work, contrary to his saying "today". Its like has passed in divorce. Translation: Whoever hired someone to bake these ten sa' today for one dirham, it is fasid, and this is according to Abu Hanifa. The Sahibayn said in Ijarat: it is valid because work is made the subject matter and mention of time is for acceleration to correct the contract, so ignorance is removed. Abu Hanifa's proof: the subject matter is unknown because mentioning time requires benefit to be the subject matter and mentioning work requires work to be the subject matter, and there is no preference. The hirer's benefit is in the second and the hired's benefit is in the first, so it leads to dispute. And from Abu Hanifa it is narrated that the hire is valid if he said "in the day" and specified work, because it is for (indicating) the container, so the subject matter becomes work, contrary to his saying "today". Its example has passed in divorce. Commentary: The word makhateem is plural of makhtum meaning sa'. Evidence from hadith of Abu Sa'eed al-Khudri: al-wasuq sittuna makhtuman. A sa' is called makhtum because its mouth is sealed so it does not increase. Al-Mabsut says makhtum and qafiz are the same. In the saying, the word "hadhihi" is the object of the verb "liyakhbiz", and "al-asharah" is its adjective, and "al-makhatim" is genitive due to idafah, like "al-khamsata athwabin" where "athwabin" is genitive according to the Basran view, and "al-yawma" is accusative as a container, and "bidirham" is connected to "ista'jara". The issue: Zaid hired a baker to bake ten sa' of flour today for one dirham. According to Abu Hanifa this hiring is fasid; in Mabsut's Kitab al-Ijarat, according to the Sahibayn it is valid, and the three Imams also hold this. He said: Because he makes the subject matter... Sahibayn's proof: to correct this contract, work will be considered the subject matter, so even if he does not finish in half the day, he must complete it tomorrow. In any case, his work is the subject matter and the work is known, so the contract is valid because there remains no confusion whether the subject matter is work or time, since we have taken his work as subject matter and placed mention of time only for haste. He said: And for him (Abu Hanifa) the subject matter... Abu Hanifa's proof: the subject matter here is unknown, and the subject matter being unknown invalidates the contract. The reason for ignorance is that the hirer combined work and time. The mention of time proves that the subject matter is benefit, and the mention of work shows that the subject matter is work. Acting upon both is impossible because if the subject matter is work, wages are not due without doing the work; if the subject matter is benefit, wages are due as soon as the hired person presents himself, even if he does nothing. People's objectives differ, so neither time nor work can be determined as subject matter because of conflict and lack of preference. Then, if work is subject matter, the hirer benefits, and if benefit is subject matter, the hired benefits, so dispute will certainly arise: at the end of the day the baker will demand full wage even if he didn't bake all ten sa', and the hirer will refuse to pay without full work. He said: Because mention of time... It should be known that if a baker was hired on condition to finish today, the hire is valid by consensus because time here is a condition, not subject matter. And if a tailor was hired such that if he sews today he gets one dirham, if tomorrow half dirham, then according to Abu Hanifa the first condition is valid and time mention is for acceleration due to the second condition. Then some scholars stated a rule for whether time mention is for acceleration or for specification: when both time and work are mentioned, the contract is fasid if they are mentioned before the wage; but if one of them is mentioned with the wage first (tam al-aqd) and then the other, the contract is not fasid. For example, if he said "I hire you today for one dirham to bake for me this qafiz of flour", the contract is valid; if he said "I hire you to bake for me this qafiz of flour today for one dirham" or "I hire you today to bake for me this flour for one dirham", then the contract is fasid.
Source pages p. 75

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute (Abu Hanifa vs. Sahibayn) regarding the validity of an ijara (hiring) contract where the hirer says: "I hire you to bake these ten sa' of flour today for one dirham." The key issue is whether mentioning a specific time (today) along with the work (baking) creates ambiguity in the subject matter (ma'qud alayh) and thus makes the contract fasid. Abu Hanifa holds it is fasid because the mention of time suggests the subject matter is the benefit (manfa'ah) of the baker's availability, while the mention of work suggests it is the actual baking. These conflict, leading to potential dispute. Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold it is sahih (valid) because the time mention is interpreted as a condition for acceleration (isti'jal), not as part of the subject matter; thus the work is the sole subject matter. They argue that by taking time as a mere container (zarf) for haste, the ignorance (jihala) is removed. The text also reports a narration from Abu Hanifa that if the phrase "fi al-yawm" (within the day) is used instead of just "al-yawm" (today), the contract is valid because it clearly treats time as a container. Later, scholars derive a rule: if both time and work are mentioned together before mentioning the wage, the contract is fasid; but if one is mentioned with the wage first (completing the contract) and then the other, it is valid. Examples illustrate this: correct order: "I hire you today for one dirham to bake this qafiz" – valid; incorrect order: "I hire you to bake this qafiz today for one dirham" – fasid. The passage includes linguistic analysis of the Arabic terms (makhateem, qafiz).

Key Terms
معقود علیہ (ma'qud alayh): The subject matter of the contract; what the parties have agreed upon. In ijara, it is either the benefit (manfa'ah) or the specific work.
منفعت (manfa'ah): The benefit or usufruct derived from the hired person's availability or skill, as opposed to the specific output (work).
جہالت (jihālah): Ambiguity or ignorance regarding an essential term of the contract, which can render the contract fasid.
استعمال (isti'jāl): Acceleration or urging haste; a legal device where a time mention is interpreted as a condition for speed, not as part of the subject matter.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), why is the contract to bake ten sa' today for one dirham valid despite mentioning a time?
A) Because time is considered the subject matter
B) Because work is made the subject matter and time is for acceleration
C) Because the wage is fixed
D) Because both work and time are equally valid as subject matter

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi ijara, ambiguity (jihalah) in the subject matter can be resolved by interpreting time references as acceleration, not as part of the subject matter.

The Baker Dispute: Intra-Hanafi Ikhtilaf on the Subject Matter in Ijarah
Intra-Hanafi dispute on ijarah with action and time

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on the validity of an ijarah contract that mentions both action and time, and explain the talil behind each position.

Core Idea
When both action and time are mentioned in ijarah, the subject matter becomes ambiguous, leading to an intra-madhhab dispute.

In Hanafi fiqh, the validity of an ijarah contract hinges on the clarity of its subject matter (ma'qud 'alayh). When a contract mentions both a specific action and a time frame, a question arises: which is the actual subject matter? This lesson examines a classic intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn over hiring a baker to bake today. By understanding their differing talil, you will gain deeper insight into the importance of ma'qud 'alayh in contracts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed case
Zaid hires a baker to bake ten sa' of bread today for one dirham. The contract mentions both the action (baking) and the time (today).
2
State the two Hanafi positions
Imam Abu Hanifa rules the ijarah fasid (void) because the subject matter is unknown. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) rule it ja'iz (valid).
3
Analyze Abu Hanifa's talil
Abu Hanifa argues that combining action and time creates ignorance (jahalah) about what is the actual subject matter. If action is the subject matter, wages are due only after work; if time/benefit is the subject matter, wages are due upon mere availability. This conflict leads to inevitable dispute, so the contract is fasid.
4
Analyze the Sahibayn's talil
The Sahibayn consider the action as the subject matter and time only as a condition for urgency (isti'jal). Thus the subject matter is known, and the contract is valid. If the baker does not finish today, he must complete the work later.
5
Apply the rule of precedence
Later scholars formulated a rule: if both action and time are mentioned before specifying the wage, the contract is fasid; if the wage is specified with one of them first, the contract is ja'iz. This resolves ambiguity based on word order.
This rule is illustrated with examples in the text: saying 'I hire you today for one dirham to bake' is valid, while 'I hire you to bake today for one dirham' is fasid.
