مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ زید نے کسی نان بائی کو اس لئے اجرت پر لیا تا کہ وہ آج کے دن ایک درہم کے عوض میں دس صاع آٹے کی روٹی پکا دے تو امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک یہ اجارہ فاسد ہے اور مبسوط کی کتاب الاجارات میں صاحبین کے نزدیک جائز ہے ائمہ ثلاثہ بھی اسی کے قائل ہیں۔

قوله لانه يجعل المعقود عليه ... الخ - صاحبین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ اس عقد کو صحیح کرنے کے لئے عمل کو معقود علیہ ٹھہرالیا جائے گا۔ یہاں تک کہ اگر وہ آدھے دن میں بھی کام سے فارغ نہ ہوا تو آئندہ کل کے دن اس کو کام کرنا لازم ہوگا۔ بہر کیف معقود علیہ اس کا عمل ہے اور عمل معلوم ہے تو عقد جائز ہوگا ۔ کیونکہ اب یہ اشتباہ نہیں رہا کہ معقود علیہ عمل ہے یا وقت اس لئے کہ ہم نے اس کے عمل کو معقود علیہ قرار دے کر بیان وقت کو صرف جلدی کی غرض سے رکھا ہے یعنی یہ کام بعجلت تمام ایک ہی دن میں کر دے۔

قوله وله ان المعقود علیہ الخ - امام ابو حنیفہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ یہاں معقود علیہ مجہول ہے۔ اور معقود علیہ کا مجبول ہو نا مفسد عقد ہوتا ہے۔ لہذا عقد اجارہ صحیح نہ ہو گا جہالت معقود علیہ کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ مستاجر نے عمل اور وقت دونوں کو جمع کر دیا اب وقت کا مذکور ہونا تو یہ ثابت کرتا ہے کہ معقود علیہ منفعت ہے اور عمل کا مذکور ہونا یہ بتلاتا ہے کہ معقود علیہ عمل ہے۔ اور ان دونوں پر عمل کرنا ناممکن ہے اس لئے کہ معقود علیہ اگر عمل ہو تو کام کئے بغیر اجرت واجب نہ ہوگی۔ اور اگر معقود علیہ منفعت ہو تو اسیر جب خود کو پیش کر دے تو اجرت واجب ہوگی۔ اگر چہ اس نے کچھ کام نہ کیا ہو۔ اور اس سلسلہ میں لوگوں کے مقاصد مختلف ہوتے ہیں تو وقت و عمل میں سے کوئی ایک معقود علیہ ہونے کے لئے متعین نہیں ہوسکتا۔ کیونکہ تعارض موجود ہے اور ترجیح مفقود، پھر عمل کے معقود علیہ ہونے میں مستاجر کا نفع ہے اور منفعت کے معقود علیہ ہونے میں اجیر کا نفع ہے تو یقیناً بعد میں منازعت پیش آئے گی۔ اس واسطے کہ دن گزرنے پر نان پز اپنی پوری اجرت طلب کرے گا۔ اگر چہ دس صاع آٹا پکانے کا کام پورا نہ ہوا ہو۔ اور مستاجر اس کام کو معقود علیہ ہرا کر کام پورا ہوئے بغیر اجرت دینے سے انکار کرے گا تو جھگڑا ہوگا۔

قوله لان ذكر الوقت ..... الخ - جانا چاہیئے کہ اگر نان پر کو ایک من آٹا پکانے کے لئے بائیں شرط اجارہ پر لیا کہ اس کام سے آج ہی فارغ ہو جائے تو یہ اجارہ بالا لجماع جائز ہے کیونکہ اسمیں وقت شرط ہے نہ کہ معقود علیہ، اور اگر کسی درزی کو بایں طورا چارہ پر لیا کہ اگر تو اس کو آج ہی سی دے تو ایک درہم ملے گا۔ اور اگر کل سیئے گا تو نصف درہم ملے گا تو امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک شرط اول جائز ہوگی۔ اور وقت کا بیان صرف استعمال ( جلدی) کے لئے ہو گا بقرینہ شرط دوم۔

پھر بعض حضرات نے ذکر وقت کے برائے استعمال اور براے بیان وقت ہونے کا ضابطہ یہ بیان کیا ہے کہ وقت و عمل دونوں کو ذکر کرنے سے عقد اس وقت فاسد ہو گا جب ان کو بیان اجرت سے پہلے ذکر کرے اوراگر ان میں سے کسی ایک کو ذکر کر کے اسی کے ساتھ اجرت ذکر کر دی ( حتی تم العقد ) اس کے بعد دوسرے کو ذکر کیا تو عقد فاسد نہ ہوگا۔ مثلاً اگر اس نے یوں کہا۔ ”استاجر تك اليوم بدرهم على ان تخبز لى هذا القفيز من الدقیق تو عقد جائز ہوگا اور اگر اس نے یہ کہا ۔ استاجر تك لتخبز لى هذا القفيز من الدقيق اليوم بدهم یا یوں کہا۔ استاجر تك اليوم لتخبز لي هذا الدقيق بدرهم تو اس صورت میں عقد فاسد ہوگا۔

قوله ولا ترجیح ... الخ - اس پر کوئی یہ کہہ سکتا ہے کہ ذکر عمل کو مقدم کرتا اس امر کے لئے مرچ ہو سکتا ہے کہ عمل معقود علیہ ہے۔ جیسا کہ فقہاء نے مسئلہ رائی میں کہا ہے کہ اگر مستاجر نے مدت اور عمل دونوں کے ذکر کو جمع کر دیا تو ان میں سے جس کو مقدم ذکر کرے اسی کا اعتبار ہوگا۔
Book of Ijarah. 75. The issue is that Zaid hired a baker to bake ten sa' of flour into bread today for one dirham. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, this ijarah is fasid. In the Mabsut's book of Ijarah, according to the Sahibayn, it is ja'iz, and the three Imams also hold this view. Statement: 'because he makes the subject matter...' etc. - The Sahibayn's argument: To validate this contract, the action is considered as the subject matter. So if he does not finish the work in half the day, he must complete it the next day. In any case, the subject matter is his action, and the action is known, so the contract is valid. Because now there is no confusion whether the subject matter is action or time, since we have made his action the subject matter and mentioned time only for urgency. Statement: 'and his argument that the subject matter...' etc. - Imam Abu Hanifa's argument: Here the subject matter is unknown. The subject matter being unknown invalidates the contract. Therefore, the ijarah contract will not be valid. The reason for the ignorance of the subject matter is that the musta'jir combined both action and time. Now, the mention of time indicates that the subject matter is manfa'ah, and the mention of action indicates that the subject matter is action. It is impossible to act on both because if the subject matter is action, wages are not due without work, and if the subject matter is manfa'ah, wages are due when he presents himself even if he did no work. People's objectives differ, so neither time nor action can be determined as the subject matter because there is conflict and no preference. Then, if action is the subject matter, the musta'jir gains; if manfa'ah, the ajir gains, so conflict will certainly arise. When the day passes, the baker will demand full wages even if he did not complete baking ten sa', and the musta'jir will refuse to pay until the work is complete. Statement: 'because the mention of time...' etc. - It should be known that if a baker is hired to bake one maund of flour with a condition to finish today, this ijarah is valid by consensus because time is a condition, not the subject matter. If a tailor is hired with the condition: if you sew today, you get one dirham; if tomorrow, half a dirham, then according to Imam Abu Hanifa the first condition is valid, and the mention of time is only for urgency, indicated by the second condition. Then some scholars have stated a rule: when both time and action are mentioned, the contract is fasid if they are mentioned before stating the wage; if one is mentioned and the wage is tied to it, and then the other is mentioned afterward, the contract is not fasid. For example, if he said: 'I hire you today for one dirham to bake this qafiz of flour' - the contract is valid. But if he said: 'I hire you to bake this qafiz of flour today for one dirham' or 'I hire you today to bake this flour for one dirham' - then the contract is fasid. Statement: 'and no preference...' etc. - Someone might say that mentioning action first could give preference to action as the subject matter, as the jurists have said in the case of ra'i: if the musta'jir combined both time and action, whichever he mentions first is considered.
Source pages p. 76

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning the validity of an ijarah contract where both a specific action and a time limit are mentioned. The case: Zaid hires a baker to bake ten sa' of flour into bread today for one dirham. Imam Abu Hanifa rules this ijarah fasid (void) because the subject matter (ma'qud alayh) is unknown – the contract mentions both the action (baking) and the time (today), and it is unclear which is the actual subject matter. This ignorance leads to invalidity. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) rule it ja'iz (valid) because they take the action as the subject matter, considering the time only as a condition for urgency. If the baker does not finish, he must complete it later. The passage then discusses a tailor case with two different wages for different timeframes, where Abu Hanifa validates the first condition due to context. Finally, a rule from some scholars is given: the order of mentioning time and action relative to the wage matters. If both are mentioned before the wage, the contract is fasid; if the wage is tied to one first, then the other is mentioned, it is valid. The passage ends with an objection that mentioning action first should give preference, but the author does not resolve it here.

Key Terms
اجارہ (ijarah): A contract of hire or lease where one party provides a benefit (manfa'ah) in exchange for compensation (ujrah).
معقود علیہ (ma'qud 'alayh): The subject matter of the contract – the thing or benefit that is the object of the transaction. In ijarah, it is the benefit (manfa'ah) or the work (amal).
مستاجر (musta'jir): The person who hires or leases – the employer in an ijarah contract.
اجیر (ajir): The person hired to provide work or service – the employee or worker.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, why is the ijarah contract for a baker (to bake today) considered fasid?
A) Because the baker's work is unknown.
B) Because both time and action are mentioned, causing ignorance of the subject matter.
C) Because the wage is unknown.
D) Because the baker cannot finish in one day.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi ijarah, the clarity of the subject matter is paramount; when both action and time are mentioned, the validity hinges on whether time is treated as a condition or as part of the subject matter, leading to an intra-madhhab ikhtilaf.

Ijarah — Hire and Lease

Hiring Land for Cultivation: Valid and Void Conditions
Ruling on validity of agricultural ijarah conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between valid conditions (muqtadayat al-'aqd) and void extra-benefit conditions in an ijarah contract for land, and apply the Hanafi standard of 'effect remaining after term'.

Core Idea
A condition necessary for the contracted purpose is valid; one that leaves lasting benefit for the lessor is void as a second transaction.

In this passage, the author explains a key Hanafi rule for agricultural ijarah: only conditions that are inherent to the contract are valid. Additional conditions like double-plowing or fertilizing are void because they confer extra benefit after the lease term. Understanding this distinction prevents invalid contracts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is hiring land for cultivation with specific conditions. Determine which conditions lead to validity (jaiz) and which to invalidity (fasid).
The ruling distinguishes between necessary agricultural conditions and extra ones.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites the principle that agriculture cannot be done without plowing and irrigation, so those conditions are muqtadayat. Extra conditions like double-plowing are prohibited because they create two transactions in one (صفقتان في صفقة).
The hadith 'نهى عن صفقتين في صفقة' is implicit.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The proof links: (a) Necessity makes the condition valid; (b) Extra benefit that remains after the term makes it invalid as it becomes a separate transaction for the lessor's benefit.
The key is whether the condition's effect persists beyond the lease period.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
The passage does not mention other madhhabs, but the Hanafi position is clear and authoritative.
Cross-madhhab comparisons are not provided here.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The mufta bihi is that basic agricultural conditions are valid; extra conditions like tathniyah (where benefit remains) are void. Clarifications are given for longer leases where benefit may not remain.
This ruling is from Zahir al-Riwayah.

قوله ومن استاجر ارضا على ان يكربها ويزرعها ويسقيها فهو جائز لان الزراعة مستحقة بالعقد ولا يتاتى الزراعة الا بالسقى والكراب فكان كل واحد منهما مستحقا وكل شرط هذه صفته يكون من مقتضيات العقد فذكره لا يوجب الفساد فان شرط ان يُشنيها او يكرى انهارها او يُسرقنها فهو فاسد لانه يبقى اثره بعد انقضاء المدة وانه ليس من مقتضيات العقد وفيه منفعة لاحد المتعاقدين وما هذا حاله يوجب الفساد ولان مواجر الأرض يصير مستاجرا منافع الاجير على وجه يبقى بعد المدة فيصير صفقتان في صفقة وهو منهى عنه ثم قيل المراد بالتثنية ان يردها مكروبة ولا شبهة فى فساده وقيل ان يكربها مرتين وهذا في موضع يُخرج الأرض الريع بالكراب مرة والمدة سنة واحدة وان كانت ثلث سنين لا يبقى منفعة وليس المراد بكرى الانهار الجداول بل المراد منها الانهار العظام هو الصحيح لانه يبقى منفعته في العام القابل

توضيح اللغة.... يكر بها (ن) كرباً زمین جو نا۔ يسقيها (ض) سقیاً سینچنا، سیراب کر نایشنیها تثنية دوباره کرنا بیکری (ض) كرياً نہر کھودتا ۔ يسر قنھا کھاد ڈالنا۔ اثر نشان۔ ریع ، سرسبز پیداوار ۔ جد اول جمع جدول نالی۔

ترجمہ کسی نے اجارہ پر لی زمین بایں شرط کہ اس کو جوئے ، کاشت کرے اور پہنچے گا۔ تو یہ جائز ہے اس لئے کہ عقد سے زراعت کا استحقاق ہوا اور زراعت نہیں ہو سکتی مگر سینچنے اور جو تنے سے تو ان میں سے ہر ایک مستحق ہوا اور ہر وہ شرط جس کی صفت یہ ہو وہ عقد کے مقتضیات میں سے ہوتی ہے پس اسکا ذکر کرنا موجب فسادنہ ہوگا۔ ہاں اگر یہ شرط لگائی کہ زمین کو مکرر بوئے یا اسکی نہریں اگارے یا اس میں کھاد ڈالے تو یہ شرط فاسد ہے۔ کیونکہ اس کا اثر مدت گزرنے کے بعد بھی رہتا ہے۔ اور یہ مقتضیات عقد میں سے بھی نہیں ہے اور اس میں احد المتعاقدین کا نفع بھی ہے اور جس شرط کا یہ حال ہو وہ موجب فساد ہو گی۔ اور اس لئے بھی کہ زمین اجارہ پر دینے والا اجیر کے منافع اجرت پر لینے ولا ہوگا ۔ ایسے طریقہ پر کہ اس کی منفعت بعد مدت کے باقی رہتی ہے تو یہ عقد گویا ایک صفقہ میں دو صلتے ہو گئے حالانکہ یہ ممنوع ہے۔ پھر کہا گیا ہے کہ تنثنیہ سے مراد یہ ہے کہ حل چلائی ہوئی زمین واپس کرلے اور اس کے فساد میں کوئی شک نہیں ۔ اور کہا گیا ہے کہ اس سے مراد یہ ہے کہ دوبارہ جوت کر زراعت کرے تو حکم فساد ایسے مقام میں ہوگا جہاں ایک ہی مرتبہ گوڑنے سے پیداوار حاصل ہوتی ہو اور مدت اجارہ بھی ایک سال ہو۔ اگر مدت تین سال ہو تو اس کی منفعت باقی نہیں رہ سکتی اور نہر میں اگارنے سے مراد نالیاں نہیں ہیں بلکہ اس سے بڑی نہریں مراد ہیں۔ یہی صحیح ہے۔ کیونکہ اس کی منفعت آئندہ سال تک باقی رہتی ہے۔

تشریح قوله ومن استاجر ارضاً.. الخ - زید نے ایک زمین بایں شرط ٹھیکہ پر لی کہ اس میں بھل جو توں گا اور اس کو پینچ کر کھیتی کروں گا تو یہ درست ہے۔ کیونکہ عقد اجارہ سے اس کو زراعت کا استحقاق ہوا ہے اور زراعت ہل جوتے اور سینچے بغیر نہی ہوسکتی تو ہل جوتنا
Statement: 'Whoever hires land with the condition that he plows it, sows it, and irrigates it, it is valid because agriculture is due by the contract, and agriculture cannot be achieved except by irrigation and plowing. So each of these is due, and every condition of this nature is among the requirements of the contract, so mentioning it does not cause invalidity. But if he conditions that he double-plows it, or digs its canals, or fertilizes it, it is void because its effect remains after the term ends, it is not among the requirements of the contract, and it contains benefit for one of the two parties. Such a condition causes invalidity. Also because the lessor of the land becomes a hirer of the worker's benefits in a way that the benefit remains after the term, thus two transactions in one, which is prohibited. It is said that 'tathniyah' means that he returns it plowed, and there is no doubt about its invalidity. And it is said that it means he plows it twice, and this is in a place where the land yields produce with one plowing, and the lease term is one year. If the term is three years, the benefit does not remain. And the intended meaning of digging canals is not small channels but large rivers, this is correct because their benefit remains for the coming year.'

Language clarification...

Translation: Someone hired land with the condition that he plow it, sow it, and irrigate it – this is valid because the contract gives the right to agriculture, and agriculture cannot be done without plowing and irrigating, so each is due. Every condition of this nature is from the requirements of the contract, so mentioning it does not invalidate. However, if he conditions that he double-plows, or digs its canals, or fertilizes it, this condition is void because its effect remains after the term, it is not from the requirements of the contract, and it contains benefit for one of the two parties, so it causes invalidity. Also because the lessor becomes a hirer of the worker's benefits in a way that the benefit remains after the term, thus two transactions in one, which is prohibited. Then it is said that 'tathniyah' means that he returns it plowed, and there is no doubt about its invalidity. And it is said that it means he plows it twice, and the ruling of invalidity applies in a place where produce is obtained with one plowing and the lease term is one year. If the term is three years, its benefit does not remain. And the intended meaning of digging canals is not small channels but large rivers, this is correct because its benefit remains until the next year.

Explanation of statement: 'Whoever hires land...' – Zaid hired land with the condition that he plow it and irrigate it and sow it – this is valid because the ijarah contract gives him the right to agriculture, and agriculture cannot be done without plowing and irrigating, so plowing is included.
Source pages p. 77

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof concerning the validity of conditions in an ijarah contract for land. The ruling: If someone hires land with the conditions that he plows, sows, and irrigates it, the contract is valid because these actions are necessary for agriculture, which is the contracted purpose. Such conditions are considered inherent requirements (muqtadayat) of the contract. However, if he stipulates additional conditions like double-plowing (tathniyah), digging large canals (yakri anharaha), or fertilizing (yusarqinaha), the contract becomes fasid (invalid). The reason: these conditions leave a benefit that persists after the lease term ends, they are not required by the contract, and they confer an extra benefit to one party (the lessor). This constitutes two transactions in one (safqatani fi safqah), which is prohibited. The passage then clarifies that 'tathniyah' may mean returning the land plowed (which is obviously invalid) or plowing twice, which is invalid only when a single plowing suffices for the season and the lease is for one year; if the lease is longer (e.g., three years), the benefit may not remain, and thus the condition might be valid. Regarding digging canals, it refers to large rivers whose benefit lasts beyond the term, not small irrigation channels. The explanation emphasizes that the key factor is whether the condition's effect remains after the term and whether it is necessary for the contracted purpose.

Key Terms
تنثنیہ (tathniyah): Double-plowing or returning the land plowed; a condition that requires the lessee to plow the land twice or leave it plowed after the term.
مقتضیات عقد (muqtadayat al-'aqd): The inherent requirements of a contract – actions that are naturally necessary to fulfill the contracted purpose.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is a condition to fertilize the land in an ijarah contract considered void?
A) Because fertilization is not necessary for agriculture.
B) Because the benefit of fertilization remains after the lease term, conferring extra benefit to the lessor.
C) Because fertilization damages the land.
D) Because the lessee cannot afford fertilizer.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi ijarah, conditions necessary for the intended use are valid; conditions that give lasting extra benefit to the lessor are void because they create a second transaction.

Leasing Land with Conditions: Valid and Invalid Stipulations
States ruling on valid and invalid conditions in land lease with proof from two-transactions prohibition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between valid and invalid conditions in a land lease and apply the Hanafi criteria (muqtadayat al-aqd vs. extra benefit) to new scenarios.

Core Idea
Lease conditions that are part of the contract's requirements are valid; conditions that give lasting extra benefit to the lessor make the lease corrupt.

This passage from al-Hidayah clarifies which conditions in a land lease are valid and which render the contract corrupt (fasid). The key distinction is whether the condition is necessary for the contracted purpose or whether it provides an enduring benefit to the lessor beyond the lease term. Understanding this distinction helps prevent contracts that fall into the prohibited category of 'two transactions in one.'

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling on basic lease conditions
State that stipulating plowing, sowing, and watering is permissible (ja'iz). These acts are necessary for cultivation, which is the purpose of the lease.
2
Understand why they are valid
These conditions are muqtadayat al-aqd (requirements of the contract). Mentioning them does not add extra benefit; they are inherent to the contracted obligation.
3
Identify the invalid conditions
Stipulating tathniyah (doing work twice), digging large canals, or fertilizing (yusrqinaha) is corrupt (fasid).
4
Understand the reason for invalidity
The benefit of these conditions lasts beyond the lease term, giving extra advantage to the lessor without compensation. This effectively creates a separate hire transaction, which is prohibited as safqatayn fi safqa (two transactions in one).
The hadith 'Nahi Rasulullah صلى الله عليه وسلم an safqatayn fi safqa wahida' is cited.
5
Clarify the nuances
Tathniyah may be valid if the land requires multiple plowings or the term is longer; digging canals distinguishes large canals (invalid) from small streams (jadaawil, temporary, valid).
The benefit assessment depends on whether the effect remains after the lease.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال ومن استاجر ارضا على ان يكربها ويزرعها ويسقيها فهو جائز لان الزراعة مستحقة بالعقد ولا يتاتى الزراعة الا بالسقى والكراب فكان كل واحد منهما مستحقا وكل شرط هذه صفته يكون من مقتضيات العقد فذكره لا يوجب الفساد فان شرط ان يُثنيها او يكرى انهارها او يُسرقنها فهو فاسد لانه يبقى اثره بعد انقضاء المدة وانه ليس من مقتضيات العقد وفيه منفعة لاحد المتعاقدين وما هذا حاله يوجب الفساد ولان موجر الارض يصير مستاجرا منافع الاجير على وجه يبقى بعد المدة فيصير صفقتين في صفقة وهو منهى عنه ثم قيل المراد بالتثنية ان يردها مكروبة ولا شبهة فى فساده وقيل ان يكربها مرتين وهذا في موضع يُخرج الارض الريع بالكراب مرة والمدة سنة واحدة وان كانت ثلث سنين لا يبقى منفعة وليس المراد بكرى الانهار الجداول بل المراد منها الانهار العظام هو الصحيح

ثم قوله فان شرط ان يثنيها ... الخ - اور اگر یہ شرط کی کہ زمین پھیرتے وقت پھر ہل جوتے یا مکرر ہل جوتے یا اس کی نہریں اگارے یا اس میں کھاد ڈالے تو اس صورت میں اجارہ فاسد ہو گا۔

نهى رسول الله صلى الله عليه و سلم عن صفقتين في صفقة واحدة

تنبیہ: شیخ سعدی چلی نے کہا ہے کہ لان موجر الارض اھ اصل مدعی کی دوسری دلیل ہے لہذا ولان موجر الارض واو کے ساتھ ہونا چاہیے (چنانچہ بعض نسخوں واو موجود ہے) لیکن صاحب نتائج نے لان موجر الارض کو وما هذا حاله يوجب الفساد کی دلیل مانا ہے نہ کہ اصل مدعی کی، فالظاهر ترک الواو۔
He said: Whoever leases land on condition that he plows it, sows it, and waters it - it is permissible, because cultivation is owed by the contract, and cultivation is only possible with watering and plowing, so each of them is owed. And every condition of this description is among the requirements of the contract, so mentioning it does not cause corruption. If he stipulates that he will do it twice, or dig its canals, or fertilize it, then it is corrupt because its effect remains after the expiry of the term, and it is not from requirements of the contract, and there is benefit for one of the two contracting parties, and whatever has this state causes corruption. And because the lessor of the land becomes the hirer of the worker's benefits in a manner that remains after the term, so it becomes two transactions in one transaction, which is prohibited. Then it is said: The meaning of tathniyah is that he returns it plowed, and there is no doubt in its corruption. And it is said: that he plows it twice, and this is in a place where the land yields produce with one plowing, and the lease term is one year; if it is three years, the benefit does not remain. And the meaning of digging canals is not the small streams, but rather the large canals - that is correct. Then his statement: If he stipulates that he will do it twice... And it is prohibited by the Prophet (peace be upon him) from two transactions in one transaction. Note: Sheikh Sa'di Chali said that 'because the lessor of the land' is the second proof of the original claimant, so it should be with a waw (and indeed in some copies the waw is present), but the author of Nata'ij considered 'because the lessor of the land' as a proof for 'and whatever has this state causes corruption', not for the original claimant, so apparently the waw is omitted.
Source pages p. 77

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the Book of Ijarah in al-Hidayah. It first states the general principle: leasing land for plowing, sowing, and watering is valid because these acts are necessary for the contracted purpose (cultivation). The condition is considered part of the contract's requirements (muqtadayat al-'aqd), so it does not invalidate the lease. Then it contrasts invalid conditions: stipulating that the tenant will do the work twice (tathniyah), dig large canals, or fertilize the land. These are invalid because their benefit extends beyond the lease term, they are not required by the contract, and they provide a benefit to the lessor (owner) without additional consideration. The proof is twofold: (1) any condition that gives extra benefit to one party invalidates the contract (based on the prohibition of conditional benefits in leases), and (2) such a condition makes the lessor effectively hire the tenant's labor for post-term benefit, which constitutes two transactions in one (safqatayn fi safqa), prohibited by a hadith. The passage then clarifies ambiguities: 'tathniyah' means plowing a second time, which is invalid only if one plowing suffices and the term is one year; if the land needs multiple plowings or the term is longer, it may be valid. 'Digging canals' refers to large canals whose benefit persists, not small streams that are temporary. A textual note discusses whether the word 'wa' (and) should appear in the phrase 'li-anna mujir al-ard' - some scholars consider it part of the second proof, others as an independent statement.

Key Terms
تثنية (tathniyah): Doing the work (e.g., plowing) twice; also interpreted as returning the land already plowed.
كرى الانهار (kari al-anhar): Digging or cleaning large canals whose benefit lasts beyond the lease term.
صفقتين في صفقة (safqatayn fi safqa): Two transactions combined into one contract, e.g., lease and separate hire.
مقتضيات العقد (muqtadayat al-aqd): Requirements of the contract; conditions inherently necessary for the contracted purpose.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is the condition of fertilizing the land (yusrqinaha) considered invalid in a land lease?
A) Because fertilizer is not mentioned in the contract terms
B) Because its benefit remains after the lease term ends, providing extra benefit to the lessor
C) Because it is a condition that contradicts the nature of ijara
D) Because the tenant must use his own fertilizer

Key Takeaway
Lease conditions that are necessary for the contracted purpose are valid; conditions that provide lasting extra benefit to the lessor render the contract corrupt (fasid) due to the prohibition of two transactions in one.

Leasing Land for Cultivating Another Land: The Riba-Like Barter of Usufructs
Presents dispute: bartering agricultural labor for land use

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school invalidates the barter of similar agricultural usufructs with deferment, and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument based on the commodity-like nature of usufructs.

Core Idea
Bartering the same genus of usufruct with deferment is invalid in Hanafi — it mirrors riba al-fadl.

This passage from al-Hidayah presents a key inter-madhhab dispute: can one lease land in return for cultivating another piece of land? At stake is whether bartering similar usufructs falls under riba. The Hanafi school, following Imam Muhammad, declares it invalid; Imam al-Shafi'i permits it. Understanding the Hanafi reasoning requires grasping the concept of jins (genus) and nasi'ah (deferment) in exchange contracts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed contract
The contract is leasing land for cultivating another land, i.e., barter of agricultural usufruct.
2
State the Hanafi position and its proof
Hanafi: invalid; proof: analogy to selling wheat for wheat with deferment (riba al-fadl).
The proof is qiyas jaliy.
3
Present the Shafi'i counter-argument
Shafi'i: permissible; usufructs are like commodities, so exchange is valid as a debt price.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The genus alone, when deferred, triggers prohibition. The analogy holds because the genus (jins) of usufruct is same.
Hanafi holds that jins alone prohibits nasi'ah.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Practically, Hanafi: contract void, must compensate. Shafi'i: contract valid and enforceable.
This difference affects legal transactions in daily life.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال: وان استاجرها ليزرعها بزراعة ارض اخرى فلا خير فيه وقال الشافعى هو جائز وعلى هذا اجارة السكنى بالسكنى واللبس باللبس والركوب بالركوب له ان المنافع بمنزلة الاعيان حتى جازت الاجارة باجرة دين ولا يصير دينا بدين ولنا ان الجنس بانفراده يحرم النساء عندنا فصار كبيع القوهى بالقوهى
He said: If he leases it to cultivate it with the cultivation of another land, there is no good in it. Al-Shafi'i said: It is permissible, and on this basis is the lease of dwelling for dwelling, clothing for clothing, riding for riding - because usufructs are like commodities such that lease is valid for a debt price, and it does not become debt for debt. For us, the genus alone is prohibited in sale (nasi'ah) according to us, so it becomes like selling wheat for wheat.
Source pages p. 78

Commentary
This passage presents an inter-madhhab dispute regarding leasing land in return for cultivating another land (i.e., barter of usufructs). The Hanafi position (Imam Muhammad's statement in the matn) is that it is invalid (la khayra fihi). Imam al-Shafi'i holds it is permissible. The Shafi'i argument: usufructs are like physical commodities, so leasing a house for a house or clothes for clothes is allowed; they analogize to a debt price (ajratun dayn) which does not become debt for debt. The Hanafi response: The genus (jins) alone, when exchanged for itself with deferment (nasi'ah), is prohibited based on riba al-fadl. This is analogous to selling wheat for wheat (with deferment), which is not allowed. Therefore, bartering one agricultural labor for another is invalid because it resembles riba.

Key Terms
اجارة السكنى بالسكنى (ijarat al-sukna bi al-sukna): Leasing a dwelling in exchange for a dwelling (barter of usufructs).
النساء (al-nasi'ah): Deferred sale or exchange where one or both countervalues are delayed.
بيع القوهى بالقوهى (bay' al-qawhi bi al-qawhi): Selling wheat for wheat (exchange of same genus).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because the land cannot be used as a price
B) Because it is an exchange of the same genus with deferment, akin to riba
C) Because the contract lacks a defined duration
D) Because Shafi'i allows it

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi, bartering the same genus of usufruct with deferment is invalid, analogized to selling wheat for wheat on credit.

Conditions That Make a Land Lease Contract Fasid
Explains conditions providing lasting benefit beyond lease term invalidate contract

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify conditions in land lease contracts that provide lasting benefit beyond the term and state why they render the contract fasid according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
A condition giving lasting benefit beyond the lease term makes the contract fasid – it resembles two transactions in one.

In Hanafi fiqh, not every stipulation in a lease contract invalidates it. The key is whether the condition provides a lasting benefit to the property owner beyond the lease period, and whether it is from the requirements of the contract. This passage from Al-Hidayah guides us to identify such conditions and understand the underlying reasoning based on the prohibition of two transactions in one.

Guided Path
1
Identify the conditions that cause fasid
From the passage, list the specific actions that, if stipulated, make the lease fasid: plowing again after the lease, digging large canals, and fertilizing. Note that these actions benefit the owner beyond the lease term.
These are explicitly mentioned as conditions that cause fasid.
2
Understand the rationale: lasting benefit and not from contract requirements
The contract is fasid because the condition provides a benefit that persists after the lease ends, and it is not a natural consequence of the lease (like normal cultivation). Such conditions are considered extraneous and benefit one party unfairly.
The passage states 'fā'idah wa athar ba'd muddat al-ijārah bāqī rahtā hai' – the benefit remains after the term.
3
Connect to the second proof: analogy to two transactions in one
The author draws an analogy to the prohibited 'ṣafqatayn fī ṣafqa' (two transactions in one). By stipulating a condition that provides lasting benefit, the lease effectively becomes two contracts: a lease and a separate transfer of benefit, which is impermissible based on the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud.
The hadith is cited from Musnad Ahmad: 'Nahā Rasūlallāh ṣallallāhu 'alayhi wa sallam 'an ṣafqatayn fī ṣafqatin wāḥidah'.
4
Apply the distinction between large canals and small channels
The passage distinguishes between large canals (nahar) whose benefit lasts beyond the term and small channels (jadwal) whose benefit does not. This illustrates that the ruling depends on whether the benefit outlasts the lease period.
Small channels are not considered lasting, so they do not cause fasid.

اور زمین سینچنا بھی مستحق بالعقد ہوا۔ اور یہ شرط مقتضائے عقد کے خلاف نہ ہوئی لہذا اعتقد اجارہ صحیح ہوگا۔ قوله فان شرط ان يثنيها ... الخ - اور اگر یہ شرط کی کہ زمین پھیرتے وقت پھر ہل جوتے یا مکر رہل جوتے یا اس کی نہریں اگارے یا اس میں کھاد ڈالے تو اس صورت میں اجارہ فاسد ہو گا اس لئے کہ ان امور کا فائدہ اور اثر مدت اجارہ گزرنے کے بعد بھی باقی رہتا ہے اور یہ مقتضیات عقد میں سے بھی نہیں ہے۔ پھر اس میں احد المتعاقدین یعنی مالک زمین کا فائدہ بھی ہے اور ایسی شرط موجب

تنبیہ شیخ سعدی چلی نے کہا ہے کہ لان موجر الارض اھ اصل مدعی کی دوسری دلیل ہے لہذاولان موجر الارض واؤ کے ساتھ ہونا چاہیئے (چنانچہ بعض نسخوں واؤ موجود ہے) لیکن صاحب نتائج نے لان موجر الارض احكووما هذا حاله يوجب الفساد کی دلیل مانا ہے نہ کہ اصل مدعی کی فالظاهر ترک الواؤ ۔
قوله ثم قيل المراد ... الخ - پھر تجمیۂ ارض سے مراد بقول عوض یہ ہے کہ مستاجر مالک زمین کا فائدہ ہے۔ اور بعض حضرات نے تعمیہ ارض کے یہ معنی کئے ہیں کہ زمین دوبارہ جوت کر زراعت کرے۔ اس صورت میں فاسد ہونے کا حکم ایسے مقام پر ہوگا۔ جہاں ایک ہی بار گوڑنے سے پیداوار حاصل ہو جاتی ہو اور عقد اجارہ کی مدت بھی ایک ہی سال ہو۔ اگر وہ زمین ایسے مقام پر ہو جہاں پیداوار حاصل ہونے کے لئے مکرر گوڑنے کی ضرورت ہو تو یہ شرط مفسد عقد نہ ہوگی بلکہ مقتضائے عقد ہوگی ۔ اسی طرح اگر مدت اجارہ تین سال ہو تب بھی عقد فاسد نہ ہوگا کیونکہ اس کی منفعت باقی نہیں رہ سکتی۔
قوله وليس المراد ... الخ اور نہریں اگا نے سے مراد چھوٹی نہریں یعنی الیاں اور بر سے نہیں ہیں بلکہ اسے بڑی نہریں مراد ہیں۔ کیونکہ اس کی منفعت آئندہ سال تک باقی رہتی ہے۔ صاحب ہدایہ نے عوایح کہہ کر شیخ الاسلام خواہر زادہ کے قول سے احتراز کیا ہے کہ انہار سے مراد جداول ( نالیاں) ہیں چنانچہ وہ انہا و جداول دونوں کو یکساں کہتے اور اسی کا فتویٰ دیتے تھے۔ صاحب محیط نے بھی اسی کو اختیار کیا ہے۔ وجہ احتراز یہ ہے کہ نالیوں کی منفعت مدت اجارہ کے بعد تک باقی نہیں رہ سکتی تو اس میں سے بظاہر کوئی وجہ
فساد نہیں ہے۔
The text discusses conditions in land lease contracts. If the lessee stipulates to plow again, dig canals, or fertilize after the lease term, the contract is fasid because the benefit lasts beyond the term and contradicts the contract's requirement. The second proof: the owner thus leases usufruct that extends beyond the term, resembling two transactions in one, which is prohibited as narrated by Ibn Mas'ud: the Prophet forbade two transactions in one. A note: some scholars interpret that the phrase 'then it is said' refers to different interpretations of 'tajmiyat al-ard'. The intended meaning of 'digging canals' is large canals whose benefit lasts, not small channels.
Source pages p. 78

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the Hidayah sharh. It explains that if a lease contract includes conditions like plowing again, digging canals, or fertilizing, which provide lasting benefit to the owner after the term, the contract becomes fasid. The reason is that such conditions are not from the requirements of the contract and benefit only one party. The second proof compares it to two transactions in one, citing a hadith from Ibn Mas'ud. It also clarifies that if the land requires multiple plowings within the lease term, the condition is valid. Large canals (nahar) cause fasid, but small channels (jadwal) do not, as their benefit does not last.

Key Terms
فساد (fasād): Voidable contract that is not valid due to an illegal condition, but can be corrected by removing the condition or paying ujrat al-mithl.
صفقتين في صفقة (ṣafqatayn fī ṣafqa): Two transactions combined into one, which is prohibited.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Stipulating that the lessee will water the land
B) Stipulating that the lessee will plow again after the lease ends
C) Stipulating that the lessee will cultivate the land
D) Stipulating a monetary rent

Key Takeaway
A condition providing lasting benefit to the lessor beyond the lease term, not required by the contract, makes the lease fasid in the Hanafi school.

Leasing Land in Exchange for Cultivating Another Land
Dispute on leasing land with a usufruct of the same genus as payment

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school prohibits leasing land in exchange for cultivating another land of the same genus and compare it to the Shafi'i position.

Core Idea
Exchanging same-genus usufructs in ijarah is invalid; the single genus triggers riba prohibition.

This lesson examines a key dispute between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools regarding ijarah: Is it valid to lease land with payment being the cultivation of another land of the same type? The Hanafi school holds it invalid, drawing an analogy to the prohibition of riba al-nasi'ah. The Shafi'i school allows it, treating usufructs like physical assets. Understanding the reasoning behind each position is essential for mastering the fiqh of ijarah.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
According to Imam Muhammad, there is no good in leasing land to be cultivated in exchange for cultivating another land. This means the contract is not permissible (fasid).
The Arabic phrase 'لا خير فيه' indicates prohibition.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Imam al-Shafi'i and Imam Malik hold that such a lease is permissible. They extend this to other similar usufruct exchanges: residence for residence, wearing for wearing, riding for riding.
These are called 'اجارة المنافع بالمنافع'.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
The Shafi'i proof is that usufructs are like physical assets (بمنزلة الأعيان), so exchanging them is akin to selling a share of a physical asset, which is permissible. Also, ijarah with deferred payment is valid, so it does not become debt-for-debt.
This is a qiyas on physical property.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response has two parts: (1) The single genus alone prohibits nasi'ah (delay) in exchange, making it analogous to selling one type of cloth for the same type on credit, which is prohibited due to riba. (2) Ijarah was permitted against qiyas only due to need; when the genus of usufruct is the same, there is no need, so the original prohibition applies.
The analogy to 'بيع القوهى بالقوهى' is key.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
In practice, if someone leases land and pays the rent by cultivating the lessor's other land of the same type, the contract is void according to Hanafi, but valid according to Shafi'i. The Hanafi view is relied upon for fatwa in the Hidayah.
This difference has real implications for agricultural contracts.

قال وان استاجرها ليزرعها بزراعة ارض اخرى فلا خير فيه وقال الشافعى هو جائز وعلى هذا اجارة السكنى بالسكنى واللبس باللبس والركوب بالركوب له ان المنافع بمنزلة الاعيان حتى جازت الاجارة باجرة دين ولا يصير دينا بدين ولنا ان الجنس بانفراده يحرم النساء عندنا فصار كبيع القوهى بالقوهى

Ruling on leasing land to cultivate it in exchange for cultivating another land. He said: If one leases land to cultivate it in exchange for cultivating another land, there is no good in it. Al-Shafi'i said it is permissible, and similarly leasing residence for residence, wearing for wearing, riding for riding. His proof: usufructs are like physical assets, so leasing is valid even with deferred payment, and it does not become debt for debt. Our proof: the single genus alone prohibits delay (nasi'ah) according to us, so it becomes like selling one type of cloth for the same type on credit. Also, ijarah was granted exception from qiyas only due to need; when the genus of usufruct is the same, there is no need.
Source pages p. 78

Commentary
This is an inter-madhhab dispute. The Hanafi position is that leasing land in exchange for cultivating another land (i.e., paying rent with a similar usufruct) is not permissible. Al-Shafi'i and Malik allow it, analogizing usufructs to physical assets, and arguing that deferred payment is allowed in ijarah. The Hanafi response is that the single genus makes it analogous to selling one commodity for the same commodity on credit, which is prohibited due to riba. Further, ijarah is allowed against qiyas only for need; when the genus of usufruct is the same, there is no need, so the original prohibition by qiyas applies.

Key Terms
منافع (manāfi‘): Usufructs, the benefits derived from an asset, considered here as non-physical.
بيع القوهى بالقوهى (bay‘ al-quhī bi al-quhī): Selling one type of cloth for the same type on credit, prohibited due to riba al-nasi'ah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the Hanafi school prohibit leasing land in exchange for cultivating another land of the same type?
A) Because it involves debt for debt
B) Because the single genus makes it analogous to selling one commodity for the same commodity on credit, which is riba
C) Because the contract is not in writing
D) Because the land is not owned by the lessor

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school prohibits leasing land with similar usufruct as rent because it resembles riba al-nasi'ah, even though ijarah is normally flexible.

Hiring a Co-owner to Carry His Share: Hanafi vs Shafi'i
Ruling on hiring a co-owner to carry his specific share but carrying all

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school denies a wage to a co-owner who carries all jointly-owned grain, and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
Physical acts cannot be performed on an undivided share; delivery of a share's work is impossible.

When two partners jointly own grain, can one hire the other to carry only his share? If the hired partner ends up carrying all the grain, what wage is due? The Hanafi and Shafi'i schools differ sharply. In this lesson, we examine the legal reasoning behind each position and its practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling: the hired co-owner receives no wage (fala ajr lahu).
2
Identify the opposing view and its basis
Imam al-Shafi'i says he gets the named wage because usufruct is considered an asset ('ayn) in his school, and selling a share is permissible.
Opponent: Shafi'i
3
Analyse the Hanafi proof (dalil)
Hanafi proofs: (1) Carrying is a physical act that cannot be imagined on a share; (2) every part carried is partly his own, so he works for himself; (3) delivery (taslim) is impossible.
Key concept: taslim of a share of a physical act is impossible.
4
Distinguish from analogous cases
Unlike hiring a shared house (where usufruct can be delivered without possession), here the act is physical and cannot be split.
The analogy to a shared house fails.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical difference: Hanafi says no wage; Shafi'i says full wage. The Hanafi position is relied upon for fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
دو شخصوں کے مشترک اناج میں ایک نے دوسرے شریک کو یا اس کے گدھے کو بایں شرط اجارہ پر لیا آسکا حصہ اٹھائے اس نے کل اناج اٹھا کر پہنچا دیا اس کے لئے کچھ اجرت نہ ہوگی
قال و اذا كان الطعام بين رجلين فاستاجر احدهما صاحبه او حمار صاحبه على ان يحمل نصيبه فحمل الطعام كله فلا اجر له وقال الشافعى له المسمى لان المنفعة عين عنده وبيع العين شائعا جائز فصار كما اذا استاجر دارا مشتركة بينه وبين غيره ليضع فيها الطعام او عبدا مشتركا ليخيط له الثياب ولنا انه استاجره العمل لا وجود له لان الحمل فعل حسى لا يتصور فى الشائع بخلاف البيع لانه تصرف حكمى واذا لم يتصور تسليم المعقود عليه لا يجب الاجر ولان ما من جزء يحمله الا وهو شريك فيه فيكون عاملا لنفسه فلا يتحقق التسليم بخلاف الدار المشتركة لان المعقود عليه هنالك المنافع ويتحقق تسليمها بدون
In joint grain between two men, one hires the other or his donkey to carry his share, but he carries all the grain; he has no wage. Al-Shafi'i said he gets the named wage because usufruct is an asset in his school, and selling a share of an asset is permissible, so it is like hiring a shared house to store food or a shared slave to sew clothes. Our proof: he hired work that has no existence, because carrying is a physical act that cannot be imagined on a share; unlike a sale which is a legal disposition. When delivery of the contracted object is not possible, wage is not obligatory. Also, every part he carries, he is a partner in it, so he works for himself; delivery is not realized. Unlike a shared house, because there the contracted object is usufructs, and delivery is realized without possession.
Source pages p. 79

Commentary
This is an inter-madhhab dispute. The Hanafi ruling is that if two partners jointly own grain, and one hires the other (or his donkey) to carry his specific share, but ends up carrying all the grain, he receives no wage. Al-Shafi'i says he receives the named wage, reasoning that usufruct is like a physical asset, and selling a share of a physical asset is permissible. The Hanafi response: carrying is a physical act that cannot be performed on a share; hence delivery is impossible. Also, every part he carries is jointly owned, so he works for himself in part. This differs from hiring a shared house or slave, where the object is usufruct (like space or work) that can be delivered without possession of the asset.

Key Terms
شائع (shā'i‘): Undivided share in joint ownership; here, the grain is shā'i‘, and carrying of a share is not possible physically.
تسليم (taslīm): Delivery of the contracted object; required for wage obligation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the case of joint grain, why does the Hanafi school deny the wage to the partner who carried all the grain?
A) Because he did not complete the work
B) Because the work is a physical act that cannot be performed on an undivided share, and he works for himself
C) Because the contract was not in writing
D) Because the grain was not his property

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, physical acts cannot be performed on an undivided share, so a co-owner hired to work on his specific share receives no wage if he works on the whole, as every part is partly his own.

Ijarah of Land with Same-Type Benefit: Hanafi Ruling of Fasid
Inter-madhhab dispute on ijarah with same-type benefit

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that ijarah with a same-type benefit is fasid, explain the riba-based analogy, and distinguish the Hanafi position from the Shafi'i/Maliki view.

Core Idea
Ijarah of like-for-like benefits is fasid due to analogy with prohibited credit sale.

This lesson examines a key dispute between the Hanafi school and the Shafi'i/Maliki schools regarding ijarah (leasing) when the rental payment is a benefit of the same kind as the leased benefit. The Hanafis rule it invalid (fasid) because it resembles a prohibited sale of debt for debt (riba al-nasi'ah). Understanding the reasoning clarifies the boundaries of valid ijarah contracts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core scenario
Recognize the disputed transaction: leasing land for cultivation in exchange for cultivating another land. The rent is a benefit of the same type (cultivation).
2
State the Hanafi ruling
The Hanafi ruling is fasid (invalid). The contract is not void (batil) but defective; it cannot be enforced.
The Hanafis analogize this to selling a commodity for the same commodity on credit, which is prohibited due to riba.
3
Identify the opposing view
Imam al-Shafi'i and Imam Malik consider it valid. Their evidence: benefits are like physical objects ('ayn).
4
Analyze the Hanafi counter-evidence
The Hanafis respond that mere same genus plus deferment (nasī'ah) is sufficient to trigger the riba prohibition. Ijarah was permitted against analogy only due to necessity, and when benefits are same type, necessity is absent.
This is a qiyas khafi (hidden analogy) based on the operative cause (illa) of riba.
5
Determine the practical effect
Under Hanafi law, the contract is fasid and will not be upheld in a Hanafi court. Under Shafi'i/Maliki law, it is valid and enforceable.
This is the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence of the disagreement).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الاجارات نسيئة والى هذا اشار محمد ولان الاجارة جوزت بخلاف القياس للحاجة عند اتحاد الجنس بخلاف ما اذا اختلف جنس المنفعة.
ترجمہ اگر زمین اجارہ پر لی تاکہ اس میں کاشت کرے دوسری زمین کی کاشت کے عوض تو اس میں کوئی بہتری نہیں ہے۔ امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں کہ یہ جائز ہے اور اسی اختلاف پر ہے رہائش کا اجارہ رہائش کے عوض اور پہننے کا اجارہ پہننے کے عوض اور سواری کا اجارہ سواری کے عوض ۔ امام شافعی کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ منافع بمنزلہ اعیان کے ہیں۔ یہاں تک کہ اجارہ ۔ قرض اجرت پر جائز ہوتا ہے اور دین کا عوض دین سے نہیں ہوتا۔ ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ تنہا جنس ادھار کو حرام کر دیتی ہے ہمارے نزدیک پس یہ تو ہستانی کپڑے کو قوہستانی کپڑے کے عوض ادھار فروخت کرنے کی طرح ہو گیا۔ امام محمد نے اس کی طرف اشارہ کیا ہے اور اس لئے کہ اجارہ کو خلاف قیاس صرف ضرورت کی وجہ سے جائز رکھا گیا ہے اور اتحاد جنس کے وقت کوئی ضرورت نہیں ہے بخلاف اس کے جب جنس منفعت مختلف ہو۔ تشریح قوله وان استاجرها .... الخ - زید نے بکر کی زمین کاشت کے لئے اس شرط پر لی کہ اس کے عوض میں وہ زید کی زمین کاشت کرے گا تو اس میں کوئی خیر نہیں۔ یعنی نا جائز ہے۔ امام مالک اور امام شافعی کے نزدیک جائز ہے۔ اسی طرح اگر کسی نے اپنا گھر کرایہ پر دیا اور اجرت یہ طے ہوئی کہ کرایہ دار اپنا گھر مجھے رہنے کے لئے دے یا ایک لباس پہنے کو دوسرا لباس پہننے کے عوض یا ایک جانور کی سواری کو دوسرے جانور کی سواری کے عوض اجارہ پر لیا تو ان میں بھی یہی اختلاف ہے۔ امام شافعی کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ منافع بمنزلہ اعیان ہیں۔ یہاں تک کہ اجارہ قرض اجرت پر جائز ہو جاتا ہے اور یہ دین کا عوض دین سے نہیں ہوتا تو منع ہونے کی کوئی وجہ نہیں ہے۔ قوله ولنا ان الجنس ..... الخ - ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ اگر صرف جنسیت موجود ہو تو ہمارے نزدیک ادھار حرام ہو جاتا ہے تو ایسا ہو گیا جیسے توہستانی کپڑا تو ہستانی کپڑے کے عوض ادھار فروخت کیا جائے کہ یہ جائز نہیں لان احد وصفى علة الربوا كاف في حرمة النساء
Book of Ijarah (lease): On credit. And to this Imam Muhammad pointed. And because ijarah was permitted contrary to analogy due to need when the type is the same, unlike when the type of benefit differs. Translation: If land is taken on ijarah so that he cultivates it in exchange for cultivation of another land, then there is no good in it. Imam Shafi'i says it is permissible. And the same difference exists for ijarah of residence in exchange for residence, and wearing in exchange for wearing, and riding in exchange for riding. Imam Shafi'i's evidence: Benefits are like physical objects. So much so that ijarah on a loan of wages is permissible. And it is not debt in exchange for debt. Our evidence: mere same genus makes credit haram in our view. So this becomes like selling a Tustani cloth for a Qustani cloth on credit, which is not permissible because one of the two causes of riba is sufficient for prohibition of delay. Imam Muhammad indicated this. And because ijarah was permitted contrary to analogy only due to need, and when the genus is the same there is no need, unlike when the genus of benefit differs. Commentary on 'If he leases it...' - Zaid took Bakr's land for cultivation on condition that in exchange he will cultivate Zaid's land. There is no good in it, i.e., invalid. According to Imam Malik and Imam Shafi'i it is valid. Similarly if someone rents out his house and the rent is that the tenant gives his house for him to live, or a garment for wearing in exchange for another, or an animal for riding in exchange for another, then the same difference exists. Imam Shafi'i's evidence: Benefits are like physical objects; so much so that ijarah on a loan of wages is valid, and this is not debt in exchange for debt. Our evidence: If mere genus exists, then in our view credit is prohibited. So it becomes like selling a Tustani cloth for a Tustani cloth on credit, which is not permissible because one of the two causes of riba is sufficient for prohibition.
Source pages p. 79

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute regarding the validity of ijarah where the rental payment is in the form of a benefit of the same type as the leased benefit. The Hanafi position is that such a transaction is invalid (fāsid). The Shāfiʿī position considers it valid. Key scenario: A person leases land for cultivation, and the agreed rent is that he cultivates another person's land in return. The Hanafīs analogize this to selling a commodity for the same commodity on credit (e.g., cloth for cloth), which is prohibited due to ribā al-nasīʾa. Even though benefits are not actual physical objects, the same legal principle applies: when the genus of the benefit is identical, the transaction resembles bayʿ al-salam or sarf-like exchanges. The Hanafīs argue that ijarah was permitted contrary to analogy (khilāf al-qiyās) only due to necessity (ḥājah). When the benefits are of the same type, there is no necessity, so the original analogy—that ijarah is a contract of exchange—prevails, and it is invalid. The Shāfiʿīs counter that benefits are treated like physical objects ('ayn) in many contexts, and since the ijarah is not a sale of debt for debt (because both are current), it is valid. The text also notes that Imām Muḥammad (al-Shaybānī) indicated this ruling. The commentary expands by giving examples: residence for residence, wearing for wearing, riding for riding—all follow the same difference of opinion.

Key Terms
اجارہ (ijārah): A contract of leasing or hiring where one party provides a benefit (manfaʿah) in exchange for compensation (ujr).
نسيئة (nasīʾah): Credit/deferred payment; in this context, the ijarah payment is deferred.
منفعت (manfaʿah): Benefit or usufruct derived from an asset; the object of ijarah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why do Hanafis consider ijarah of a house in exchange for the tenant giving his own house as rent to be invalid?
A) Because houses cannot be rented for other houses.
B) Because the benefits are of the same type, resembling a sale of debt for debt which is prohibited.
C) Because the tenant does not own the house.
D) Because the rent must be in cash.

Key Takeaway
Ijarah where the rent is a benefit of the same type as the leased benefit is fasid in Hanafi law, analogized to prohibited credit sale of the same commodity.

Ijarah on Undivided Property: Partner Hiring Co-Partner to Carry His Share
Inter-madhhab dispute on ijarah of undivided property

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school invalidates an ijarah for carrying a partner's share from undivided grain, and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument using the distinction between physical acts and legal dispositions.

Core Idea
A physical act cannot be delivered in undivided property – the carrier always works for himself.

This lesson examines a classic inter-madhhab dispute: two partners share grain; one hires the other (or his donkey) to carry only his share, but the hired party ends up carrying all the grain. The Hanafi school rules that no wage is due, while Imam al-Shafi'i holds that the named wage is payable. The disagreement hinges on whether the contracted action can be delivered in undivided (shā'iʿ) property, and whether benefits are treated like physical objects (ʿayn). We will walk through both positions, proofs, and the key Hanafi distinction between physical acts (ḥissī) and legal dispositions (ḥukmī).

Guided Path
1
State the scenario and both positions
Read the case carefully: two partners own grain (food) jointly. One hires the other or his donkey to carry his own share. The hired party carries all grain. Identify the Hanafi ruling (no wage) and the Shafi'i ruling (named wage due).
Note that the hired party is himself a partner in the grain.
2
Identify the Hanafi proof
The Hanafi argument is that the contracted action (carrying only the other's share) is impossible to deliver because the grain is undivided. Each part the carrier moves includes his own share, so he works for himself. Delivery of the contracted object is not conceivable, so no wage is obligatory.
This is based on the principle that physical acts cannot be performed on undivided property in a way that isolates another's share.
3
Identify the Shafi'i proof and its analogies
Imam al-Shafi'i argues that benefits are like ʿayn (physical objects); selling an undivided ʿayn is valid. He draws analogies to hiring a shared house to store food or a shared slave to sew clothes – both are valid ijarah despite the property being undivided.
The Shafi'i position relies on the validity of benefit transfer in undivided property.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response to the analogies
The Hanafis distinguish: a shared house: the benefit (right to use space) can be delivered without physically dividing the house; a shared slave: the contracted matter is ownership of the other's share of the slave's labor, which is a legal (ḥukmī) concept that can be assigned even in undivided property. Carrying is a physical act that cannot be split – it is inherently tied to the whole load.
This distinction between physical acts and legal dispositions is the key to the Hanafi position.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf and mufta bihi
The practical consequence (thamarah): Hanafi – no wage; Shafi'i – named wage due. The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position in the Hanafi school is that no wage is due, as per Zahir al-Riwayah.
This ruling applies when the hired party is a partner; if a third party were hired, the case may differ.

He said: And if food (grain) is between two men, and one of them hires the other or the other's donkey on condition that he carries his share, but he carries all the food, then there is no wage for him. And al-Shafi'i said: He gets the named wage because benefit is like an 'ayn in his view, and selling an undivided 'ayn is valid, so it becomes as if he hired a shared house between him and another to put food in it, or a shared slave to sew clothes for him. Our evidence: He hired him for an action that has no existence; because carrying is a physical act (hissi) that cannot be imagined in something undivided (shā'i'), unlike sale because it is a legal disposition (hukmī). And if delivery of the contracted subject matter is not conceivable, wage is not obligatory. And also because no part of the grain does he carry except that he is a partner in it, so he is working for himself; thus delivery is not realized. Unlike the shared house because the contracted subject matter there is benefits (manāfi') and its delivery is possible without placing food. And unlike the shared slave because the contracted subject matter is only the ownership of the other's share, which is a legal matter that can occur in an undivided thing.
Source pages p. 79

Commentary
This passage presents an inter-madhhab dispute concerning a specific scenario: two partners share grain (food). One partner hires the other partner (or his donkey) to carry his (the first partner's) share, but the hired party ends up carrying all the grain (both shares). The Hanafī ruling is that no wage is due, while Imām al-Shāfiʿī holds that the named wage is due. The Hanafī reasoning is twofold: (1) The contracted action (carrying) is a physical act (hissī) that cannot be delivered in an undivided (shā'iʿ) property because it is impossible to segregate the carrier's own share from the other's. Since the grain is mixed, each part carried includes the carrier's own share, so he is working for himself regarding his share. Delivery of the contract object (carrying only the other's share) is impossible. (2) In contrast, if a shared house is hired to store food, the benefit (manfaʿah) is the right to use space, which can be delivered without physically dividing the house. Similarly, hiring a shared slave to sew clothes: the contracted benefit is the slave's work, and the ownership of the slave's labor is a legal concept that can be assigned even in an undivided slave. The commentary further explains that the Shāfiʿīs treat benefits as 'ayn (physical objects), so an undivided 'ayn can be sold; thus ijarah on an undivided benefit is valid. The Hanafī response distinguishes between physical actions and legal ownership: physical actions cannot be split, but legal ownership can.

Key Terms
شائع (shā'iʿ): Undivided, shared property (mushāʿ); a property where shares are not physically separated.
عمل حسى (ʿamal ḥissī): Physical action that is perceptible by the senses, such as carrying.
تصرف حكمى (taṣarruf ḥukmī): Legal/constructive disposition, such as sale, which transfers ownership without physical separation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why do Hanafīs say no wage is due when a partner hires his co-partner to carry his share but the carrier carries all grain?
A) Because the carrier did not complete the work.
B) Because the contracted action cannot be delivered in undivided property since the carrier is also a partner.
C) Because the wage was not specified.
D) Because a partner cannot hire his co-partner.

Key Takeaway
A contract for a physical act on undivided property is void if delivery cannot separate shares; the carrier is deemed to work for himself.

Ijarah — Hire and Lease

Hiring a Co-Owner for Joint Property: The Hanafi- Shafi'i Dispute
Ruling and dispute on hiring a partner for undivided grain

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on hiring a partner for undivided property, explain the reasoning based on impossibility of delivery, and distinguish it from valid hires of joint houses or slaves.

Core Idea
A hire contract for physical labor on jointly owned property is invalid; the worker acts for himself.

Can you hire your business partner to carry your share of their jointly owned grain? The Hanafi school says no—the contract is invalid and no wage is due. Imam Shafi'i disagrees, treating the benefit as akin to a chattel. This lesson unpacks the reasoning behind each position and the crucial distinction between physical acts and legal dispositions.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi ruling
Identify the exact Hanafi position: the hire contract is invalid (fasid) and no wage is owed.
The worker is a co-owner, so every part he carries includes his own share.
2
Identify the opposing view and its proof
Imam Shafi'i holds the contract valid; he analogizes to hiring a jointly owned house or slave where benefit can be delivered even in undivided property.
For Shafi'i, usufruct (manfa‘ah) is like a chattel, and sale of joint chattel is allowed.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response to the analogy
The Hanafi rebuttal: in a joint house, the subject is abstract benefits (can be delivered without occupying the whole); in a slave, it's ownership (a legal concept). Carrying grain is a physical act inseparable from the property.
Physical acts cannot be divided; each grain carried is partly the worker's own.
4
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
Hanafi: no wage at all (neither specified nor fair). Shafi'i: specified wage is due.
This difference has real financial impact.

تشریح قوله واذا كان الطعام ... الخ - کچھ اناج دو آدمیوں کے درمیان مشترک ہے ان میں سے ایک نے دوسرے شریک .الخ۔ کو یا اس کے گدھے کو اپنے حصہ کا اناج اٹھانے کے لئے اجارہ پر لیا اور اس نے کل اناج اٹھا کر پہنچا دیا تو ہمارے نزدیک اس کو مزدوری نہیں ملے گی نہ اجر سمی اور نہ اجر مثل ، ائمہ ثلاثہ کے نزدیک اجارہ مذکورہ بیج ہے اس لئے ان کے یہاں اٹھانے والے کو مقررہ مزدوری ملے گی ۔ وجہ یہ ہے کہ ان کے یہاں منفعت بمنزلہ عین ہے۔ اور مین مشاع کی بیع جائز ہے تو مشاع کا اجارہ بھی جائز ہوگا ۔ پس یہ ایسا ہو گیا جیسے اناج رکھنے کے واسطے مشترک مکان یا کپڑا سینے کے لئے مشترک غلام اجارہ پر لیا کہ اجرت واجب ہوتی ہے۔ قوله ولنا انه استاجره .... الخ - ہماری دلیل ہے کہ احد الشریکین نے دوسرے کو ایسے عمل کے لئے اجرت پر لیا ہے جس کا وجود غیر متمیز ہے۔ اسلئے کہ بوجھ اٹھانے کا عمل فعل حسی ہے جو امر شائع میں متصور نہیں ہوسکتا۔ پس تسلیم معقود علیہ غیر متصور ہوئی لہذا اجرت واجب نہ ہوگی ۔ بخلاف بیع کے کہ وہ تصرف حکمی (شرعی ) ہے نیز اس لئے بھی کہ اناج کا ہر وہ جز جس کو منتقل کیا ہے اس میں وہ خود بھی شریک ہے تو اپنے لئے عامل ہوا تو سپرد کر نا محقق نہ ہوگا۔ اس لئے اجرت واجب نہ ہوگی۔

Regarding food: and unlike the slave because the subject of contract is only the ownership of the partner's share and it is a legal matter that can take effect in joint property. Translation: Grain is shared between two persons. Then one of them hired the other partner or his donkey on condition that he carry his share. He carried all the grain and delivered it. So he gets no wage. Imam Shafi'i says he gets the specified wage because benefit in his view is like a chattel, and selling undivided chattel is permissible. So this becomes like hiring a house that is jointly owned for storing grain, or hiring a joint slave to sew cloth. Our proof is that he hired for an act that has no existence because carrying is a physical act that cannot be conceived in undivided property, unlike sale because it is a legal disposition. And when delivery of the subject matter is inconceivable, wage is not obligatory. Also because there is no part that he carries except that he is a partner in it, so he works for himself, thus delivery is not actualized. Unlike a joint house because the subject there is benefits that can be delivered without storing grain, and unlike a slave because the subject is only the other's share of ownership, which is a legal matter that can occur in joint property. Explanation of the saying 'and if the food...': Some grain is shared between two persons, one hired the other or his donkey to carry his share, and he carried all grain and delivered it. According to us, he gets no wage, neither specified nor fair wage. According to the three Imams, this hire is valid, so the carrier gets the specified wage. Reason: benefit in their view is like chattel, and sale of joint chattel is permissible, so hire of joint property is also permissible. It becomes like hiring a joint house for storing grain or a joint slave for sewing cloth where wage is obligatory. Our proof is that one co-owner hired the other for an act that is non-separable, because carrying is a physical act not conceivable in joint property. Thus delivery of subject matter is not actualized, so wage is not obligatory. Unlike sale which is a legal disposition. Also because every part of grain he moved, he himself is a partner in it, so he acts for himself, so delivery is not actualized. Regarding the house: It is a response to Imam Shafi'i's analogy that unlike a joint house where hire is valid because the subject is benefits that can be delivered without storing grain, so storing grain makes delivery even more possible. And unlike a joint slave where the subject is only the other's share of ownership, which is a legal matter that can occur in joint property.
Source pages p. 80

Commentary
This is an inter-madhhab dispute concerning the hire of a co-owner (or his donkey) to carry grain from jointly owned property. The Hanafi position is that the contract is invalid and no wage is due, while Imam Shafi'i and the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold it valid. The Hanafi proof rests on the nature of the usufruct: carrying is a physical act that cannot be separated from the joint property. Since the hired person is himself a co-owner, every part he carries includes his own share, so he works for himself and cannot deliver the service exclusively to the other. The opponent analogizes it to the hire of a joint house or slave, where the subject matter is abstract (benefits or ownership) and can be delivered even if undivided. The Hanafi response distinguishes physical acts from legal dispositions.

Key Terms
مشاع (mushāʿ): Undivided share in joint property.
منفعت (manfaʿat): Usufruct or benefit, treated as a chattel by Shafi'i but as a distinct property by Hanafi.
اجارہ (ijārah): Hire contract for a known usufruct in exchange for known wage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if two co-owners of grain and one hires the other to carry all the grain to market, what is the ruling?
A) The contract is valid and the worker gets the agreed wage.
B) The contract is invalid and no wage is due.
C) The contract is valid but only fair wage is due.
D) The contract becomes valid if the worker is a non-owner.

Key Takeaway
Hiring a co-owner for physical work on undivided property is invalid in Hanafi law because the service cannot be delivered exclusively; the worker acts for himself.

Land Lease Without Specifying Crop – Istihsan Validates
Ruling with proof: land lease, initial invalidity, istihsan validation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a land lease lacking specification of use or crop, explain the role of istihsan in validating it after cultivation and term expiry, and evaluate the opposing qiyas-based position held by Imam Zufar.

Core Idea
A lease invalid due to ignorance can become valid when ignorance is removed before the term ends.

This lesson examines a specific scenario in ijara (lease) where the lessee hires land without stating whether it will be cultivated or what crop will be grown. The Hanafi school rules the contract initially invalid (fasid) due to ignorance (jahalah) of the subject matter. However, if the lessee cultivates and the term expires, the contract is validated by istihsan (juristic preference). The lesson contrasts this with the strict qiyas position of Imam Zufar, who holds the contract remains invalid. Understanding this ruling is essential for grasping how Hanafi fiqh balances contractual certainty with practical outcomes through istihsan.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and initial ruling
The act is a land lease (ijara) where the lessee does not specify use (e.g., cultivation) or crop type. The initial ruling is fasid (invalid) because the subject matter is unknown.
Jahalah (ignorance) of the subject matter invalidates the contract.
2
Locate the cause of invalidity
The land can be used for multiple purposes (cultivation, construction, storage) and crops vary in their effect on the land. Without specification, the contract lacks certainty of the subject matter.
Certainty of subject matter is a core requirement in contracts.
3
Understand the istihsan argument
If the lessee cultivates and the term expires, the ignorance is removed: it becomes known that the land was used for cultivation and which crop. The lessor's silence implies consent. Istihsan overrides qiyas to validate the contract.
Istihsan: juristic preference for a stronger reason outweighing analogy.
4
Note the opposing position
Imam Zufar (and Shafi'i, Ahmad) hold that a contract beginning invalid cannot become valid. This is based on qiyas: once fasid, always fasid.
The dispute is a legitimate ikhtilaf within and across schools.
5
Evaluate the practical consequence
Under the Hanafi view, the lessee must pay the agreed rent (musamma). Under the opposing view, no rent or only fair wage would be due. The Hanafi view is mufta bihi.
The thamarah al-khilaf (practical effect) is the obligation to pay the specified rent.

ومن استاجر أرضًا ولم يذكر انه يزرعها او اى شيء يزرعها فالاجارة فاسدة لان الارض تستاجر للزراعة ولغيرها وكذا ما يزرع فيها مختلف فمنه ما يضر بالارض وما لا يضربها غيره فلم يكن المعقود عليه معلوما فان زرعها ومضى الاجل فله المسمى وهذا استحسان وفى القياس لا يجوز وهو قول زفر لانه وقع فاسدا فلا ينقلب جائزا وجه الاستحسان ان الجهالة ارتفعت قبل تمام العقد فينقلب جائزا
ترجمہ کسی نے زمین اجارہ پر لی اور یہ بیان نہیں کیا کہ اس میں کاشت کرے گا۔ یا کس چیز کی کاشت کرے گا۔ تو اجارہ فاسد ہے کیونکہ زمین کاشت کے لئے اجارہ پر لی جاتی ہے اور اس کے علاوہ کے لئے اس میں جو چیز ہوئی جائے وہ مختلف ہوتی ہے۔ چنانچہ بعض چیزیں زمین کے لئے مضر نہیں ہوتیں۔ پس معقود علیہ معلوم نہ ہوا ۔ پھر اگر اس نے زمین میں کاشت کر لی اور میعاد گزرگئی تو اس کے لئے اجر سمی ہوگا۔ اور یہ استحسان ہے قیاس میں جائز نہیں۔ یہی امام زفر کا قول ہے کیونکہ عقد فاسد واقع ہوا تھا تو بدل کر جائز نہ ہو جائے گا۔ وجہ استحسان یہ ہے کہ جہالت تمام عقد سے پہلے اٹھ گئی تو بدل کر جائز ہو جائے گا۔
تشریح قوله ومن استاجرار ضا الخ۔ ایک شخص نے زمین اجارہ پر لی اور یہ بیان نہیں کیا، کہ اس میں کھیتی کرے گا یا کچھ اور ، نیز گیہوں کی کھیتی کرے گا یا کسی اور چیز کی تو اجارہ فاسد ہے (اگر موجر نے تعمیم ندی ہو ورنہ جائز ہوگا ) اس واسطے کہ زمین میں صرف کاشت ہی نہیں ہوتی۔ بلکہ تعمیر بھی ہو سکتی ہے۔ درخت وغیر ہ بھی لگائے جا سکتے ہیں سامان کی حفاظت کے لئے لی جاسکتی ہے پھر کاشت بھی مختلف چیزوں کی ہو سکتی ہے جن میں سے بعض چیزیں ایسی ہیں جو زمین کے لئے مضر ہوتی ہیں جیسے رطبہ اور ترکاریاں اور بعض چیزیں اتنی مضر نہیں ہوتیں ۔ پس معقود علیہ مجہول ہوا لہذا اجارہ صحیح نہ ہوگا۔ امام شافعی اور امام احمد بھی اسی کے قائل ہیں۔
قوله فان زرعها .... الخ ۔ ہاں اگر اس کے بعد مستاجر نے اس میں کاشت کی اور مدت بھی گزرگئی تو استحسانا اجارہ صحیح ہو جائے گا۔ لیکن امام زفر، امام شافعی اور امام احمد کے نزدیک اب بھی صحیح نہ ہوگا اور مقتضائے قیاس بھی یہی ہے اس لئے کہ وہ ابتداء فاسد واقع ہوا ہے۔ تو منتقلب بصحت نہ ہوگا ۔ وجہ استحسان یہ ہے کہ مدت عقد تمام ہونے سے پہلے جہالت معقود علیہ جاتی رہی ۔ یعنی یہ معلوم ہو گیا کہ اس نے زمین کاشت کے لئے لی تھی۔ نیز جو چیز اس نے ہوئی ہے وہ بھی معلوم ہوگئی ۔ پھر مالک زمین اتنے وقت تک خاموش رہا۔ یہاں تک کہ مدت گزر گئی اس لئے اجارہ منقلب بصحت ہو جائے گا۔ جیسے اگر عقد کی حالت میں جہالت مرتفع ہو جائے تو الاتفاق جائز ہو جاتا ہے۔ پس یہ ایسا ہو گیا جیسے بیع میں میعاد مجهول گزرنے سے قبل ساقط کردی یا خیار شرط میں تین روز سے زائد کو
And whoever hires a land and does not mention that he will cultivate it or what he will cultivate, the hire is invalid because land is hired for cultivation and other uses, and what is cultivated varies: some harm the land, some do not. So the subject matter is not known. Then if he cultivates it and the term expires, he gets the specified wage. This is istihsan; by qiyas it is not valid, and it is the saying of Zufar because it occurred as invalid and cannot become valid. The reason for istihsan is that the ignorance was removed before the completion of the contract, so it becomes valid. Translation: Someone hired land and did not state whether he would cultivate it or what he would cultivate. So the hire is invalid because land is hired for cultivation, and what is sown varies. Some things harm the land, some do not. So the subject matter was not known. Then if he cultivated it and the term passed, he gets the specified wage. This is istihsan; by qiyas it is not valid. This is the saying of Imam Zufar because the contract was invalid initially and cannot become valid. The reason for istihsan is that ignorance was removed before the completion of the contract, so it becomes valid. Explanation of the saying: A person hired land and did not state whether he would cultivate or do something else, nor the crop. The hire is invalid (unless the lessor generalized, then it is valid) because land is used for various purposes, and some crops harm it. So the subject matter is unknown. Therefore the hire is not valid. Imam Shafi'i and Imam Ahmad also hold this. Regarding 'then if he cultivates it': Yes, after cultivation and expiry of term, by istihsan the hire becomes valid. But Imam Zufar, Shafi'i, and Ahmad hold it remains invalid because the initial invalid cannot become valid. The reason for istihsan is that before the term ends, the ignorance is removed: it becomes known that he took it for cultivation and which crop. Also the landowner remained silent until the term expired. So the contract becomes valid, just as in a sale if ignorance is removed during the contract, it becomes valid. This is like in sale when an unknown time is dropped before expiry, or a condition of option exceeding three days is dropped.
Source pages p. 80

Commentary
This is a ruling on a land lease where the lessee does not specify the use or crop. The initial contract is invalid (fasid) due to ignorance (jahalah) of the subject matter. However, if the lessee cultivates and the term expires, the contract becomes valid by istihsan (juristic preference), and the agreed rent is due. The qiyas (analogy) would hold it invalid since it began invalidly. The text notes that Imam Zufar, Shafi'i and Ahmad stick to qiyas. The Hanafi justification for istihsan is that the ignorance was removed before the contract's completion (i.e., before the term ended), and the landowner's silence implies consent. This principle applies also to other contracts like sale when an unknown condition is dropped.

Key Terms
استحسان (istiḥsān): Juristic preference that overrides qiyas due to a stronger reason, here removal of ignorance before contract completion.
جہالت (jahālah): Ignorance of the subject matter that renders the contract invalid.
قیاس (qiyās): Analogical reasoning; here qiyas would hold the contract invalid after its initial invalidity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what happens if someone leases land without specifying the crop, cultivates wheat, and the term ends?
A) The lease remains invalid; no rent due.
B) The lease becomes valid by istihsan; agreed rent due.
C) The lease is valid from start because wheat is not harmful.
D) The lease is invalid but fair wage is due.

Key Takeaway
A land lease that is initially invalid due to ignorance of the subject matter may be validated by istihsan when the ignorance is removed and the lessor acquiesces before the term expires.
