Donkey Hire Without Specifying Load
Ruling on donkey hire with unspecified load and istihsan validation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on hiring a donkey with unspecified load, explain the amanah principle, and apply istihsan in validating a fasid contract.

Core Idea
A fasid hire contract can become valid by istihsan once the service is performed; the hired animal remains an amanah until then.

When a hire contract is invalid due to unspecified terms, one might assume the entire transaction collapses. However, Hanafi fiqh applies istihsan (juridical preference) to salvage the contract if the hirer completes the journey with customary load. Additionally, the hired animal is treated as a trust, shielding the hirer from liability for accidental death. This lesson unpacks the ruling and its basis.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and initial ruling
The act is hiring a donkey to a specific destination without specifying the load. The initial ruling is that the contract is fasid (invalid) due to ignorance of the load.
Ignorance of the load constitutes gharar, making a contract fasid in Hanafi law.
2
Examine the two outcomes after performance
Two scenarios: (1) If the donkey dies en route after loading, the hirer is not liable for compensation. (2) If the journey is completed and the donkey reaches the destination, the hirer must pay the specified wage by istihsan.
The ruling distinguishes between liability and wage obligation.
3
Trace the reasoning (talil)
The hired donkey is an amanah (trust) in the hirer's possession even though the contract is fasid. Therefore, no liability unless negligence. The wage is due by istihsan because the benefit (usufruct) has been received.
Istihsan overrides the initial qiyas that would void the contract entirely.
4
Note the exception: dispute before loading
If the parties dispute before the hirer loads the donkey (or before cultivation in analogous cases), the contract is annulled to remove the invalidity, as the defect is still present.
The contract is annulled ex nunc, not retroactively.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن استاجر حمارا الى بغداد بدرهم ولم يسم ما يحمل عليه فحمل ما يحمل الناس فنفق فى بعض الطريق فلاضمان عليه لان العين المستاجرة امانة فى يد المستاجر وان كانت الاجارة فاسدة فان بلغ الى بغداد فله الاجر المسمى استحسانا على ما ذكرنا فى المسألة الأولى وان اختصما قبل ان يحمل عليه وفى المسألة الأولى قبل ان يزرع نقضت الاجارة دف دفع فساد اذ الفساد قائم
ترجمہ کسی نے ایک گدھا بغداد تک ایک درہم کے عوض اجارہ پر لیا اور جو اس پر لا دے گا وہ بیان نہیں کیا پھر اس نے وہ چیز لادی جو لوگ لا دا کرتے ہیں۔ پھر گدھا راہ میں مر گیا تو اس پر تاوان نہ ہو گا۔ کیونکہ اجارہ پر لی ہوئی چیز مستاجر کے پاس امانت ہوتی ہے۔ اگر چہ اجارہ فاسدہ ہو۔ پھر اگر اس نے بغداد تک پہنچادیا تو اس کے لئے اجر مسٹمی ہوگا۔ استحسانا جیسا کہ ہم نے پہلے مسئلہ میں ذکر کیا ہے اور اگر دونوں نے باہم جھگڑا کیا بوجھ لادنے سے پہلے اور مسئلہ اولی میں کاشت کرنے سے پہلے تو اجارہ تو ڑ دیا جائے گا۔ فساد دور کرنے کے لئے کیونکہ فسادا بھی تک قائم ہے۔
And whoever hires a donkey to Baghdad for a dirham and does not specify what to load on it, then he loaded what people usually load, and it died en route, then there is no liability on him because the hired chattel is a trust in the hirer's hand even if the hire is invalid. If it reached Baghdad, he gets the specified wage by istihsan, as we mentioned in the first issue. If they dispute before loading (and in the first issue before cultivation), the contract is annulled to remove the invalidity, because the invalidity still exists. Translation: Someone hired a donkey to Baghdad for a dirham and did not state what he would load. Then he loaded what people usually load. The donkey died on the way. There is no compensation because the hired chattel is a trust in the hirer's hand, even if the hire is invalid. If it reached Baghdad, he gets the specified wage by istihsan, as mentioned in the first issue. If they dispute before loading (and in the first issue before cultivation), the contract is annulled to remove invalidity because the invalidity remains.
Source pages p. 81

Commentary
This is a ruling on a hire contract for a donkey where the load is not specified. The initial contract is invalid due to ignorance. However, if the hirer loads the customary load and the donkey performs the journey, the contract becomes valid by istihsan and the agreed wage is due. If the donkey dies en route, there is no liability on the hirer because the donkey is considered an amanah (trust) in his hands, even during an invalid contract. If a dispute arises before loading (or before cultivation in the previous case), the contract is cancelled to eliminate the invalidity.

Key Terms
امانت (amānah): Trust; the hired animal is in the hirer's possession as a trust, so no liability for loss without negligence.
اجارہ فاسدہ (ijārah fāsidah): An invalid hire contract that lacks a condition but may be validated later.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The hirer must compensate the owner for the donkey.
B) No compensation is due; the donkey is a trust.
C) The hirer pays half the value.
D) The contract is void so no liability or wage.

Key Takeaway
A fasid hire contract can be validated by istihsan after performance, and the hired chattel remains an amanah, absolving the hirer from liability for accidental loss.

Istihsan in Ijarah: Curing Fasid Lease of Land
Ruling on ijarah fasid for unspecified land use with istihsan cure

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on ijarah of land without specifying the use and explain why istihsan makes it valid after cultivation and expiry.

Core Idea
If land is rented without specifying the use, the ijarah is fasid; but if cultivated and the term expires, istihsan cures it.

This passage explores a nuanced scenario in lease contracts: renting land without specifying what will be planted. The Hanafi school initially treats such a contract as defective (fasid) due to uncertainty. However, if the lessee actually cultivates and the lease term expires, the contract becomes valid by istihsan, departing from strict qiyas. This illustrates the Hanafi preference for equity over rigid analogy.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Initial Ruling
The act is renting land without specifying the use, including the crop type. The initial ruling is that the ijarah is fasid (defective) because the subject matter is unknown.
2
Understand the Reason for Fasid
Land can be used for various purposes (cultivation, construction, storage) and cultivation varies (some crops harm the land, others do not). This uncertainty (jahalah) makes the contract fasid.
Hanafis consider specifying the intended use a condition for validity.
3
Trace the Istihsan Exception
If the lessee cultivates and the term expires, the contract becomes sahih (valid) by istihsan. The ignorance is removed before the contract is fully executed.
Istihsan is a departure from qiyas due to a stronger reason (removal of uncertainty).
4
Note the Qiyas Position
By strict qiyas, the contract remains fasid because it was invalid at inception – this is the view of Imam Zufar, Imam Shafi'i, and Imam Ahmad.
Hanafis follow istihsan, making the mufta bihi the valid after cultivation.
5
Apply the Ruling
If the parties dispute before the term ends, the lease is annulled due to the remaining defect. If cultivation occurs and the term ends, the lessee pays the named rent.

Book of Ijarah. And for other [purposes] as well, and likewise what is sown in it varies: among it is what harms the land and what does not harm it. So the object of contract was not known. If he cultivates it and the term expires, he has the named wage. This is istihsan. By qiyas it is not valid, which is the saying of Zufar, because it occurred as fasid so it does not become valid. The reason for istihsan is that ignorance was removed before completion of the contract, so it becomes valid.
Source pages p. 81

Commentary
This passage presents the ruling on a lease of land where the lessee does not specify what he will cultivate or even that he will cultivate. The Hanafi school says such an ijarah is fasid because the subject matter is uncertain; land can be used for various purposes, some beneficial, some harmful. However, if the lessee actually cultivates and the term expires, the contract becomes valid by istihsan, and he is entitled to the named rent. This is opposed to qiyas (analogy) which holds the contract remains fasid – the view of Imam Zufar, Imam Shafi'i, and Imam Ahmad. The istihsan reasoning is that ignorance was removed before the contract was fully executed (the term ended), so the contract is rectified. The commentator explains the types of uses and emphasizes that if the parties dispute before cultivation, the contract is annulled because the defect remains.

Key Terms
استحسان (istihsan): A legal method of preferring a ruling that departs from qiyas due to a stronger evidence or equity.
قياس (qiyas): Analogical reasoning from an original case to a new case based on a common effective cause.
اجارة فاسدة (ijarah fasidah): A defective lease contract that is missing a condition for validity but not its essence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If someone rents land without specifying the use, and then cultivates it, and the term expires, what is the Hanafi ruling on the ijarah?
A) The ijarah remains fasid and no rent is due.
B) The ijarah becomes sahih by istihsan and the named rent is due.
C) The ijarah becomes sahih automatically regardless of use.
D) The ijarah is void (batil) ab initio.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school uses istihsan to cure a fasid ijarah of land when the uncertainty about the use is resolved before the contract is fully executed.

Renting a Donkey Without Specifying Load: Ijara Fasid and Istihsan
Ruling on ijara fasid for unspecified load, amanah, and istihsan

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on leasing without specifying the load, explain why it is fasid, and apply the rule of amanah and istihsan to similar cases.

Core Idea
A lease with an unspecified load is initially fasid, but becomes valid by istihsan if usual goods are loaded and delivered.

This lesson examines a case where a donkey is hired for a journey without specifying what it will carry. The Hanafi school treats such a contract as fasid due to the unknown subject matter. However, when the lessee loads ordinary goods and the journey is completed, the ruling changes: the lessee becomes entitled to the named wage by istihsan. We will also see how the leased animal remains an amanah (trust) even in a fasid contract, protecting the lessee from liability unless he transgresses.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its initial ruling
The act is hiring a donkey for a specific journey (to Baghdad) without specifying what load it will carry. The initial ruling is that the ijarah is fasid (defective).
Fasid means the contract is flawed in a way that can potentially be corrected, as opposed to batil (void).
2
Understand why it is fasid
The contract is fasid because the subject matter (the load) is unknown at the time of contract. In ijara, the benefit (here, carrying a specific load) must be known to both parties.
Ignorance of the load creates gharar (uncertainty), which invalidates the contract unless later cured.
3
Note the exception by istihsan
If the lessee loads what people normally load (not exceeding custom) and completes the journey to the destination, the contract becomes valid by istihsan. The lessee then deserves the named wage.
Istihsan overrides qiyas in this case because the defect (ignorance of load) is removed before the contract is fully executed.
4
Recognize the amanah principle
Even though the contract is fasid, the leased donkey is considered a trust (amanah) in the lessee's hands. Therefore, if the donkey dies without any transgression (e.g., overloading or deviation), the lessee is not liable.
This distinguishes amanah from dhaman (guarantee). The lessee only becomes liable if he acts as a usurper (ghasib).
5
Distinguish the scenario if dispute occurs before loading
If the parties dispute before the load is placed (or in the analogous case of land, before cultivation), the contract is annulled to remove the defect, because the defect still exists at that point.
This shows that istihsan only applies after performance that removes the uncertainty.

And whoever hires a donkey to Baghdad for a dirham and did not specify what to load on it, then he loaded what people normally load, and the donkey died on the way, there is no liability on him because the leased item is a trust in the hands of the lessee even if the ijarah was fasid. If he reached Baghdad, he has the named wage by istihsan, as we mentioned in the first issue. If they dispute before loading, and in the first issue before cultivating, the ijarah is annulled to remove the defect, since the defect still exists.

Commentary
This passage presents a second case of ijara fasid: hiring a donkey for a journey without specifying the load. The initial contract is fasid because the subject matter (the load) is unknown. However, if the lessee loads the usual type of goods and completes the journey, the contract becomes valid by istihsan and he is entitled to the named wage. If the donkey dies en route, the lessee is not liable because the leased animal is an amanah (trust) in his hands, even if the contract is fasid, provided he did not transgress (e.g., by overloading). If the parties dispute before loading, the contract is annulled, similar to the previous case of land. The commentator emphasizes the distinction between amanah and liability: in a fasid ijarah, the animal remains amanah unless the lessee acts as a usurper.

Key Terms
امانت (amanah): A trust; the leased item in the lessee's hands is considered a trust, so no liability for loss without transgression.
اجیر (ajir): A hired person; here, the lessee of the donkey is considered an ajir.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) The contract was void.
B) The donkey is a trust (amanah).
C) The owner is responsible.
D) The lessee was forced.

Key Takeaway
In a fasid ijarah, the leased item remains an amanah; liability is avoided unless the lessee transgresses, and istihsan may validate the contract if the defect is removed by performance.

Liability of the Common Hired Worker (Ajir Mushtarak)
Explains liability of common hired worker and intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the liability of the ajīr mushtarak, explain the intra-Hanafi dispute between Abū Ḥanīfah and the Ṣāḥibayn, and apply the mufta bihi opinion to real-world scenarios.

Core Idea
The common hired worker is a trustee: no liability without negligence, but the later fatwa holds him liable for preventable losses.

When you hand over your fabric to a tailor or your garment to a dry cleaner, who bears the risk if it is stolen? The Hanafi school has a classic dispute on this question. This lesson unpacks the legal reasoning of Imām Abū Ḥanīfah and his two disciples, and explains which opinion is relied upon today.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its legal classification
What is being ruled upon? The goods in the hands of an ajīr mushtarak. Are they a trust (amānah) or a guarantee (ḍamān)?
The ajīr mushtarak is a worker who serves multiple customers, e.g., a tailor, dyer, or goldsmith.
2
State the positions of Abū Ḥanīfah and the Ṣāḥibayn
Abū Ḥanīfah: goods are amānah – no liability. Ṣāḥibayn: liable except for overwhelming calamities.
Imām Zufar agrees with Abū Ḥanīfah.
3
Examine the evidence for each view
Ṣāḥibayn cite the practice of ʿUmar and ʿAlī and argue preservation is a contractual duty. Abū Ḥanīfah relies on the principle that consensual possession creates a trust and the hadith 'lā ḍamān ʿalā muʾtaman'.
The evidence is zannī (speculative), allowing ijtihād.
4
Analyze the key point of contention
Is preservation (ḥifẓ) a primary or incidental obligation? Abū Ḥanīfah says incidental; Ṣāḥibayn say necessary for the work, thus part of the contract.
The distinction determines whether liability exists.
5
Determine the muftā bihī (operative opinion)
Later scholars like al-Zaylaʿī gave fatwa on the Ṣāḥibayn's view due to societal changes, making it the relied-upon position today.
Al-Marghīnānī and Qāḍī Khān preferred Abū Ḥanīfah's view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الاجارات

المفاعل كالجليس والحسيب فليس للمبالغة فلا يعمل اتفاقا

قال والمتاع امانة في يده فان هلك لم يضمن شيئا عند ابي حنيفة وهو قول زفر ويضمنه عندهما الامن شىء غالب كالحريق الغالب والعدو المكابر لهما ما روى عن عمر وعلى رضى الله عنهما انهما كانا يضمنان الاجير المشترك ولان الحفظ مستحق عليه اذ لا يمكنه العمل الا به فاذا هلک بسبب يمكن الاحتراز عنه كالغصب والسرقة كان التقصير من جهته فيضمنه كالوديعة اذا كانت باجر بخلاف ما لا يمكن الاحتراز عنه كالموت حتف انفه والحريق الغالب وغيره لانه لا تقصير من جهته ولابي حنيفة ان العين امانة فى يده لان القبض حصل باذنه ولهذا لو هلك بسبب لا يمكن الاحتراز عنه لا يضمنه ولو كان مضمونا يضمنه كما فى المغصوب والحفظ مستحق عليه تبعا لا مقصودا ولهذا لا يقابله الاجر بخلاف المودع بالاجر لان الحفظ مستحق عليه مقصوداً حتى يقابله الاجر

وقد روي انه كان يضمن الصباغ والصائغ

وروي لا ضمان على مؤتمن
Book of Hiring

Al-mufa'il is like al-jalis and al-hasib, so it is not for exaggeration, so it does not operate by agreement.

He said: The goods are a trust in his hand. If they are destroyed, he does not guarantee anything according to Abu Hanifa, and this is the statement of Zufar. And he guarantees them according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) except for something overwhelming like an overwhelming fire and an overwhelming enemy. For them is what was narrated from Umar and Ali (رضى الله عنهما) that they used to hold the common hired worker liable. And because preservation (hifz) is obligatory upon him, since he cannot perform the work except with it. So if it is destroyed due to a cause from which one can guard, like usurpation and theft, then there is negligence from his side, so he becomes liable, like the deposit when it is for hire. Contrary to what cannot be guarded against, like natural death, overwhelming fire, etc., because there is no negligence from his side. And for Abu Hanifa: the item is a trust in his hand because possession was obtained with his permission. Therefore, if it is destroyed due to a cause from which one cannot guard, he does not become liable; and if it were a guarantee, he would become liable, as in the case of a usurped item. And preservation is obligatory upon him subordinately, not as a main purpose. Thus, it is not compensated by the hire. Contrary to the depositee for hire, because preservation is obligatory upon him as a main purpose, so it is compensated by the hire.

And it was narrated that he used to hold the dyer and the goldsmith liable.

And it was narrated: 'No liability on a trustee.'
Source pages p. 83

Commentary
This passage is a commentary from Ashraf al-Hidayah on a ruling from al-Hidayah regarding the liability of the common hired worker (ajir mushtarak). The commentary opens with a brief grammatical note on the word 'mufa'il', explaining that it resembles 'jalīs' and 'ḥasīb' in form and is not exaggerated, hence it does not convey agency by agreement. The main ruling states that the goods in the hands of an ajir mushtarak are a trust (amānah). Therefore, if they are destroyed without negligence, he is not liable according to Imam Abū Ḥanīfah and Imam Zufar. However, the two companions (Abū Yūsuf and Muḥammad) hold that he is liable except for overwhelming calamities such as a general fire or an irresistible enemy. Their evidence includes a narration that Caliphs ʿUmar and ʿAlī (may Allah be pleased with them) used to hold dyers and goldsmiths liable for loss. They reason that preservation (ḥifẓ) of the goods is necessary for the work, so it is implicitly part of the contract. If loss occurs from a preventable cause like theft or usurpation, the worker is negligent and becomes a guarantor. This is analogous to a deposit (wadīʿah) taken for hire, where the depositee is liable. Conversely, if the loss is unpreventable, there is no negligence and no liability. Imam Abū Ḥanīfah responds that the goods are a trust because possession was obtained with the owner's consent. The essential characteristic of a trust is that it is not guaranteed unless there is transgression (taʿaddī). If the goods were guaranteed (like a usurped item), the worker would be liable even for unpreventable losses, but that is not the case. Preservation is required from the worker only as a means to perform the work, not as the primary purpose of the contract; therefore, the hire payment is not in exchange for preservation. This differs from a paid depositee, where preservation is the main purpose and the hire is paid for it. The passage also mentions a hadith from al-Dāraquṭnī: 'There is no liability on a trustee,' which supports Abū Ḥanīfah's position. Later Hanafi scholars have differed on which opinion is relied upon: some prefer Abū Ḥanīfah's view, while others, due to changing times, give fatwa on the opinion of the two companions, which also aligns with the three other imams (Mālik, al-Shāfiʿī in one narration, and Aḥmad). The commentary thus presents the full legal reasoning and evidence for each position within the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
أجير مشترك (ajīr mushtarak): A hired worker who works for multiple people or the general public, like a tailor or dyer; entitled to wages only after completing the work.
أمانة (amānah): A trust: goods held with the owner's permission, not guaranteed unless the holder transgresses.
ضمان (ḍamān): Liability to compensate for loss or damage; being a guarantor.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi position in the later Hanafi school, what is the ruling if an ajīr mushtarak's goods are stolen without negligence?
A) No liability, because goods are a trust.
B) Liable, because theft is a preventable loss.
C) Liable only if the worker was grossly negligent.
D) The contract becomes void.

Key Takeaway
The common hired worker (ajīr mushtarak) is a trustee by default, but the relied-upon fatwa holds him liable for preventable losses, reflecting a shift in practice.

8 min
Why the Common Hired Worker Is Liable: The Hanafi Intra-Madhhab Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute and tarjih on liability of ajir mushtarak

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the mufta bihi ruling for the liability of the common hired worker and explain the arguments of Abu Hanifa and the two disciples, including why the fatwa shifted.

Core Idea
The common hired worker is liable for avoidable loss — the Sahibayn's view became mufta bihi due to changed circumstances.

In this lesson, we examine the liability of the common hired worker (ajir mushtarak) for goods destroyed during his work. The Hanafi school has an important intra-madhhab disagreement: Imam Abu Hanifa holds that the worker is a trustee (amin) and not liable, while his two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, argue that he is contractually obligated to preserve the goods and is liable for avoidable causes. Understanding this dispute and its resolution is essential for applying the correct ruling in contemporary practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling
Read the matn: 'And what is destroyed by his work ... is guaranteed upon him.' The common hired worker is liable. But note the conditions: only for avoidable causes.
The matn is from the Arabic section: 'و ما تلف بعمله ... مضمون عليه'.
2
Examine Abu Hanifa's amanah argument
Abu Hanifa argues that the worker is a trustee (amin) because the contract is on the work, not on the goods. Liability only arises from transgression or contract; neither applies here. He cites the hadith 'No liability on a trustee'.
The text calls this the 'statement of Abu Hanifa'.
3
Examine the Sahibayn's contractual duty argument
The Sahibayn argue that preservation (hifz) is a necessary part of the contract; the worker cannot work without preserving the goods. If the destruction is from an avoidable cause, it is negligence, making him liable.
They analogize to a paid depository, where the depositary is liable if he takes wages.
4
Understand the fatwa evolution
Early fatwa followed Abu Hanifa, but later scholars like Zayla'i adopted the Sahibayn's view due to changing circumstances (people no longer trusted workers). This is the current mufta bihi.
The text mentions Faqih Abu al-Layth, Taj al-Shari'ah, and Marghinani following Abu Hanifa, but Zayla'i and others preferring Sahibayn.

انه كان يضمن الصباغ والصائغ وقال لا يصلح للناس الاذالك قوله ولان الحفظ .... الخ- یہ صاحبین کی عقلی دلیل ہے کہ اجیر کے ذمہ حفاظت کرنا واجب ہے کیونکہ وہ حفاظت کے بغیر کام نہیں کر سکتا۔ گویا حفاظت بھی معقود علیہ ہے اور عقد معاوضہ معقود علیہ کی سلامتی کا مقتضی ہے۔ پس جب مال عین ایسے سبب سے تلف ہو جس سے احتراز ممکن ہے جیسے سرقہ وغصب وغیرہ تو یہ اجیر کی جانب سے تقصیر ہوگی۔ لہذا ضامن ہوگا۔ جیسے ودیعت میں اگر مودع نے مستودع کے لئے حفاظت کی اجرت ٹھہرانی ہو تو تلف ہو جانے سے مستودع ضامن ہوتا ہے۔ ہاں اگر ایسے سبب سے تلف ہو جس سے بچاؤ ناممکن ہے۔ مثلاً چروا نہے کے پاس بکری اپنی موت سے مرگئی یا عام طور پر آگ لگ گئی یا ڈا کا پڑ گیا تو اس صورت میں ضامن نہ ہوگا کیونکہ اب اجیر کی جانب سے کوئی کوتاہی نہیں ہے۔
قوله ولابي حنيفة ... الخ - امام ابو حنیفہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ اجیر مشترک کے پاس بھی امانت تھی ۔ اور امانت میں ضمان نہیں ہوتی ۔ یؤیده مارواه الدارقطني لاضمان علی مؤتمن وجہ یہ ہے کہ ضمان یا تو بوجہ تعدی واجب ہوتا ہے یا بوجہ عقد اور یہاں ان دونوں میں سے کوئی بات نہیں پائی گئی ، تعدی تو اس لئے نہیں ہے کہ اجیر کو متاجر کے اجارہ سے قبضہ حاصل ہوا تھا اور عقد کی وجہ سے ضمان اس لئے نہیں ہو سکتا کہ عقد کا درد د عمل پر ہے نہ کہ مال عین پر ۔ پس مال عین مضمون بالعقد نہیں ہوسکتا۔ یہی وجہ ہے کہ اگر وہ شئی یسے سبب سے تلف ہو جس سے احتراز ممکن نہیں تو اجیر بالا تفاق ضامن نہیں ہوتا اگر مال مذکور اس کے پاس ضمانت میں ہوتا تو وہ ضرور ضامن ہوتا جیسے غاصب ہر حال میں ضامن ہوتا ہے۔
قوله و الحفظ مستحق عليه ... الخ ۔ رہا یہ کہنا کہ اجیر کے ذمہ حفاظت واجب ہے سو اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ حفاظت کا واجب ہونا تبعا ہے نہ کہ قصداً۔ اس لئے کہ عقد کا ورود اجیر مشترک کے عمل پر ہے۔ حفاظت معقود عالیہ نہیں ہے۔ پس حفاظت اصلی مقصود نہیں بلکہ وہ چونکہ اقامت عمل کا وسیلہ ہے اس لئے تبعا مقصود ہے اسی لئے حفاظت کے مقابلہ میں کچھ اجرت نہیں ہوتی بخلاف اس شخص کے کہ جس کو ودیعت اجرت پر دی گئی ہو کہ اس پر حفاظت قصد اواجب ہے یہاں تک کہ اس کے مقابلہ میں اجرت ہے۔
تنبیہ اجیر مشترک کے ضامن ہونے میں صحابہ کرام کا اختلاف ہے۔ بعض کے نزدیک ضامن ہوتا ہے اور بعض کے نزدیک ضامن نہیں ہوتا بلکہ ایسا بھی ہے کہ ایک ہی شخص سے مختلف روایات وارد ہیں۔ چنانچہ حضرت علی سے جہاں اجیر مشترک کے ضامن ہونے کی روایت ہے وہیں عدم ضمان بھی مروی ہے۔ اس لئے بعض متاخرین فقہا ء نے یہ فتویٰ دیا ہے کہ اجیر ومستاجر دونوں جس مقدار پر چاہیں با ہم صلح کر لیں۔ ویسے فقیہ ابواللیث نے ذکر کیا ہے کہ فتویٰ امام ابو حنیفہ کے قول پر ہے۔ تاج الشریعہ، شیخ مرغینانی اور قاضی خان بھی اسی پر فتوی دیتے تھے۔ لیکن علامہ زیلعی وغیرہ نے کہا ہے ۔ کہ آج کل فتویٰ صاحبین کے قول پر ہے۔ کیونکہ لوگوں کے حالات متغیر ہو چکے اور اموال کی حفاظت اسی سے ہو سکتی ہے کہ اجیر سے ضمان لیا جائے ۔ ائمہ ثلاثہ کا قول بھی یہی ہے۔

جو چیز اجیر مشترک کے عمل سے تلف ہو جائے اس کا حکم
قال و ما تلف بعمله كتخريق الثوب من دقَه وزَلِق الحمّال وانقطاع الحبل الذي يشد به المكارى الحمل وغرق السفينة من مده مضمون عليه وقال زفر والشافعي لا ضمان عليه لانه امره بالفعل مطلقا فينتظمه بنوعيه المعيب والسليم وصار كاجير الوحد ومعين القصار ولنا ان الداخل تحت الاذن ما هو الداخل تحت العقد وهو العمل الصالح لانه هو الوسيلة الى الاثر وهو المعقود عليه حقيقة حتى لو حصل بفعل الغير يجب الاجر فلم يكن المفسد مأذونا فيه بخلاف المعين لانه متبرع فلا يمكن تقييده بالمصلح لانه يمتنع عن التبرع وفيما نحن فيه يعمل بالاجر فامكن تقييده وبخلاف الاجير الوحد على ما نذكره ان شاء الله تعالى وانقطاع الحمل من قلة اهتمامه فكان من صنيعه قال الا انه لا يضمن به بني آدم ممن غرق في السفينة أو سقط من الدابة وان كان بسوقه وقوده لان الواجب ضمان الآدمى وانه لا يجب بالعقد وانما يجب بالجناية ولهذا يجب على العاقلة وضمان العقود لا تتحمله العاقلة

توضیح اللغة تلف (س) تسلفاً برباد ہونا۔ تخریق پھاڑنا۔ دق کونا۔ زلق (س) پھسلنا_حمال قلی_حبل رییشدشدا باندهنامکاری جانوروں کو کرایہ پر دینے والا حمل بوجھ سفینه سنتی - مد کھینچنا۔ معیب عیب دار - قصار دھوبی۔سوق (ن) جانور کو پیچھے سے ہانکنا۔ قود (ن) جانور کو آگے سے کھینچنا جناية جرم ۔ ترجمہ اور جو تلف ہو جائے اجیر کے عمل سے جیسے کپڑے کو پھاڑ دینا کوٹنے سے۔ حمال کا پھسل جانا اس رسی کا ٹوٹ جانا جس سے کرایہ پر دینے والا بوجھ باندھتا ہے اور کشتی کا ڈوب جانا اس کے کھینچنے سے یہ سب اجیر پر مضمون ہے۔ امام زفر اور امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں کہ اس پر ضمان نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ مالک نے اس کو مطلقاً کام کرنے کا حکم کیا ہے تو یہ معیب و سلیم ہر دو کو شامل ہوگا اور یہ ایسا ہو گیا جیسے اجیر خاص اور دھوبی کا مددگار ۔ ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ اجازت کے تحت میں وہی داخل ہے جو عقد کے تحت میں داخل ہے اور وہ صحیح و درست کام ہے۔ کیونکہ یہی حصول اثر کا وسیلہ ہے اور در حقیقت یہ اثر ہی معقود علیہ ہے یہاں تک کہ اگر یہ غیر کے فعل سے حاصل ہو تو اجرت واجب ہوگی پس مفسد عمل داخل اجازت نہ ہوا بخلاف معین کے کیونکہ وہ احسان کنندہ ہے۔ تو اس کے کام کو مصلح ہونے کے ساتھ مقید نہیں کیا جا سکتا۔ ورنہ وہ احسان کرنے سے باز رہے گا اور مانحن فیہ میں وہ اجرت پر کام کرتا ہے تو اسکے عمل کے درست ہونے کی قید لگانا ممکن ہے۔ اور بخلاف اجیر خاص کے۔ بنابر آنکہ ہم ذکر کریں گے انشاء اللہ تعالیٰ اور رتی کا ٹوٹنا اس کے اہتمام کی کوتاہی سے ہے تو یہ اس کی حرکت کا نتیجہ ہے۔ مگر وہ آدمی کا ضامن نہ ہوگا جو کشتی میں غرق ہو جائے یا بھاڑے کے ٹو پر سے گر مرے۔ اگر چہ اس کے ہانکنے یا کھینچنے سے ہو۔ اس لئے کہ واجب تو آدمی کا ضمان ہے۔ جو عقد سے واجب نہیں ہوتا بلکہ جرم سے واجب ہوتا ہے۔ اسی لئے یہ عاقلہ پر واجب ہوتا ہے اور جو ضمان بوجہ عقد ہو وہ عاقلہ نہیں اٹھائے۔ تشریح قوله وما تلف الخ- جو چیز اجیر مشترک کے عمل سے تلف ہو جائے وہ اس کا ضامن ہوگا۔ جیسے دھوبی کے کوٹنے سے کپڑا پھٹ جائے یا مزدور کے پھسلنے یا جس رسی سے بوجھ بندھا ہوا تھا اس کے ٹوٹنے سے مال ضائع ہو جائے یا ملاح کے بے قاعدہ کھینچنے سے کشتی ڈوب جائے اور مال غرق ہو جائے تو ان سب صورتوں میں اجیر مشترک ضامن ہوگا۔ امام مالک، امام احمد اور ابن ابی لیلی بھی اسی
Book of Ijarah. Ashraf al-Hidayah, Urdu commentary on Hidayah, Volume 12. Except if the taxi (hired vehicle) is destroyed due to a cause from which escape is not possible, such as it dying its own death, or fire breaking out, or an enemy attack destroying it, etc. Their evidence is that 'Umar and 'Ali used to take guarantee from the goldsmith and dyer. Thus, Imam Bayhaqi narrated from 'Ali via Imam Shafi'i: 'He used to make the dyer and goldsmith liable and said: People cannot do without that.' The statement 'and because preservation...' - this is the rational proof of the two disciples (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad): that preservation is obligatory upon the hired worker because he cannot work without preservation. So preservation is also included in the contract, and a contract of exchange necessitates the safety of the subject matter. Thus, if the property is destroyed by a cause from which avoidance is possible, such as theft or usurpation, this is negligence on the part of the hired worker, so he is liable. Similarly, in a deposit, if the depositor fixes a wage for preservation for the depositary, then if it is destroyed, the depositary is liable. Yes, if it is destroyed by a cause from which escape is impossible, e.g., a goat in the custody of a shepherd dies naturally, or a general fire occurs, or a calamity befalls, then in such a case, he is not liable because there is no negligence from the hired worker. The statement 'and Abu Hanifa's statement...' - Imam Abu Hanifa's proof is that the common hired worker has a trust (amanah) with him, and there is no liability in trust. This is supported by what al-Daraqutni narrated: 'No liability upon a trusted person.' The reason is that liability is either due to transgression or due to contract, and neither exists here. Transgression is absent because the hired worker gained possession through the hire contract, and liability cannot be due to contract because the contract is on the work, not on the property itself. So the property is not guaranteed by contract. This is why if the item is destroyed by a cause from which avoidance is impossible, the hired worker is not liable by consensus. If the mentioned property were in his possession as a guarantee, he would certainly be liable, like a usurper is liable in all cases. The statement 'and preservation is binding upon him...' - as for saying that preservation is obligatory upon the hired worker, the answer is that preservation is binding subordinately, not primarily. Because the contract is upon the work of the common hired worker, preservation is not the subject matter. So preservation is not the main objective, but it is intended subordinately because it is a means to perform the work. Therefore, no wage is fixed for preservation, unlike the person who receives a deposit for a wage, where preservation is primarily obligatory and there is a wage for it. Note: There is a disagreement among the Companions regarding the liability of the common hired worker. Some consider him liable, others not. In fact, different narrations exist from the same person, such as from 'Ali, where both liability and non-liability are narrated. Therefore, some later jurists gave the fatwa that the hired worker and the hirer should reconcile on any amount they wish. Otherwise, Faqih Abu al-Layth mentioned that the fatwa is according to Imam Abu Hanifa's statement. Taj al-Shari'ah, Shaykh al-Marghinani, and Qadi Khan also gave fatwa accordingly. But Allamah Zayla'i and others said that nowadays the fatwa is according to the statement of the two disciples (Sahibayn) because people's conditions have changed, and the protection of wealth can only be achieved by taking a guarantee from the hired worker. The three Imams (Malik, Shafi'i, Ahmad) also hold this view. The ruling on what is destroyed by the work of the common hired worker: He said: And what is destroyed by his work, such as tearing the cloth by beating it, the porter slipping, the rope breaking by which the carrier ties the load, and the sinking of the ship by his pulling, is guaranteed upon him. Zufar and al-Shafi'i said: There is no liability upon him, because the owner commanded him to do the act absolutely, so it includes both its defective and sound types, and it becomes like a specific hired worker (ajir khas) and the helper of the launderer. Our proof: That which enters under permission is what enters under the contract, which is sound work, because it is the means to the effect, and the effect is the actual subject matter. So if the effect is achieved by the act of another, the wage is due. Therefore, the destructive act is not permitted. Unlike the volunteer, because he is a benefactor, so his work cannot be restricted to what is proper, otherwise he would refrain from beneficence. In our case, he works for a wage, so it is possible to restrict him. And unlike the specific hired worker, as we will mention, God willing. The breaking of the load is due to his lack of care, so it is from his own doing. He said: But he is not liable for a human being, such as one who drowns in the ship or falls from the animal, even if it is by his driving or pulling, because the obligatory is the guarantee of a human being, which is not obligatory by contract but by crime. Hence it is upon the 'aqilah (tribal surety), and guarantees of contracts are not borne by the 'aqilah.
Source pages p. 84

Commentary
This passage is a detailed treatment of the liability of the common hired worker (ajir mushtarak) for goods that are destroyed by his work. It begins by presenting the ruling that such destruction is guaranteed (mazmun) — meaning the worker is liable. Examples include a cloth torn by beating, a porter slipping, a rope breaking, or a ship sinking due to the worker's pulling. The passage then presents the opposition of Imam Zufar and Imam al-Shafi'i, who argue that the worker should not be liable because the employer gave absolute permission to work, which includes both defective and sound outcomes, similar to a specific hired worker or a volunteer assistant. The Hanafi response is that permission under the contract only covers sound work, as the actual subject matter of the contract is the effect (e.g., clean clothes, transport), and the work is merely a means. If the work is destructive, it is outside the scope of permission. The Hanafis distinguish this from a volunteer, whose work cannot be restricted because he might refrain from beneficence, whereas a hired worker can be restricted. They also distinguish from a specific hired worker (ajir khas), who is not liable for destruction as he is considered a trustee. The passage further specifies that the worker is not liable for injury to a human being (blood money) because such liability arises from crime (jinayah), not contract, and is borne by the 'aqilah. The earlier part of the text on page 84 explains the dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two disciples (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) regarding the basis of liability. Abu Hanifa considers the worker a trustee (amin) and thus not liable except for transgression, while the two disciples argue that preservation (hifz) is a contractual duty, making the worker liable for destruction from avoidable causes. The passage also notes the evolution of the fatwa: earlier scholars followed Abu Hanifa, but later scholars like Zayla'i adopted the view of the two disciples due to changing circumstances. The commentary emphasizes the analytical reasoning (talil) behind each position.

Key Terms
أجير مشترك (ajir mushtarak): A common hired worker who works for multiple people or for a wage per task, not exclusively for one person. His liability is disputed.
أجير خاص (ajir khas): A specific hired worker who is hired exclusively for a period or for a specific task. He is not liable for destruction of goods in his custody.
ضمان (daman): Liability or guarantee to compensate for loss or destruction of property.
أمانة (amanah): Trust; property held without liability for accidental destruction, as per Abu Hanifa's view of the ajir mushtarak.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the mufta bihi (relied-upon) position regarding the liability of a common hired worker (ajir mushtarak) for goods destroyed by his work?
A) He is not liable at all, as per Imam Abu Hanifa
B) He is liable only for avoidable causes of destruction, as per the two disciples (Sahibayn)
C) He is liable for all destruction, including acts of God
D) He is liable but only for human life, not property

Key Takeaway
The common hired worker is liable for avoidable destruction of property, but not for acts of God; this is the mufta bihi view of the Sahibayn adopted by later Hanafi jurists.

Ijarah — Hire and Lease
intermediate
7 min
The Ajir Mushtarak vs. the Ajir Khas: Inter-Madhhab Dispute and the Human Life Exception
Inter-madhhab dispute and distinction between property and human liability

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the liability of the ajir mushtarak from that of the ajir khas and the volunteer, and state the exception for human life.

Core Idea
The ajir mushtarak is liable for property damage from negligent work, but not for human life — that is a crime, not a contract.

This lesson focuses on the inter-madhhab dispute between the Hanafis and Imam Zufar/Shafi'i regarding the liability of the common hired worker. The Hanafis distinguish the ajir mushtarak from the specific hired worker (ajir khas) and the volunteer, arguing that the contract only covers sound work. Additionally, the text clarifies that the worker is not liable for injury to a human being, as that liability falls under crimes (jinayat) and is borne by the 'aqilah.

Guided Path
1
State the inter-madhhab dispute
Zufar and al-Shafi'i hold no liability for the ajir mushtarak; the Hanafis (mufta bihi) hold liability for avoidable destruction. Identify the thamarah al-khilaf.
The matn says 'mazmun' (guaranteed) but Zufar and Shafi'i disagree.
2
Understand the Hanafi proof: Only sound work is permitted
The contract is on the effect (e.g., clean laundry), so only work that achieves that effect is authorized. Destructive work is not covered by permission.
The text says: 'That which enters under permission is what enters under the contract, which is sound work.'
3
Distinguish from the volunteer and the specific hired worker (ajir khas)
A volunteer (mutabarri') cannot be restricted to sound work because he would refrain from beneficence. The ajir khas is hired for his time, not a specific task, so his liability is different.
The text explicitly distinguishes the ajir mushtarak from both.
4
Apply the exception for human life
The worker is not liable for death or injury to a person even if caused by his work, because that is a crime (jinayah) whose compensation is on the 'aqilah, not a contractual obligation.
The text states: 'But he is not liable for a human being... because the obligatory is the guarantee of a human being, which is not obligatory by contract but by crime.'

اشرف الهدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد - ۱۲ الا یہ کہ ٹیکسی ایسے سبب سے ہلاک ہو جس سے بچاؤ ممکن نہ ہو۔ جیسے اس کا اپنی موت مر جانا یا آگ لگ جانا یا قاتل دشمن کا حملہ کر کے برباد کر دینا وغیرہ۔ ان کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ حضرت عمر اور حضرت علی صائغ اور صباغ ( زرگر رنگریز) سے ضمان لیتے تھے۔ چنانچہ حافظ بیہاتی نے بطریق امام شافعی حضرت علیؓ سے روایت کیا ہے۔
انه كان يضمن الصباغ والصائغ وقال لا يصلح للناس الاذالك قوله ولان الحفظ .... الخ- یہ صاحبین کی عقلی دلیل ہے کہ اجیر کے ذمہ حفاظت کرنا واجب ہے کیونکہ وہ حفاظت کے بغیر کام نہیں کر سکتا۔ گویا حفاظت بھی معقود علیہ ہے اور عقد معاوضہ معقود علیہ کی سلامتی کا مقتضی ہے۔ پس جب مال عین ایسے سبب سے تلف ہو جس سے احتراز ممکن ہے جیسے سرقہ وغصب وغیرہ تو یہ اجیر کی جانب سے تقصیر ہوگی۔ لہذا ضامن ہوگا۔ جیسے ودیعت میں اگر مودع نے مستودع کے لئے حفاظت کی اجرت ٹھہرانی ہو تو تلف ہو جانے سے مستودع ضامن ہوتا ہے۔ ہاں اگر ایسے سبب سے تلف ہو جس سے بچاؤ ناممکن ہے۔ مثلاً چروا نہے کے پاس بکری اپنی موت سے مرگئی یا عام طور پر آگ لگ گئی یا ڈا کا پڑ گیا تو اس صورت میں ضامن نہ ہوگا کیونکہ اب اجیر کی جانب سے کوئی کوتاہی نہیں ہے۔
قوله ولابي حنيفة ... الخ - امام ابو حنیفہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ اجیر مشترک کے پاس بھی امانت تھی ۔ اور امانت میں ضمان نہیں ہوتی ۔ یؤیده مارواه الدارقطني لاضمان علی مؤتمن وجہ یہ ہے کہ ضمان یا تو بوجہ تعدی واجب ہوتا ہے یا بوجہ عقد اور یہاں ان دونوں میں سے کوئی بات نہیں پائی گئی ، تعدی تو اس لئے نہیں ہے کہ اجیر کو متاجر کے اجارہ سے قبضہ حاصل ہوا تھا اور عقد کی وجہ سے ضمان اس لئے نہیں ہو سکتا کہ عقد کا درد د عمل پر ہے نہ کہ مال عین پر ۔ پس مال عین مضمون بالعقد نہیں ہوسکتا۔ یہی وجہ ہے کہ اگر وہ شئی یسے سبب سے تلف ہو جس سے احتراز ممکن نہیں تو اجیر بالا تفاق ضامن نہیں ہوتا اگر مال مذکور اس کے پاس ضمانت میں ہوتا تو وہ ضرور ضامن ہوتا جیسے غاصب ہر حال میں ضامن ہوتا ہے۔
قوله و الحفظ مستحق عليه ... الخ ۔ رہا یہ کہنا کہ اجیر کے ذمہ حفاظت واجب ہے سو اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ حفاظت کا واجب ہونا تبعا ہے نہ کہ قصداً۔ اس لئے کہ عقد کا ورود اجیر مشترک کے عمل پر ہے۔ حفاظت معقود عالیہ نہیں ہے۔ پس حفاظت اصلی مقصود نہیں بلکہ وہ چونکہ اقامت عمل کا وسیلہ ہے اس لئے تبعا مقصود ہے اسی لئے حفاظت کے مقابلہ میں کچھ اجرت نہیں ہوتی بخلاف اس شخص کے کہ جس کو ودیعت اجرت پر دی گئی ہو کہ اس پر حفاظت قصد اواجب ہے یہاں تک کہ اس کے مقابلہ میں اجرت ہے۔
تنبیہ اجیر مشترک کے ضامن ہونے میں صحابہ کرام کا اختلاف ہے۔ بعض کے نزدیک ضامن ہوتا ہے اور بعض کے نزدیک ضامن نہیں ہوتا بلکہ ایسا بھی ہے کہ ایک ہی شخص سے مختلف روایات وارد ہیں۔ چنانچہ حضرت علی سے جہاں اجیر مشترک کے ضامن ہونے کی روایت ہے وہیں عدم ضمان بھی مروی ہے۔ اس لئے بعض متاخرین فقہا ء نے یہ فتویٰ دیا ہے کہ اجیر ومستاجر دونوں جس مقدار پر چاہیں با ہم صلح کر لیں۔ ویسے فقیہ ابواللیث نے ذکر کیا ہے کہ فتویٰ امام ابو حنیفہ کے قول پر ہے۔ تاج الشریعہ، شیخ مرغینانی اور قاضی خان بھی اسی پر فتوی دیتے تھے۔ لیکن علامہ زیلعی وغیرہ نے کہا ہے ۔ کہ آج کل فتویٰ صاحبین کے قول پر ہے۔ کیونکہ لوگوں کے حالات متغیر ہو چکے اور اموال کی حفاظت اسی سے ہو سکتی ہے کہ اجیر سے ضمان لیا جائے ۔ ائمہ ثلاثہ کا قول بھی یہی ہے۔

جو چیز اجیر مشترک کے عمل سے تلف ہو جائے اس کا حکم
قال و ما تلف بعمله كتخريق الثوب من دقَه وزَلِق الحمّال وانقطاع الحبل الذي يشد به المكارى الحمل وغرق السفينة من مده مضمون عليه وقال زفر والشافعي لا ضمان عليه لانه امره بالفعل مطلقا فينتظمه بنوعيه المعيب والسليم وصار كاجير الوحد ومعين القصار ولنا ان الداخل تحت الاذن ما هو الداخل تحت العقد وهو العمل الصالح لانه هو الوسيلة الى الاثر وهو المعقود عليه حقيقة حتى لو حصل بفعل الغير يجب الاجر فلم يكن المفسد مأذونا فيه بخلاف المعين لانه متبرع فلا يمكن تقييده بالمصلح لانه يمتنع عن التبرع وفيما نحن فيه يعمل بالاجر فامكن تقييده وبخلاف الاجير الوحد على ما نذكره ان شاء الله تعالى وانقطاع الحمل من قلة اهتمامه فكان من صنيعه قال الا انه لا يضمن به بني آدم ممن غرق في السفينة أو سقط من الدابة وان كان بسوقه وقوده لان الواجب ضمان الآدمى وانه لا يجب بالعقد وانما يجب بالجناية ولهذا يجب على العاقلة وضمان العقود لا تتحمله العاقلة

توضیح اللغة تلف (س) تسلفاً برباد ہونا۔ تخریق پھاڑنا۔ دق کونا۔ زلق (س) پھسلنا_حمال قلی_حبل رییشدشدا باندهنامکاری جانوروں کو کرایہ پر دینے والا حمل بوجھ سفینه سنتی - مد کھینچنا۔ معیب عیب دار - قصار دھوبی۔سوق (ن) جانور کو پیچھے سے ہانکنا۔ قود (ن) جانور کو آگے سے کھینچنا جناية جرم ۔ ترجمہ اور جو تلف ہو جائے اجیر کے عمل سے جیسے کپڑے کو پھاڑ دینا کوٹنے سے۔ حمال کا پھسل جانا اس رسی کا ٹوٹ جانا جس سے کرایہ پر دینے والا بوجھ باندھتا ہے اور کشتی کا ڈوب جانا اس کے کھینچنے سے یہ سب اجیر پر مضمون ہے۔ امام زفر اور امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں کہ اس پر ضمان نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ مالک نے اس کو مطلقاً کام کرنے کا حکم کیا ہے تو یہ معیب و سلیم ہر دو کو شامل ہوگا اور یہ ایسا ہو گیا جیسے اجیر خاص اور دھوبی کا مددگار ۔ ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ اجازت کے تحت میں وہی داخل ہے جو عقد کے تحت میں داخل ہے اور وہ صحیح و درست کام ہے۔ کیونکہ یہی حصول اثر کا وسیلہ ہے اور در حقیقت یہ اثر ہی معقود علیہ ہے یہاں تک کہ اگر یہ غیر کے فعل سے حاصل ہو تو اجرت واجب ہوگی پس مفسد عمل داخل اجازت نہ ہوا بخلاف معین کے کیونکہ وہ احسان کنندہ ہے۔ تو اس کے کام کو مصلح ہونے کے ساتھ مقید نہیں کیا جا سکتا۔ ورنہ وہ احسان کرنے سے باز رہے گا اور مانحن فیہ میں وہ اجرت پر کام کرتا ہے تو اسکے عمل کے درست ہونے کی قید لگانا ممکن ہے۔ اور بخلاف اجیر خاص کے۔ بنابر آنکہ ہم ذکر کریں گے انشاء اللہ تعالیٰ اور رتی کا ٹوٹنا اس کے اہتمام کی کوتاہی سے ہے تو یہ اس کی حرکت کا نتیجہ ہے۔ مگر وہ آدمی کا ضامن نہ ہوگا جو کشتی میں غرق ہو جائے یا بھاڑے کے ٹو پر سے گر مرے۔ اگر چہ اس کے ہانکنے یا کھینچنے سے ہو۔ اس لئے کہ واجب تو آدمی کا ضمان ہے۔ جو عقد سے واجب نہیں ہوتا بلکہ جرم سے واجب ہوتا ہے۔ اسی لئے یہ عاقلہ پر واجب ہوتا ہے اور جو ضمان بوجہ عقد ہو وہ عاقلہ نہیں اٹھائے۔ تشریح قوله وما تلف الخ- جو چیز اجیر مشترک کے عمل سے تلف ہو جائے وہ اس کا ضامن ہوگا۔ جیسے دھوبی کے کوٹنے سے کپڑا پھٹ جائے یا مزدور کے پھسلنے یا جس رسی سے بوجھ بندھا ہوا تھا اس کے ٹوٹنے سے مال ضائع ہو جائے یا ملاح کے بے قاعدہ کھینچنے سے کشتی ڈوب جائے اور مال غرق ہو جائے تو ان سب صورتوں میں اجیر مشترک ضامن ہوگا۔ امام مالک، امام احمد اور ابن ابی لیلی بھی اسی
Book of Ijarah. Ashraf al-Hidayah, Urdu commentary on Hidayah, Volume 12. Except if the taxi (hired vehicle) is destroyed due to a cause from which escape is not possible, such as it dying its own death, or fire breaking out, or an enemy attack destroying it, etc. Their evidence is that 'Umar and 'Ali used to take guarantee from the goldsmith and dyer. Thus, Imam Bayhaqi narrated from 'Ali via Imam Shafi'i: 'He used to make the dyer and goldsmith liable and said: People cannot do without that.' The statement 'and because preservation...' - this is the rational proof of the two disciples (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad): that preservation is obligatory upon the hired worker because he cannot work without preservation. So preservation is also included in the contract, and a contract of exchange necessitates the safety of the subject matter. Thus, if the property is destroyed by a cause from which avoidance is possible, such as theft or usurpation, this is negligence on the part of the hired worker, so he is liable. Similarly, in a deposit, if the depositor fixes a wage for preservation for the depositary, then if it is destroyed, the depositary is liable. Yes, if it is destroyed by a cause from which escape is impossible, e.g., a goat in the custody of a shepherd dies naturally, or a general fire occurs, or a calamity befalls, then in such a case, he is not liable because there is no negligence from the hired worker. The statement 'and Abu Hanifa's statement...' - Imam Abu Hanifa's proof is that the common hired worker has a trust (amanah) with him, and there is no liability in trust. This is supported by what al-Daraqutni narrated: 'No liability upon a trusted person.' The reason is that liability is either due to transgression or due to contract, and neither exists here. Transgression is absent because the hired worker gained possession through the hire contract, and liability cannot be due to contract because the contract is on the work, not on the property itself. So the property is not guaranteed by contract. This is why if the item is destroyed by a cause from which avoidance is impossible, the hired worker is not liable by consensus. If the mentioned property were in his possession as a guarantee, he would certainly be liable, like a usurper is liable in all cases. The statement 'and preservation is binding upon him...' - as for saying that preservation is obligatory upon the hired worker, the answer is that preservation is binding subordinately, not primarily. Because the contract is upon the work of the common hired worker, preservation is not the subject matter. So preservation is not the main objective, but it is intended subordinately because it is a means to perform the work. Therefore, no wage is fixed for preservation, unlike the person who receives a deposit for a wage, where preservation is primarily obligatory and there is a wage for it. Note: There is a disagreement among the Companions regarding the liability of the common hired worker. Some consider him liable, others not. In fact, different narrations exist from the same person, such as from 'Ali, where both liability and non-liability are narrated. Therefore, some later jurists gave the fatwa that the hired worker and the hirer should reconcile on any amount they wish. Otherwise, Faqih Abu al-Layth mentioned that the fatwa is according to Imam Abu Hanifa's statement. Taj al-Shari'ah, Shaykh al-Marghinani, and Qadi Khan also gave fatwa accordingly. But Allamah Zayla'i and others said that nowadays the fatwa is according to the statement of the two disciples (Sahibayn) because people's conditions have changed, and the protection of wealth can only be achieved by taking a guarantee from the hired worker. The three Imams (Malik, Shafi'i, Ahmad) also hold this view. The ruling on what is destroyed by the work of the common hired worker: He said: And what is destroyed by his work, such as tearing the cloth by beating it, the porter slipping, the rope breaking by which the carrier ties the load, and the sinking of the ship by his pulling, is guaranteed upon him. Zufar and al-Shafi'i said: There is no liability upon him, because the owner commanded him to do the act absolutely, so it includes both its defective and sound types, and it becomes like a specific hired worker (ajir khas) and the helper of the launderer. Our proof: That which enters under permission is what enters under the contract, which is sound work, because it is the means to the effect, and the effect is the actual subject matter. So if the effect is achieved by the act of another, the wage is due. Therefore, the destructive act is not permitted. Unlike the volunteer, because he is a benefactor, so his work cannot be restricted to what is proper, otherwise he would refrain from beneficence. In our case, he works for a wage, so it is possible to restrict him. And unlike the specific hired worker, as we will mention, God willing. The breaking of the load is due to his lack of care, so it is from his own doing. He said: But he is not liable for a human being, such as one who drowns in the ship or falls from the animal, even if it is by his driving or pulling, because the obligatory is the guarantee of a human being, which is not obligatory by contract but by crime. Hence it is upon the 'aqilah (tribal surety), and guarantees of contracts are not borne by the 'aqilah.
Source pages p. 84

Commentary
This passage is a detailed treatment of the liability of the common hired worker (ajir mushtarak) for goods that are destroyed by his work. It begins by presenting the ruling that such destruction is guaranteed (mazmun) — meaning the worker is liable. Examples include a cloth torn by beating, a porter slipping, a rope breaking, or a ship sinking due to the worker's pulling. The passage then presents the opposition of Imam Zufar and Imam al-Shafi'i, who argue that the worker should not be liable because the employer gave absolute permission to work, which includes both defective and sound outcomes, similar to a specific hired worker or a volunteer assistant. The Hanafi response is that permission under the contract only covers sound work, as the actual subject matter of the contract is the effect (e.g., clean clothes, transport), and the work is merely a means. If the work is destructive, it is outside the scope of permission. The Hanafis distinguish this from a volunteer, whose work cannot be restricted because he might refrain from beneficence, whereas a hired worker can be restricted. They also distinguish from a specific hired worker (ajir khas), who is not liable for destruction as he is considered a trustee. The passage further specifies that the worker is not liable for injury to a human being (blood money) because such liability arises from crime (jinayah), not contract, and is borne by the 'aqilah. The earlier part of the text on page 84 explains the dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two disciples (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) regarding the basis of liability. Abu Hanifa considers the worker a trustee (amin) and thus not liable except for transgression, while the two disciples argue that preservation (hifz) is a contractual duty, making the worker liable for destruction from avoidable causes. The passage also notes the evolution of the fatwa: earlier scholars followed Abu Hanifa, but later scholars like Zayla'i adopted the view of the two disciples due to changing circumstances. The commentary emphasizes the analytical reasoning (talil) behind each position.

Key Terms
أجير مشترك (ajir mushtarak): A common hired worker who works for multiple people or for a wage per task, not exclusively for one person. His liability is disputed.
أجير خاص (ajir khas): A specific hired worker who is hired exclusively for a period or for a specific task. He is not liable for destruction of goods in his custody.
ضمان (daman): Liability or guarantee to compensate for loss or destruction of property.
أمانة (amanah): Trust; property held without liability for accidental destruction, as per Abu Hanifa's view of the ajir mushtarak.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, why is the ajir mushtarak not liable for a person who drowns in the ship due to his pulling?
A) Because it is an act of God
B) Because liability for human life arises from crime, not contract
C) Because the owner assumed the risk
D) Because the worker is a trustee

Key Takeaway
The ajir mushtarak's liability is limited to avoidable property damage; human life is governed by criminal law (jinayat), not contract.

Ijarah — Hire and Lease
intermediate
8 min
Liability of the Common Hireling (Ajir Mushtarak)
Ruling on ajir mushtarak's liability with examples and distinction

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that a common hireling is liable for property damage caused by his action, and distinguish his case from that of a special hireling.

Core Idea
A common hireling works for wages and is liable for damage; a special hireling works gratuitously and is not.

Imagine you hire a porter to carry your goods. If he slips and the goods are damaged, is he responsible? According to the Hanafi school, the answer depends on whether the porter is a common hireling (works for many clients) or a special hireling (exclusively for you). This lesson explains the Hanafi ruling and the key distinction.

Guided Path
1
Identify the hireling type
Determine if the hireling is ajir mushtarak (common) or ajir wahid (special). The key indicator: does he work for multiple employers or a single one? Does he receive wages for the task?
2
State the ruling for ajir mushtarak
He is liable (mazmun) for any property damage caused by his action. Examples: porter slipping, fuller tearing cloth, boatman sinking ship.
3
State the ruling for ajir wahid/mu'ayyan
He is not liable for damage, because his work is gratuitous (tabarru').
4
Apply the distinction to scenarios
Given a scenario (e.g., a painter hired to paint a house but accidentally spills paint on furniture), classify the hireling and determine liability.

جو چیز اجیر مشترک کے عمل سے تلف ہو جائے اس کا حکم
قال و ما تلف بعمله كتخريق الثوب من دقَه وزَلِق الحمّال وانقطاع الحبل الذي يشد به المكارى الحمل وغرق السفينة من مده مضمون عليه وقال زفر والشافعي لا ضمان عليه لانه امره بالفعل مطلقا فينتظمه بنوعيه المعيب والسليم وصار كاجير الوحد ومعين القصار ولنا ان الداخل تحت الاذن ما هو الداخل تحت العقد وهو العمل الصالح لانه هو الوسيلة الى الاثر وهو المعقود عليه حقيقة حتى لو حصل بفعل الغير يجب الاجر فلم يكن المفسد مأذونا فيه بخلاف المعين لانه متبرع فلا يمكن تقييده بالمصلح لانه يمتنع عن التبرع وفيما نحن فيه يعمل بالاجر فامكن تقييده وبخلاف الاجير الوحد على ما نذكره ان شاء الله تعالى
توضیح اللغة تلف (س) تسلفاً برباد ہونا۔ تخریق پھاڑنا۔ دق کونا۔ زلق (س) پھسلنا_حمال قلی_حبل رییشدشدا باندهنامکاری جانوروں کو کرایہ پر دینے والا حمل بوجھ سفینه سنتی - مد کھینچنا۔ معیب عیب دار - قصار دھوبی۔سوق (ن) جانور کو پیچھے سے ہانکنا۔ قود (ن) جانور کو آگے سے کھینچنا جناية جرم ۔
ترجمہ اور جو تلف ہو جائے اجیر کے عمل سے جیسے کپڑے کو پھاڑ دینا کوٹنے سے۔ حمال کا پھسل جانا اس رسی کا ٹوٹ جانا جس سے کرایہ پر دینے والا بوجھ باندھتا ہے اور کشتی کا ڈوب جانا اس کے کھینچنے سے یہ سب اجیر پر مضمون ہے۔ امام زفر اور امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں کہ اس پر ضمان نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ مالک نے اس کو مطلقاً کام کرنے کا حکم کیا ہے تو یہ معیب و سلیم ہر دو کو شامل ہوگا اور یہ ایسا ہو گیا جیسے اجیر خاص اور دھوبی کا مددگار ۔ ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ اجازت کے تحت میں وہی داخل ہے جو عقد کے تحت میں داخل ہے اور وہ صحیح و درست کام ہے۔ کیونکہ یہی حصول اثر کا وسیلہ ہے اور در حقیقت یہ اثر ہی معقود علیہ ہے یہاں تک کہ اگر یہ غیر کے فعل سے حاصل ہو تو اجرت واجب ہوگی پس مفسد عمل داخل اجازت نہ ہوا بخلاف معین کے کیونکہ وہ احسان کنندہ ہے۔ تو اس کے کام کو مصلح ہونے کے ساتھ مقید نہیں کیا جا سکتا۔ ورنہ وہ احسان کرنے سے باز رہے گا اور مانحن فیہ میں وہ اجرت پر کام کرتا ہے تو اسکے عمل کے درست ہونے کی قید لگانا ممکن ہے۔ اور بخلاف اجیر خاص کے۔ بنابر آنکہ ہم ذکر کریں گے انشاء اللہ تعالیٰ
تشریح قوله وما تلف الخ- جو چیز اجیر مشترک کے عمل سے تلف ہو جائے وہ اس کا ضامن ہوگا۔ جیسے دھوبی کے کوٹنے سے کپڑا پھٹ جائے یا مزدور کے پھسلنے یا جس رسی سے بوجھ بندھا ہوا تھا اس کے ٹوٹنے سے مال ضائع ہو جائے یا ملاح کے بے قاعدہ کھینچنے سے کشتی ڈوب جائے اور مال غرق ہو جائے تو ان سب صورتوں میں اجیر مشترک ضامن ہوگا۔ امام مالک، امام احمد اور ابن ابی لیلی بھی اسی كے قائل ہیں اور یہ حضرت عمر عبید اللہ بن عقبہ، قاضی شریح، حسن اور حکم سے بھی مروی ہے۔ امام زفر اور امام شافعی کے نزدیک ضامن نہ ہوگا۔ یہ حضرت عطاء اور طاؤس سے بھی مروی ہے۔ کیونکہ اس کا عمل مالک کی مطلق اجازت سے واقع ہوا ہے تو معیب و سلیم ہر دو کو شامل ہوگا۔ پس ایساہو گیا جیسے اجیر خاص یا معین قصار کہ ان پر ضمان نہیں ہوتا۔ اگر چہ کام بگڑ جائے۔ قوله ولنا ان الداخل ..... الخ - ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ تحت الا ذن وہی عمل داخل ہے۔ جو تحت العقد داخل ہے اور وہ عمل صالح ہے نہ کہ عمل مفسد کیونکہ عین بھٹی میں اس کے فعل کا اثر جو در حقیقت معقود علیہ ہے وہ عمل صالح ہی کے ذریعہ سے حاصل ہو سکتا ہے۔ مثلاً کپڑے میں کندی یا رنگ یا بیل بوٹے کا اثر اسی وقت پیدا ہو گا جب کام ٹھیک طریقہ پر ہو۔ اور یہ اثر ہی درحقیقت معقود علیہ ہے یہاں تک کہ اگر یہ اثر غیر اجیر کے فعل سے حاصل ہو۔ مثلاً درزی یا رنگریز نے کپڑا کسی دوسرے سے سلایا رنگا یا تو اجرت واجب ہو جاتی ہے (بشرطیکہ بذات خود کام کرنا مشروط نہ ہو ) معلوم ہوا کہ بگاڑ دینے والا کام داخل اجازت نہیں ہے بخلاف معین قصار کے کہ وہ اس لئے ضامن نہیں ہوتا کہ اس نے وہ کام از راہ احسان کیا ہے تو اس کے حق میں عمل مصلح اور درست کام کرنے کی قید نہیں ہوسکتی۔ ورنہ وہ احسان کرنے سے باز رہے گا۔ رہا زیر بحث مسئلہ سواس میں اجیر اجرت پر کام کرتا ہے تو اس کے حق میں درست کام کرنے کی قید لگانا ممکن ہے۔ بخلاف اجیر خاص کے کہ اس کے ضامن نہ ہونے کی وجہ آگے آرہی ہے۔
The Book of Hiring. Ashraf al-Hidaya, Urdu commentary on Hidayah, Volume 12. The ruling on what is destroyed by the action of the common hireling. He said: And what is destroyed by his action, such as tearing the cloth from pounding, the porter slipping, the rope breaking that the hirer ties the load with, and the ship sinking from his pulling, are guaranteed against him. Zufar and al-Shafi'i said: There is no liability upon him, because he commanded him to act absolutely, so it includes both types: defective and sound, and it becomes like the special hireling and the specified fuller. Our proof is that what enters under permission is what enters under the contract, which is proper work, because it is the means to the effect, and the effect is the actual object of the contract, such that if it occurs by another's action, the wage becomes obligatory. So the corrupting action was not permitted. Unlike the specified one, because he is a gratuitous actor, so he cannot be restricted to proper work, as he would refrain from gratuity. In our case, he works for wages, so restriction is possible. And unlike the special hireling, as we will mention, God willing. Lexicon: talf (destroyed), takhriq (tearing), daqq (pounding), zalaq (slipped), hammal (porter), habl (rope), makkari (hirer of animals), himl (load), safinah (ship), madd (pulling), mu'ayyab (defective), qassar (fuller), sawq (driving from behind), qawd (pulling from front), jinayah (crime). Translation: And what is destroyed by the hireling's action, such as tearing cloth by pounding, the porter slipping, the rope breaking by which the hirer ties the load, and the ship sinking from his pulling—all these are guaranteed against the hireling. Imam Zufar and Imam Shafi'i say that there is no liability on him, because the owner commanded the act absolutely, so it includes both defective and sound, and it becomes like the special hireling and the fuller's helper. Our proof is that what enters under permission is what enters under the contract, which is proper and correct work, because it is the means to obtaining the effect, and in reality, the effect is the object of the contract. If the effect occurs by another's action, the wage is still obligatory. So the corrupting action is not included in permission. Unlike the specified one, because he is doing a favor, so his work cannot be restricted to proper work, otherwise he would refrain from doing the favor. In our case, he works for wages, so restricting him to proper work is possible. And unlike the special hireling, as we will mention, God willing. Commentary: His statement 'and what is destroyed by his action'—whatever is destroyed by the common hireling's action, he is liable for it. For example, the fuller's pounding tears the cloth, or the worker slips, or the rope used to tie the load breaks causing loss of property, or the boatman's irregular pulling causes the boat to sink and property to drown—in all these cases the common hireling is liable. Imam Malik, Imam Ahmad, and Ibn Abi Layla also hold this view, and it is narrated from 'Umar, 'Ubaydullah ibn 'Uqba, Qadi Shurayh, Hasan, and Hakam. According to Imam Zufar and Imam Shafi'i, he is not liable; this is also narrated from 'Ata and Tawus. Because his action occurred with the owner's absolute permission, so it includes both defective and sound. Thus it becomes like the special hireling or the specified fuller, who are not liable even if the work is ruined. His statement 'our proof is that what enters under permission...'—our proof is that only the action that enters under the contract enters under permission, and that is proper work, not corrupting work. For the effect of his action, which is the actual object of the contract, can only be obtained through proper work. For example, the effect of embossing, dyeing, or patterns on cloth only occurs when done correctly. And this effect is the object of the contract such that if obtained by another's action, e.g., the tailor or dyer gets someone else to sew or dye, the wage becomes obligatory (provided doing it himself is not stipulated). Thus we see that the corrupting action is not included in permission. Unlike the specified fuller: he is not liable because he did the work as a favor, so his work cannot be restricted to proper work, otherwise he would refrain from the favor. In the case under discussion, the hireling works for wages, so restricting him to proper work is possible. Unlike the special hireling, whose reason for non-liability will come later.
Source pages p. 85

Commentary
This passage states the ruling on the liability of the common hireling (ajir mushtarak) for property damage caused by his action. The author begins by presenting the Hanafi ruling: the common hireling is liable (mazmun) for any property that is destroyed by his action, such as a cloth torn by the fuller's pounding, goods lost due to a porter slipping, a load falling from a rope breaking, or a ship sinking from the boatman's pulling. The passage then records the opposing view of Imam Zufar (a Hanafi scholar) and Imam al-Shafi'i: they hold that the hireling is not liable because the owner gave absolute permission to act, and the action encompasses both defective and sound outcomes, analogous to a special hireling or specified fuller who are not liable for damage. The author then presents the Hanafi proof (dalil): only the act that is the object of the contract enters into the owner's permission, and that is proper work (al-'amal al-salih), because proper work is the means to the desired effect, which is the true subject of the contract. If the desired effect occurs by someone else's action, the hireling still deserves his wage, indicating that the effect—not the defective work—is the contractual obligation. Therefore, a corrupting action is not included in the permission. The Hanafi proof distinguishes between the common hireling and the gratuitous worker (mutabarri'): the gratuitous worker cannot be restricted to proper work because he might then refuse to do the favor; but the common hireling works for wages, so restriction is feasible. The passage also distinguishes the common hireling from the special hireling (ajir wahid), whose case will be explained later. Finally, the Urdu commentary (Sharh) expands on the ruling, mentioning that the same view is held by Malik, Ahmad, and Ibn Abi Layla, and reports from many early authorities. It restates the arguments, including examples like a tailor or dyer who delegates the work—the hirer still gets the wage because the effect is what matters.

Key Terms
أجير مشترك (ajir mushtarak): A hireling who works for multiple people or for the public, and his work is not exclusively for one employer; he is hired for a specific task.
ضمان (daman): Legal liability to compensate for loss or damage; obligation to pay the value of the destroyed property.
أجير خاص (ajir wahid): A special hireling whose work is exclusively for one employer for a specified period; he is not liable for damage caused by his work.
معين (mu'ayyan): A specified hireling designated for a specific task, often used interchangeably with ajir wahid in this context.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following best explains why a common hireling (ajir mushtarak) is liable for property damage according to the Hanafi school?
A) He works for wages, so he can be restricted to proper work.
B) He works for free, so he must be careful.
C) The owner always supersedes the hireling's permission.
D) The law imposes strict liability regardless.

Key Takeaway
A common hireling is liable for damage because his permission is limited to proper work, unlike a gratuitous worker who is not liable.

Ijarah — Hire and Lease
advanced
10 min
The Dispute on the Common Hireling's Liability: Hanafi vs. Shafi'i/Zufar
Inter-madhhab dispute on ajir mushtarak's liability with Hanafi proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi proof for the common hireling's liability and critically evaluate the opposing argument from the Shafi'i school and Imam Zufar.

Core Idea
The Hanafi proof: only proper work is permitted; defective work is unauthorized, so liability arises.

While the Hanafi school holds the common hireling liable for damage, other scholars disagree. Imam Zufar (Hanafi) and Imam al-Shafi'i argue that absolute permission covers all outcomes, making the hireling not liable. This lesson unpacks the Hanafi proof and how it counters the opposing view.

Guided Path
1
State the opposing position
Zufar and Shafi'i say no liability because the owner gave absolute permission.
2
Identify the Hanafi proof
The proof is that only the contracted work (proper work) enters permission, as the effect (athar) is the true object.
3
Analyze the proof: permission vs. contract
Understand that the contract is for the effect, not the act itself, so defective work is outside permission.
4
Apply the proof to examples
Show why the common hireling's defective actions are not covered.
5
Distinguish from gratuitous workers
The proof holds because the hireling works for wages; gratuitous workers cannot be restricted.

تشریح قوله وما تلف الخ- جو چیز اجیر مشترک کے عمل سے تلف ہو جائے وہ اس کا ضامن ہوگا۔ جیسے دھوبی کے کوٹنے سے کپڑا پھٹ جائے یا مزدور کے پھسلنے یا جس رسی سے بوجھ بندھا ہوا تھا اس کے ٹوٹنے سے مال ضائع ہو جائے یا ملاح کے بے قاعدہ کھینچنے سے کشتی ڈوب جائے اور مال غرق ہو جائے تو ان سب صورتوں میں اجیر مشترک ضامن ہوگا۔ امام مالک، امام احمد اور ابن ابی لیلی بھی اسی كے قائل ہیں اور یہ حضرت عمر عبید اللہ بن عقبہ، قاضی شریح، حسن اور حکم سے بھی مروی ہے۔ امام زفر اور امام شافعی کے نزدیک ضامن نہ ہوگا۔ یہ حضرت عطاء اور طاؤس سے بھی مروی ہے۔ کیونکہ اس کا عمل مالک کی مطلق اجازت سے واقع ہوا ہے تو معیب و سلیم ہر دو کو شامل ہوگا۔ پس ایساہو گیا جیسے اجیر خاص یا معین قصار کہ ان پر ضمان نہیں ہوتا۔ اگر چہ کام بگڑ جائے۔ قوله ولنا ان الداخل ..... الخ - ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ تحت الا ذن وہی عمل داخل ہے۔ جو تحت العقد داخل ہے اور وہ عمل صالح ہے نہ کہ عمل مفسد کیونکہ عین بھٹی میں اس کے فعل کا اثر جو در حقیقت معقود علیہ ہے وہ عمل صالح ہی کے ذریعہ سے حاصل ہو سکتا ہے۔ مثلاً کپڑے میں کندی یا رنگ یا بیل بوٹے کا اثر اسی وقت پیدا ہو گا جب کام ٹھیک طریقہ پر ہو۔ اور یہ اثر ہی درحقیقت معقود علیہ ہے یہاں تک کہ اگر یہ اثر غیر اجیر کے فعل سے حاصل ہو۔ مثلاً درزی یا رنگریز نے کپڑا کسی دوسرے سے سلایا رنگا یا تو اجرت واجب ہو جاتی ہے (بشرطیکہ بذات خود کام کرنا مشروط نہ ہو ) معلوم ہوا کہ بگاڑ دینے والا کام داخل اجازت نہیں ہے بخلاف معین قصار کے کہ وہ اس لئے ضامن نہیں ہوتا کہ اس نے وہ کام از راہ احسان کیا ہے تو اس کے حق میں عمل مصلح اور درست کام کرنے کی قید نہیں ہوسکتی۔ ورنہ وہ احسان کرنے سے باز رہے گا۔ رہا زیر بحث مسئلہ سواس میں اجیر اجرت پر کام کرتا ہے تو اس کے حق میں درست کام کرنے کی قید لگانا ممکن ہے۔ بخلاف اجیر خاص کے کہ اس کے ضامن نہ ہونے کی وجہ آگے آرہی ہے۔
The Book of Hiring. Ashraf al-Hidaya, Urdu commentary on Hidayah, Volume 12. The ruling on what is destroyed by the action of the common hireling. He said: And what is destroyed by his action, such as tearing the cloth from pounding, the porter slipping, the rope breaking that the hirer ties the load with, and the ship sinking from his pulling, are guaranteed against him. Zufar and al-Shafi'i said: There is no liability upon him, because he commanded him to act absolutely, so it includes both types: defective and sound, and it becomes like the special hireling and the specified fuller. Our proof is that what enters under permission is what enters under the contract, which is proper work, because it is the means to the effect, and the effect is the actual object of the contract, such that if it occurs by another's action, the wage becomes obligatory. So the corrupting action was not permitted. Unlike the specified one, because he is a gratuitous actor, so he cannot be restricted to proper work, as he would refrain from gratuity. In our case, he works for wages, so restriction is possible. And unlike the special hireling, as we will mention, God willing. Lexicon: talf (destroyed), takhriq (tearing), daqq (pounding), zalaq (slipped), hammal (porter), habl (rope), makkari (hirer of animals), himl (load), safinah (ship), madd (pulling), mu'ayyab (defective), qassar (fuller), sawq (driving from behind), qawd (pulling from front), jinayah (crime). Translation: And what is destroyed by the hireling's action, such as tearing cloth by pounding, the porter slipping, the rope breaking by which the hirer ties the load, and the ship sinking from his pulling—all these are guaranteed against the hireling. Imam Zufar and Imam Shafi'i say that there is no liability on him, because the owner commanded the act absolutely, so it includes both defective and sound, and it becomes like the special hireling and the fuller's helper. Our proof is that what enters under permission is what enters under the contract, which is proper and correct work, because it is the means to obtaining the effect, and in reality, the effect is the object of the contract. If the effect occurs by another's action, the wage is still obligatory. So the corrupting action is not included in permission. Unlike the specified one, because he is doing a favor, so his work cannot be restricted to proper work, otherwise he would refrain from doing the favor. In our case, he works for wages, so restricting him to proper work is possible. And unlike the special hireling, as we will mention, God willing. Commentary: His statement 'and what is destroyed by his action'—whatever is destroyed by the common hireling's action, he is liable for it. For example, the fuller's pounding tears the cloth, or the worker slips, or the rope used to tie the load breaks causing loss of property, or the boatman's irregular pulling causes the boat to sink and property to drown—in all these cases the common hireling is liable. Imam Malik, Imam Ahmad, and Ibn Abi Layla also hold this view, and it is narrated from 'Umar, 'Ubaydullah ibn 'Uqba, Qadi Shurayh, Hasan, and Hakam. According to Imam Zufar and Imam Shafi'i, he is not liable; this is also narrated from 'Ata and Tawus. Because his action occurred with the owner's absolute permission, so it includes both defective and sound. Thus it becomes like the special hireling or the specified fuller, who are not liable even if the work is ruined. His statement 'our proof is that what enters under permission...'—our proof is that only the action that enters under the contract enters under permission, and that is proper work, not corrupting work. For the effect of his action, which is the actual object of the contract, can only be obtained through proper work. For example, the effect of embossing, dyeing, or patterns on cloth only occurs when done correctly. And this effect is the object of the contract such that if obtained by another's action, e.g., the tailor or dyer gets someone else to sew or dye, the wage becomes obligatory (provided doing it himself is not stipulated). Thus we see that the corrupting action is not included in permission. Unlike the specified fuller: he is not liable because he did the work as a favor, so his work cannot be restricted to proper work, otherwise he would refrain from the favor. In the case under discussion, the hireling works for wages, so restricting him to proper work is possible. Unlike the special hireling, whose reason for non-liability will come later.
Source pages p. 85

Commentary
This passage states the ruling on the liability of the common hireling (ajir mushtarak) for property damage caused by his action. The author begins by presenting the Hanafi ruling: the common hireling is liable (mazmun) for any property that is destroyed by his action, such as a cloth torn by the fuller's pounding, goods lost due to a porter slipping, a load falling from a rope breaking, or a ship sinking from the boatman's pulling. The passage then records the opposing view of Imam Zufar (a Hanafi scholar) and Imam al-Shafi'i: they hold that the hireling is not liable because the owner gave absolute permission to act, and the action encompasses both defective and sound outcomes, analogous to a special hireling or specified fuller who are not liable for damage. The author then presents the Hanafi proof (dalil): only the act that is the object of the contract enters into the owner's permission, and that is proper work (al-'amal al-salih), because proper work is the means to the desired effect, which is the true subject of the contract. If the desired effect occurs by someone else's action, the hireling still deserves his wage, indicating that the effect—not the defective work—is the contractual obligation. Therefore, a corrupting action is not included in the permission. The Hanafi proof distinguishes between the common hireling and the gratuitous worker (mutabarri'): the gratuitous worker cannot be restricted to proper work because he might then refuse to do the favor; but the common hireling works for wages, so restriction is feasible. The passage also distinguishes the common hireling from the special hireling (ajir wahid), whose case will be explained later. Finally, the Urdu commentary (Sharh) expands on the ruling, mentioning that the same view is held by Malik, Ahmad, and Ibn Abi Layla, and reports from many early authorities. It restates the arguments, including examples like a tailor or dyer who delegates the work—the hirer still gets the wage because the effect is what matters.

Key Terms
أجير مشترك (ajir mushtarak): A hireling who works for multiple people or for the public, and his work is not exclusively for one employer; he is hired for a specific task.
ضمان (daman): Legal liability to compensate for loss or damage; obligation to pay the value of the destroyed property.
أجير خاص (ajir wahid): A special hireling whose work is exclusively for one employer for a specified period; he is not liable for damage caused by his work.
معين (mu'ayyan): A specified hireling designated for a specific task, often used interchangeably with ajir wahid in this context.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the key element of the Hanafi proof that makes the common hireling liable?
A) The contract is for the effect, and proper work is the only means to it, so defective work is not permitted.
B) The hireling is insured by his contract.
C) The owner's permission is absolute.
D) The hireling is always considered negligent.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds the common hireling liable because the contract's object is the effect, and only proper work is permitted; defective work is unauthorized and incurs liability.
