The Hireling's Exception: No Liability for Human Life
Exception to hireling's liability: no guarantee for human life with proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that a common hireling is not liable for human life, and explain the legal proof (dalil) distinguishing contractual liability from tortious liability.

Core Idea
A hireling is liable for property but not human life — blood money falls on the 'aqila, not the hireling.

In the previous lesson, you learned that a common hireling is liable for damage to property caused by his action. However, this liability does not extend to human life or injury. Why? Because liability for a human being arises only from a tort (jinaya), not from a contract. This lesson explains the exception and its proof, including an important intra-Hanafi clarification regarding children.

Guided Path
1
Identify the exception
Read the passage carefully. The author states that the hireling is not liable 'for a human being from among those who drown in the ship or fall from the animal.' This is an exception to the general rule of liability for damages caused by his action.
The exception applies only to human life and injury, not to property.
2
Understand the two types of liability
The proof (dalil) given is: 'the liability for a human being is not established by contract, but only by tort.' Distinguish between contractual liability (daman al-'uqood) which governs property damage, and tortious liability (daman al-jinayat) which governs harm to persons.
Tortious liability for human life is borne by the 'aqila, not by the individual wrongdoer under contract.
3
Apply the rationale to examples
Apply the rule to the examples: if a boatman pulls improperly and a passenger drowns, or a rider falls due to the hireling's driving, the hireling does not pay diya. The compensation falls on the 'aqila of the hireling.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi dispute and correct position
Some scholars distinguished between a child who can sit on an animal and one who cannot, treating the latter as property. The correct view (narrated from Imam Abu Yusuf) holds no distinction: the hireling is never liable for any human life.
The mufta bihi (operative position) is that the exception applies to all humans regardless of age or ability.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله الا انه لا يضمن به بنی آدم ممن غرق في السفينة أو سقط من الدابة وان كان بسوقه وقوده لان الواجب ضمان الآدمى وانه لا يجب بالعقد وانما يجب بالجناية ولهذا يجب على العاقلة وضمان العقود لا تتحمله العاقلة
قوله الا انه لا يضمن به الخ - يقول سابق وما تلف بعمله مضمون عليه سے استثناء ہے مطلب یہ کہ اگر اجیر مشترک کے فعل سے کچھ تلف ہو جائے تو وہ ضامن صرف مال کا ضامن ہوگا بنی آدم کا ضامن نہ ہوگا۔ پس اگر ملاح نے بے قاعدہ کشتی کھینچی اور اس میں سے کوئی غرق ہو گیا یا بھاڑے کے ٹو سے گر کر مر گیا تو اجیر پر اسکی جان کا تاوان نہ ہوگا۔ اس لئے کہ جان کا تاوان عقد کی وجہ سے واجب نہیں ہوتا بلکہ قتل یا زخمی کرنے کے جرم سے واجب ہوتا ہے اسی لئے یہ تاوان قاتل کے عاقلہ (مددگار برادری ) پر پڑتا ہے اور جو تاوان عقد معاملہ کی وجہ سے واجب ہو اس کو عاقلہ نہیں اٹھاتے۔
قوله او سقط من الدابة .... الخ - بعض حضرات نے کہا ہے کہ یہ اس کی بابت ہے جو سواری پر بذات خود سوار ہو سکے اور سواری کی پیٹھ پر جم کر بیٹھ سکے۔ اگر بہت چھوٹا بچہ ہو جو خود نہیں بیٹھ سکتا تو اس کا حکم متاع کا سا ہے۔ لیکن صحیح یہ ہے کہ بڑے چھوٹے کا کوئی فرق نہیں۔ بہر صورت اجیر بنی آدم کا ضامن نہ ہو گا۔ ابن ساعہ نے امام ابو یوسف سے یونہی روایت کیا ہے و کذا ذکرہ التمر تاشي
His statement: 'But he is not liable for a human being from among those who drown in the ship or fall from the animal, even if it is by his driving or pulling, because the liability for a human life is not established by contract, but only by tort (jinaya). For this reason, it is obligatory upon the 'aqila (male relatives on the father's side), and liabilities of contracts are not borne by the 'aqila.'
Commentary on his statement 'except that he is not liable for a human being' - it is an exception from the earlier statement 'what is destroyed by his action is guaranteed against him'. The meaning is that if the common hireling's action causes some destruction, he is only liable for property, not for a human being. So if the boatman pulls the boat improperly and someone drowns, or falls from the animal and dies, the hireling is not liable for blood money (diya). Because blood money is not obligatory due to contract, but due to the crime of killing or wounding. Therefore, this compensation falls upon the 'aqila of the killer, and compensation that is due from a contract is not borne by the 'aqila.
His statement 'or falls from the animal' - some scholars said that this applies to one who can ride on his own and sit firmly on the animal's back. If it is a small child who cannot sit by himself, then his ruling is like that of goods. But the correct view is that there is no difference between old and young. In any case, the hireling is not liable for a human being. Ibn Sa'a narrated from Imam Abu Yusuf like this, and similarly mentioned in al-Tamartashi.
Source pages p. 86

Commentary
This passage provides an exception to the general ruling that the common hireling is liable for damage caused by his action. The exception is that he is not liable for human life or injury. The author first quotes the Arabic text from the matn: 'But he is not liable for a human being...' because liability for life is not established by contract (ijara) but only by tort (jinaya). If the hireling's action causes death, the compensation (diya) falls on the 'aqila (the paternal male relatives) of the hireling, not on the hireling himself, because contract liability is not borne by the 'aqila. The Urdu commentary then clarifies: if a boatman pulls improperly and someone drowns, or a rider falls from the animal due to the hireling's driving, the hireling does not pay blood money. The passage also addresses a sub-dispute: some scholars distinguish between a child who can sit independently and one who cannot, treating the latter as property. The correct Hanafi view (as narrated from Imam Abu Yusuf) is that there is no difference; the hireling is never liable for human life, regardless of age. This ruling is consistent with the principle that liability for human life arises only from deliberate or quasi-deliberate injury, not from contractual relationships.

Key Terms
بني آدم (bani adam): Human beings; in this context, the life or person of a human being as distinct from property (mal).
جناية (jinaya): Tort or crime causing harm to a person, such as killing or wounding; it triggers liability for diya (blood money) upon the 'aqila.
عاقلة ('aqila): The male relatives on the father's side (asaba) who are liable to pay blood money (diya) on behalf of the killer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is a common hireling not liable for human life according to the Hanafi school?
A) Because human life is not compensable under any circumstances.
B) Because liability for human life arises only from tort (jinaya), not from contract.
C) Because the employer is always liable for the hireling's actions.
D) Because the hireling is considered immune from liability.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school distinguishes contractual liability (for property) from tortious liability (for human life); the latter falls on the 'aqila, not on the hireling.

Common Hirer's Liability: Property Only, Not Human Life
Ruling with proof on common hirer's liability

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a common hirer's liability for accidental harm and explain the rational basis for distinguishing property from human life.

Core Idea
A common hirer guarantees property but not life—life indemnity is criminal, not contractual.

We often think that if someone causes harm while working, they must pay. But Hanafi fiqh draws a sharp line: property is guaranteed, human life is not. This lesson unpacks why, using the example of a boatman who accidentally drowns a passenger.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
What is the act being ruled? A common hirer (ajir mushtarak) causes harm through his action. The ruling: he is liable for property damage, but not for human life.
The text begins with an exception: 'except that he is not liable for it (human life).'
2
Understand the exception
The author clarifies that the earlier statement 'whatever is destroyed by his action is subject to guarantee' applies only to property. Human life is an exception.
3
Grasp the rational proof
Why is he not liable for life? Because life indemnity (diyah) is not a contractual obligation; it arises from the crime of killing or wounding. Therefore, it falls on the 'aqila (paternal relatives), not on the hirer based on the contract.
This is a rational (aqli) proof, distinguishing between contractual and criminal liability.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Some scholars distinguished between an adult rider (no liability) and a small child (treated as property). The correct view, narrated from Abu Yusuf, is that there is no difference—the hirer is not liable for any human life.
The author affirms this with citation from Ibn Sa'ah.
5
Confirm the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that the common hirer is never liable for human life, regardless of the victim's age or ability to ride.
This is the operative ruling for fatwa.

Source Text

قوله الا انه لا يضمن به الخ - يقول سابق وما تلف بعمله مضمون عليه “ سے استثناء ہے مطلب یہ کہ اگر اجیر مشترک کے فعل سے کچھ تلف ہو جائے تو وہ ضامن صرف مال کا ضامن ہوگا بنی آدم کا ضامن نہ ہوگا۔ پس اگر ملاح نے بے قاعدہ کشتی کھینچی اور اس میں سے کوئی غرق ہو گیا یا بھاڑے کے ٹو سے گر کر مر گیا تو اجیر پر اسکی جان کا تاوان نہ ہوگا۔ اس لئے کہ جان کا تاوان عقد کی وجہ سے واجب نہیں ہوتا بلکہ قتل یا زخمی کرنے کے جرم سے واجب ہوتا ہے اسی لئے یہ تاوان قاتل کے عاقلہ (مددگار برادری ) پر پڑتا ہے اور جو تا وان عقد معاملہ کی وجہ سے واجب ہو اس کو عاقلہ نہیں اٹھاتے۔
قوله اوسقط من الدابة .... الخ - بعض حضرات نے کہا ہے کہ یہ اس کی بابت ہے جو سواری پر بذات خود سوار ہو سکے اور سواری کی پیٹھ پر جم کر بیٹھ سکے۔ اگر بہت چھوٹا بچہ ہو جو خود نہیں بیٹھ سکتا تو اس کا حکم متاع کا سا ہے۔ لیکن صحیح یہ ہے کہ بڑے چھوٹے کا کوئی فرق نہیں۔ بہر صورت اجیر بنی آدم کا ضامن نہ ہو گا۔ ابن ساعہ نے امام ابو یوسف سے یونہی روایت کیا ہے و کذا ذکرہ
The statement: 'Except that he is not liable for it...' - The author says previously: 'And whatever is destroyed by his action is subject to guarantee.' This is an exception. Meaning that if some property is destroyed by the action of a common hirer, he is only a guarantor for property, not for a human being. So if a boatman rows a boat improperly and someone drowns from it, or falls from the rented roof and dies, the hirer is not liable for the life indemnity. Because life indemnity is not obligatory due to a contract, but due to the crime of killing or wounding. Therefore, this indemnity falls upon the 'aqila (supporting clan) of the killer. And an indemnity that is obligatory due to a contract is not borne by the 'aqila. The statement: 'Or falls from the animal...' - Some scholars said that this applies to one who can ride by himself and sit firmly on the back of the animal. If it is a very small child who cannot sit by himself, its ruling is like that of property. But the correct view is that there is no difference between big and small. In any case, the hirer is not liable for a human being. Ibn Sa'ah narrated similarly from Imam Abu Yusuf, and likewise he mentioned it.
Source pages p. 86

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the Hanafi school regarding the liability of a common hirer (ajir mushtarak) who causes harm while performing his task. The commentary expands on the base text by clarifying the exception: the common hirer is only liable for property (mal) that is destroyed by his action, but not for harm to human life (bin Adam). The proof given is rational (dalil aqli): life indemnity (diyah) is a penalty for criminal acts like murder or wounding, not a contractual obligation. Therefore, it is borne by the 'aqila (the paternal relatives who assist in paying blood money), not by the hirer. The example of a boatman who rows improperly causing a passenger to drown illustrates this. Additionally, regarding a rider falling from an animal: the correct Hanafi position is that the hirer is not liable for the rider regardless of age, contrary to some who distinguish between an adult and a small child. This is in line with the narration from Imam Abu Yusuf as reported by Ibn Sa'ah.

Key Terms
اجیر مشترک (ajir mushtarak): A common hirer who works for multiple people or for general tasks, not exclusively for one employer.
عاقلہ ('aqila): The male paternal relatives of a killer who are collectively responsible for paying blood money (diyah) in cases of unintentional homicide.
دیت (diyah): Blood money paid as compensation for unintentional homicide or bodily harm.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is a common hirer (ajir mushtarak) not liable for the death of a passenger caused by his negligence?
A) Because the contract of hire excludes liability for life
B) Because life indemnity arises from a crime, not a contract, and falls on the 'aqila
C) Because the hirer did not intend to kill
D) Because the passenger assumed the risk

Key Takeaway
A common hirer's liability is limited to property; human life indemnity is a criminal matter for the 'aqila, not a contractual obligation.

Porter Breaking a Jar: Employer's Option for Compensation and Wage
Ruling on employer's option when porter breaks jar

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two options for the employer when a porter breaks goods mid-route and explain the legal basis (two aspects) underlying the option.

Core Idea
When a porter breaks goods mid-route, the employer may claim full value at pickup (no wage) or value at breakage (pro-rata wage).

This lesson examines a classic Hanafi ruling from the chapter on hire (ijara). A porter (ajir mushtarak) is hired to carry a jar from the Euphrates, but it breaks during the journey. The employer is given an option: either claim compensation for the jar's value at the pickup point and pay no wage, or claim compensation at the breakage site and pay a proportionate wage. The ruling is based on two legal perspectives regarding when transgression (ta'addi) occurred.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contract and parties
The porter is an ajir mushtarak (common hirer) hired to carry a jar from the Euphrates. His action causes the jar to break.
Ajir mushtarak is liable for property damage due to his negligence.
2
Understand the two options
The employer can either claim the full value of the jar at the loading place (and pay no wage) or claim its value at the breakage place (and pay a pro-rata wage for the distance covered).
Both options are equally valid.
3
Analyze the two legal aspects (وجهان)
Aspect 1: The carrying is a single act; breakage shows transgression from the start. Aspect 2: The loading was with permission; transgression only at breakage.
The option arises from the ambiguity of when ta'addi occurred.
4
Relate to liability of ajir mushtarak
The ajir mushtarak is liable for damage caused by his action (ta'addi). His failure to exercise care (slipping, rope breaking) constitutes ta'addi.
This principle is established in Hanafi law.
5
Determine the practical outcome
Under aspect 1: employer gets full value at pickup, porter gets no wage. Under aspect 2: employer gets value at breakage, porter gets wage proportional to distance covered.
The employer may incline to either aspect.

Source Text

ترجمہ کسی نے ایک شخص کو اجارہ پر لیا جو اس کے لئے فرات سے مٹکا اٹھائے پس وہ راہ میں گر کر ٹوٹ گیا تو مستاجر چاہے مٹکے کی اس قیمت کا تاوان لے لے جو اٹھانے کی جگہ میں تھی اب جمال کے لئے مزدوری نہ ہوگی یا اس قیمت کا تاوان لے لے جو ٹوٹنے کی جگہ میں ہے اور اس کے حساب سے اجرت دے دے۔ تاوان تو اسی وجہ سے ہے جو ہم کہہ چکے اور مٹکے کا گرنا اس کے پھسلنے سے ہو یا رسی ٹوٹ جانے سے ہو۔ ہر ایک اس کی حرکت سے ہے۔ رہا اختیار سو اس لئے کہ جب وہ راہ میں ٹوٹ گیا۔ حالانکہ بوجھ اٹھانا ایک ہی چیز ہے۔ تو یہ ظاہر ہو گیا کہ وہ اس طور پر ابتداء ہی سے تعدی واقع ہوئی۔ اور ایک دوسری وجہ یہ ہے کہ ابتدائی اٹھانا مستاجر کی اجازت سے ہوا تھا تو شروع سے تعدی نہ ہوئی بلکہ تعدی توڑنے کے وقت ہوئی ۔ پس دونوں میں سے جس طرف چاہیے مائل ہو جائے ۔ مگر دوسری صورت میں اجیر کو اس کا کام پانے کے بقد راجرت ملے گی اور پہلی صورت میں کچھ اجرت نہ ہوگی کیونکہ کام بالکل نہیں یا یا ۔
تشريح .. قوله واذا استاجر .... الخ ۔ زید نے ایک شخص کو اس لئے اجارہ پر لیا کہ دریائے فرات سے میر اشہر کا منکا فلاں مقام تک پہنچادے۔ اثناء راہ میں مزدور سے مشکا ٹوٹ گیا تو مزدور ضامن ہوگا۔ اب مالک کو اختیار ہے چاہے مزدور سے اس قیمت کا تاوان لے جو قیمت مٹکا اٹھانے کی جگہ تھی اور مزدوری نہ دے اور چاہے وہاں کی قیمت لے جہاں مٹکا ٹوٹا ہے اور جتنا راستہ مزدور نے طے کیا ہے اس کے حساب سے اس کو مزدوری دے۔ نفس ضمان تو اسلئے ہے کہ مزدور اجیر مشترک ہے جس کے فعل سے مال ضائع ہوا ہے اس لئے کہ مٹکے کا گر پڑنا خواہ اس کے پھسلنے سے ہو یا ری ٹوٹ جانے سے ہو۔ بہر حال اسی کی حرکت سے ہے کہ اس نے اہتمام کے ساتھ احتیاط نہیں کی اور اختیار اس لئے ہے کہ یہاں دو جہتیں ہیں ایک یہ کہ مٹکا اتناہواہ میں ٹوٹا ہے اور بوجھ اٹھا ناعمل واحد ہے اس لحاظ سے تعدی ابتداء ہی سے واقع ہوئی۔ دوسرے یہ کہ ابتداء بوجھ اٹھانا مالک کی اجازت سے عمل میں آیا ہے۔ پس ابتداء سے تعدی نہیں ہوئی بلکہ ٹوٹنے کے بعد ہوئی۔ فیمیل الى اى الوجهين شاء۔
قوله وفى الوجه الثاني ... الخ - پھر دوسری صورت میں اجیر کو اس قدرا جرت ملے گی جس قدر مستاجر نے اس کا کام پایا ہے۔ یعنی جہاں تک اس نے منکا پہنچایا ہے۔ اور پہلی صورت میں اس کو کچھ اجرت نہیں ملے گی۔ کیونکہ مستاجر نے اس کے کام میں سے کچھ حاصل نہیں اس لئے کہ جہاں سے مٹکا اٹھوایا وہیں کی قیمت لے لی۔
The porter asked: Someone hired a person to carry a jar from the Euphrates, then the jar fell on the road and broke. The employer will take compensation for the jar's value, and will the porter have wages or not?
He said: And if someone hires a person to carry for him a jar from the Euphrates, and it falls in some part of the road and breaks, then if he wishes, he can claim from him its value at the place where he loaded it, and he has no wage; and if he wishes, he can claim its value at the place where it broke, and give him his wage proportionately. As for the guarantee, it is as we said, and the falling due to stumbling or breaking of the rope, all that is from his action. As for the option, because when it broke on the road, and the carrying is one action, it becomes clear that transgression occurred from the beginning from this aspect. And there is another aspect: that the beginning of the carrying occurred with his permission, so there was no transgression from the beginning, but transgression only occurred at the time of breaking. So he may incline to whichever of the two aspects he wishes. In the second aspect, he has the wage to the extent of what was performed; in the first aspect, he has no wage because he did not perform anything at all.
Translation: Someone hired a person to carry a jar from the Euphrates, then it fell on the road and broke. So the employer can either take compensation for the jar's value at the place where it was loaded, and then there is no wage for the porter; or take compensation for its value at the place where it broke, and give him wage accordingly. The guarantee is due to what we have said, and the jar's falling due to his slipping or the rope breaking, each of these is from his action. As for the option, it is because when it broke on the road, while carrying is one action, it becomes clear that transgression occurred from the beginning in this manner. And another reason: the beginning of carrying occurred with the employer's permission, so there was no transgression from the beginning, but transgression only occurred at the time of breaking. So he may incline to whichever of the two aspects he wishes. Except in the second case, the porter will receive wage to the extent of the work performed, and in the first case, he will receive no wage because the work was not performed at all.
Explanation: The statement 'And if he hires...' Zaid hired a person to carry a jar from the Euphrates to such-and-such place. During the journey, the worker broke the jar, so the worker is a guarantor. Now the owner has the option: either take from the worker the value of the jar at the place where it was loaded and give no wage, or take the value where it broke and give wage according to the distance traveled. The guarantee itself is because the worker is a common hirer (ajir mushtarak) by whose action property was wasted. Because the jar's falling, whether by his slipping or rope breaking, is in any case due to his action in that he did not use proper care. And the option is because here there are two aspects: one, the jar broke on the road and carrying is a single action, so in this respect transgression occurred from the beginning. Second, the initial loading occurred with the owner's permission, so there was no transgression from the beginning, but only after the breaking. So he may incline to whichever aspect he wishes. The statement 'And in the second aspect...': In the second case, the porter will receive wage to the extent that the employer benefited from his work, i.e., how far he carried the jar. And in the first case, he receives no wage because the employer did not benefit from any of his work, since he took the value at the place where the jar was loaded.
Source pages p. 86

Commentary
This passage presents a detailed case from the chapter on hire concerning a common hirer (ajir mushtarak) who breaks the goods he is carrying. The ruling states that the employer has an option. He may either claim the full value of the jar at the location where it was picked up (in which case the porter receives no wage, since no benefit was received), or claim the value at the place of breakage and pay the porter a proportionate wage for the distance already carried. The reason for the option lies in two legal perspectives (وجهان): from one perspective, the carrying is a single act, and when it ends in breakage, the transgression (تعدی) is deemed to have occurred from the outset; from the other perspective, the initial loading was with permission, so transgression only occurs at the moment of breakage. The employer may choose either interpretation. The commentary clarifies that the porter is a common hirer liable for property because his negligence caused the loss. This ruling is based on rational reasoning (dalil aqli) and is consistent with the principle that a common hirer is liable for property damage.

Key Terms
تعدی (ta'addi): Transgression or exceeding proper conduct; here, the porter's action that caused the jar to break, making him liable.
اجیر مشترک (ajir mushtarak): A common hirer whose work is not exclusive to one employer; he is liable for property damage caused by his negligence.
خيار (khiyar): Option or choice given to the employer in this case to choose between two measures of compensation and wage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Demand a new jar or compensation
D) Fire the porter or keep him

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi hire law, when a common porter breaks the goods, the employer has a valid option between full compensation without wage or partial compensation with pro-rata wage.

Bloodletter Not Liable Within Usual Limits
Ruling that a cupper or veterinarian is not liable for death if operating within usual limits

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why a bloodletter or veterinarian is not liable for harm when operating within customary limits and identify the key condition that triggers liability.

Core Idea
No liability for harm within usual limits because outcome depends on patient's constitution, uncontrollable.

This lesson examines a Hanafi ruling that protects medical professionals from liability when they follow standard procedures. The key insight is that the outcome depends on the patient's physical strength, not the practitioner's skill. We will explore the reasoning and the condition that changes the ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is bloodletting (fasd) or veterinary cauterization (daghu). The ruling is that there is no liability (la daman) for resulting harm.
This applies to both human (cupper) and animal (veterinarian) cases.
2
Locate the condition for exemption
The condition is that the practitioner does not exceed the usual place (al-mawdi' al-mu'tad). If he deviates, he becomes liable.
The usual place is defined by customary practice (urf).
3
Analyze the rational proof
The proof is rational: the practitioner cannot guard against the spread of harm (sarayah) because it depends on the individual's constitution. Since this is unpredictable, he cannot be held responsible.
This is supported by an analogy to beating cloth, where the artisan is not liable for normal wear.
4
Examine the authority and scope
The ruling is from Zahir al-Riwayah (al-Jami' al-Saghir) and is the mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school.
Other schools may differ, but the Hanafi view is clear.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصاد فصد کیا بیطار نے داغا اور یہ معتاد جگہ سے نہیں بڑھا تو تاوان نہیں ہوگا
قال واذا فصد الفصاد او بزغ البزاغ ولم يتجاوز الموضع المعتاد فلاضمان عليه فيما عطب من ذالك وفي الجامع الصغير بيطار بزغ دابة بدائق فنفقت او حجام حجم عبدا بامر مولاه فمات لا ضمان عليه وفي كل واحد من العبارتين نوع بيان ووجهه انه لا يمكنه التحرز عن السراية لانه يبتنى على قوة الطبائع وضعفها في تحمل الالم فلا يمكن التقييد بالمصلح من العمل ولا كذالك دق الثوب ونحوه مما قد. مناه
The bloodletter bled, the veterinarian cauterized, and he did not exceed the usual place, so there is no liability.
He said: And if the bloodletter bleeds or the veterinarian performs phlebotomy and does not exceed the usual place, then there is no liability upon him for what is ruined thereby. And in al-Jami' al-Saghir: A veterinarian performed phlebotomy on an animal in a narrow place? and it died, or a cupper cupped a slave by order of his master and he died, there is no liability. In each of the two statements is a type of explanation. Its reasoning is that he cannot guard against the spread of harm because it depends on the strength and weakness of natures in bearing pain, so it is not possible to restrict to beneficial work. And likewise beating of cloth and similar things that...
Source pages p. 87

Commentary
This passage provides a ruling from the Hanafi school that a professional bloodletter (fasad or hajjam) or veterinarian (baytar) is not liable for any resulting harm or death if he performs the procedure within the customary limits (al-mawdi' al-mu'tad). The proof cited is rational: such outcomes depend on the individual's physical constitution, which the practitioner cannot fully control. Therefore, he cannot be required to guarantee only beneficial results, as that would be impossible. This is analogous to beating cloth (to soften it) where the artisan is not liable for normal wear. The text references al-Jami' al-Saghir as authority. The key principle is that liability only arises if the practitioner exceeds usual practice (ta'addi).

Key Terms
معتاد جگہ (al-mawdi' al-mu'tad): The customary or usual location for performing a medical procedure, beyond which would be transgression.
سرایت (sarayah): The spread of harm from a wound or procedure to the rest of the body, which is unpredictable and beyond the practitioner's control.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) Because the bloodletter is not a professional

Key Takeaway
A bloodletter or veterinarian is not liable for harm if they operate within usual limits because the outcome depends on factors beyond their control.

Owner's Option When a Hired Porter Breaks Goods: The Ajir Mushtarak Liability
Ruling on owner's option when hired porter breaks a jar

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the owner's two remedies when a hired porter (ajir mushtarak) breaks goods and explain the reasoning (ta'lil) behind the timing of transgression.

Core Idea
Owner may choose full compensation with no wage, or partial compensation with proportional wage.

In this lesson, we examine a specific ruling from the Book of Ijarah on the liability of a hired porter (ajir mushtarak) who accidentally breaks a jar during transport. The Hanafi school grants the owner a legal option between two remedies based on the timing of the porter's transgression (tadi). Understanding this ruling clarifies how initial permission and subsequent negligence interact in hire contracts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties and the contract
Recognize that the owner (musta'jir) hires a porter (ajir mushtarak) to carry a jar. The porter is a shared worker, not assigned exclusively to this task.
Ajir mushtarak is liable for negligence; ajir khas is not.
2
State the main ruling
The owner has an option: either claim the value of the jar at the lifting point and pay no wage, or claim the value at the breakage point and pay a proportional wage for the distance covered.
3
Understand the reasoning (ta'lil)
Two perspectives: (1) lifting and carrying is a single act, so transgression is from the start; (2) lifting was permitted, so transgression only at breakage.
This reasoning determines which option applies.
4
Apply to the scenario
The owner chooses based on his interest: full compensation (no wage) vs. partial compensation (with wage).
The porter's negligence (slipping, rope break) triggers liability.
5
Distinguish the ajir mushtarak
Ajir mushtarak is liable because his action caused loss; the type of hire affects liability rules.
Contrast with ajir khas who is not liable without explicit transgression.

Source Text

كتاب الاجارات الحمل حصل باذنه فلم يكن من الابتداء تعديا وانما صار تعديا عند الكسر فيميل الى اى الوجهين شاء وفي الوجه الثاني له الاجر بقدر ما استوفى وفى الوجه الاول لا اجر له لانه ما استوفی اصلا
ترجمہ: کسی نے ایک شخص کو اجارہ پر لیا جو اس کے لئے فرات سے مٹکا اٹھائے پس وہ راہ میں گر کر ٹوٹ گیا تو مستاجر چاہے مٹکے کی اس قیمت کا تاوان لے لے جو اٹھانے کی جگہ میں تھی اب جمال کے لئے مزدوری نہ ہوگی یا اس قیمت کا تاوان لے لے جو ٹوٹنے کی جگہ میں ہے اور اس کے حساب سے اجرت دے دے۔ تاوان تو اسی وجہ سے ہے جو ہم کہہ چکے اور مٹکے کا گرنا اس کے پھسلنے سے ہو یا رسی ٹوٹ جانے سے ہو۔ ہر ایک اس کی حرکت سے ہے۔ رہا اختیار سو اس لئے کہ جب وہ راہ میں ٹوٹ گیا۔ حالانکہ بوجھ اٹھانا ایک ہی چیز ہے۔ تو یہ ظاہر ہو گیا کہ وہ اس طور پر ابتداء ہی سے تعدی واقع ہوئی۔ اور ایک دوسری وجہ یہ ہے کہ ابتدائی اٹھانا مستاجر کی اجازت سے ہوا تھا تو شروع سے تعدی نہ ہوئی بلکہ تعدی توڑنے کے وقت ہوئی ۔ پس دونوں میں سے جس طرف چاہیے مائل ہو جائے ۔ مگر دوسری صورت میں اجیر کو اس کا کام پانے کے بقد راجرت ملے گی اور پہلی صورت میں کچھ اجرت نہ ہوگی کیونکہ کام بالکل نہیں یا یا ۔
تشريح .. قوله واذا استاجر .... الخ ۔ زید نے ایک شخص کو اس لئے اجارہ پر لیا کہ دریائے فرات سے میر اشہر کا منکا فلاں مقام تک پہنچادے۔ اثناء راہ میں مزدور سے مشکا ٹوٹ گیا تو مزدور ضامن ہوگا۔ اب مالک کو اختیار ہے چاہے مزدور سے اس قیمت کا تاوان لے جو قیمت مٹکا اٹھانے کی جگہ تھی اور مزدوری نہ دے اور چاہے وہاں کی قیمت لے جہاں مٹکا ٹوٹا ہے اور جتنا راستہ مزدور نے طے کیا ہے اس کے حساب سے اس کو مزدوری دے۔ نفس ضمان تو اسلئے ہے کہ مزدور اجیر مشترک ہے جس کے فعل سے مال ضائع ہوا ہے اس لئے کہ مٹکے کا گر پڑنا خواہ اس کے پھسلنے سے ہو یا ری ٹوٹ جانے سے ہو۔ بہر حال اسی کی حرکت سے ہے کہ اس نے اہتمام کے ساتھ احتیاط نہیں کی اور اختیار اس لئے ہے کہ یہاں دو جہتیں ہیں ایک یہ کہ مٹکا اتناہواہ میں ٹوٹا ہے اور بوجھ اٹھا ناعمل واحد ہے اس لحاظ سے تعدی ابتداء ہی سے واقع ہوئی۔ دوسرے یہ کہ ابتداء بوجھ اٹھانا مالک کی اجازت سے عمل میں آیا ہے۔ پس ابتداء سے تعدی نہیں ہوئی بلکہ ٹوٹنے کے بعد ہوئی۔ فیمیل الى اى الوجهين شاء۔
قوله وفى الوجه الثاني ... الخ - پھر دوسری صورت میں اجیر کو اس قدرا جرت ملے گی جس قدر مستاجر نے اس کا کام پایا ہے۔ یعنی جہاں تک اس نے منکا پہنچایا ہے۔ اور پہلی صورت میں اس کو کچھ اجرت نہیں ملے گی۔ کیونکہ مستاجر نے اس کے کام میں سے کچھ حاصل نہیں اس لئے کہ جہاں سے مٹکا اٹھوایا وہیں کی قیمت لے لی۔
The Book of Hiring: The carrying occurred with his permission; thus initially there was no transgression, rather transgression occurred at the time of breaking. So he may incline to whichever of the two aspects he wishes. In the second aspect, he has the wage to the extent of what he performed; in the first aspect, he has no wage because he performed nothing. (Urdu commentary expands on the scenario and reasoning)
Source pages p. 87

Commentary
This passage from the Book of Ijarah (Hiring) presents a ruling on the liability of a hired porter (ajir mushtarak) who breaks a jar during transport. The owner (musta'jir) has an option between two remedies: if the porter's transgression (tadi) is deemed to have occurred from the outset, the owner may claim the value of the jar at the point of lifting (where it was intact) and give no wage; if transgression is deemed only at the moment of breakage, the owner may claim the lower value at the breakage point and pay the porter a proportional wage for the distance covered. The reasoning (ta'lil) explores two perspectives: (1) since lifting and carrying is a single act, the transgression is present from the start; (2) since the initial lifting was with the owner's permission, transgression only arises with the breakage. The porter (ajir mushtarak) is liable because his action (slipping or rope breakage) indicates negligence (adam ihtiyat). The author (Al-Hidayah) leaves the choice to the owner. The commentary (Sharh) clarifies the scenario and states that in the second view, the porter receives wage proportionally, while in the first view he gets none because the owner received no benefit (the jar's value was taken at the original place).

Key Terms
اجیر مشترک (ajir mushtarak): A hired worker not assigned to a specific task, liable for loss due to his negligence.
تعدی (tadi): Transgression beyond the bounds of permission, here specifically causing breakage through negligence.
ضمان (daman): Liability to compensate for damage or loss, here the value of the jar.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the case of a hired porter who breaks a jar during transport, what option does the owner have?
A) He can only claim the value of the jar at the point of lifting.
B) He can claim the value at the breakage point or at the lifting point, with or without paying wage accordingly.
C) He must pay the full wage regardless.
D) He can claim double the value.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school grants the owner a choice between full compensation with no wage or partial compensation with proportional wage, based on when the porter's transgression is deemed to have occurred.
